# Toras Menachem Vol 01

Toras Menachem

## – A – The Year 5310

## With the help of Hashem. Wednesday, 14 Shevat 5710*

#### 3

(During the first week following the histalkus of the Rebbe Rayatz, on the fourth day, after Shacharis, the Rebbe said:)

The halacha is: "Three days for weeping, seven days for eulogizing." [1](#_ftn1)

I received a letter from someone in which he writes that although Chassidim do not deliver formal eulogies, they do share stories about the person, and that is the eulogy. He also writes me a story:

The Rebbe wrote to him in a letter: "I do not scatter titles. When I write 'my soul-friend' or 'my dear friend,' it is because the reality is indeed so." [2](#_ftn2)

(And the Rebbe added:) Even if, from the perspective of the *recipient*, it may be that for the time being this is not yet the case, eventually it will be so.

And in accordance with this—since the "seven days for eulogizing" weigh upon me ("mir kvetsht")—I will share stories [3](#_ftn3) about the Rebbe. [4](#_ftn4)

(And this is what he would do on the remaining days of the shivah as well, after davening.)

## – A List of Remembered Stories. The Order of the Stories is Not Remembered –

#### 4

**1.** In the year 5657, the Rebbe (Rashab) was very ill and traveled to Moscow for medical treatment.

The professors told him then that he had only a few months to live. When the Rebbe heard this, he decided to travel to Eretz Yisrael, and he told the Rabbanit, Sterna Sarah, about it.

The Rabbanit asked him: "And what will you do with your Chassidim and with Chassidus?" The Rebbe replied: "I am leaving him [referring to the Rebbe] behind." [5](#_ftn5)

And the Rebbe was only seventeen years old at the time!

**2.** When the Rebbe was a child, in the year 5644, his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), lived in a two-room apartment. One room served as a bedroom, and in the second room, he would sit and learn together with the great Gaon and Chassid, R' Yaakov Mordechai Bezpalov. [6](#_ftn6) The Rebbe’s cradle also stood there. The Rebbe was beautiful, and his face radiated light. Once, late at night while they were learning, R' Yaakov Mordechai saw the Rebbe sleeping and began speaking to the Rebbe (Rashab) about how the appearance and radiance of his face were proof of the purity of his thoughts, and so on. A strong desire then awakened in the Rebbe (Rashab) to kiss the Rebbe. [7](#_ftn7) A thought passed through his mind that in the Beis Hamikdash, in addition to sacrifices, they also brought silver, gold, etc., for the *bedek habayis* (maintenance of the Temple), and he decided to replace the kiss with a *maamar Chassidus*. He then wrote the *maamar Chassidus* beginning with the words "Mah rabu maasecha." [8](#_ftn8) In the year 5652, he gave the manuscript to the Rebbe as a gift, saying: "This is a Chassidishe kiss, and in time, I will tell you [the story behind it]." In the year 5656, he told him the whole story. [9](#_ftn9)

**3.** When the Rebbe was about six years old, his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), called him and told him to recite the *bracha* on his *tzitzis*. The Rebbe replied that he had already recited the *bracha* on *tzitzis* that day. The Rebbe (Rashab) said: "Even so!" But the Rebbe refused.

The Rebbe (Rashab) gave him a light slap (this was the only time he ever gave him a

#### 5

slap) and said: "When I command, you must obey." The Rebbe burst into tears and said: "If one must recite a *bracha* before the Ribono shel Olam—I have already recited it; but if I must recite it because you command it..."

The Rebbe (Rashab) answered him: "One must recite it because the Ribono shel Olam commanded it, but every father watches over his children, and they must obey him." [10](#_ftn10)

**4.** In the early years, when the Rebbe (Rashab) would travel to a certain place, he would not give the Rebbe the key to the cabinets containing his manuscripts, but in later years, he would make a practice of leaving the key in his possession.

Once, the Rebbe entered the manuscript room and saw that the pages of the Rebbe (Maharash) were lying there.

The Rebbe, who had trained himself even earlier to write in the handwriting of the Rebbe (Maharash), took a goose quill (the Rebbe (Maharash) would very frequently use a goose quill to write) and wrote an explanation of a certain concept in Chassidus (for the *maamar* "Vayelech ish mibeis Levi") on a sheet of paper belonging to the Rebbe (Maharash), in the handwriting of the Rebbe (Maharash).

The Rebbe then continued his study of the manuscripts, and in the midst of his deep concentration, he left, leaving the manuscript among the other papers. When the Rebbe (Rashab) returned from abroad, he entered the manuscript room and found this writing, and he said to the Rebbe: "I have joy today; I found a *maamar* of my father that I did not know about."

The Rebbe did not answer him anything. A few weeks later, the Rebbe (Rashab) spoke about it again. The Rebbe then contemplated: What had he done, and how could he rectify it? He decided to enter for a *yechidus* regarding this.

When he entered for *yechidus*, he burst into tears. The matter weighed heavily on his heart, and he could not speak at all.

When the Rebbe (Rashab) asked him the reason for his tears, he answered that he had done a certain thing and did not know how he could find rectification for it. And he told him the whole story.

The Rebbe (Rashab) said to him: "It is not so terrible!"

**5.** There were times when the Rebbe (Rashab) instructed the Rebbe to enter his room and observe his conduct.

#### 6

**6.** The Rebbe (Rashab) once needed to write long letters to many Rabbis, all in his own handwriting, a task that consumed much of his time.

He then told the Rebbe to train himself in his handwriting and write the letters, and he—the Rebbe (Rashab)—would sign them.

The Rebbe said that he agreed to this, on the condition that he would add a *shiur* in learning Chassidus with him.

The Rebbe (Rashab) agreed to the condition, and the Rebbe studied his father’s handwriting for a short time and later wrote the letters for him as mentioned above.

**7.** After a telephone was installed between the rooms of the Rebbe (Rashab) and the Rebbe, it would often happen that the Rebbe (Rashab) would call the Rebbe and say to him: "You may enter; I wish to smoke." The Rebbe would enter, strike a match, light the cigarette, and the Rebbe (Rashab) would smoke.

The Rebbe (Rashab) would speak with him about the subject he was currently occupied with, or he would ask: "What do you have to tell me?" And then the Rebbe would present his own matters. [11](#_ftn11)

After some time, an idea occurred to the Rebbe, and on Erev Shabbos or Erev Yom Tov, he would place a match under the telephone receiver so that it would not close properly, and he would be able to hear the Rebbe (Rashab) davening in his room. [12](#_ftn12)

**8.** Once, the Rebbe (Rashab) visited Prague together with the Rebbe, and they visited the shul of the Maharal. The Rebbe wanted to go up to the attic where the "Golem" was kept; he gave a tip to the *shamash*, took a ladder, and went up.

– When the Rebbe told the story, I asked him what he saw there, and the Rebbe did not answer me. –

When the Rebbe (Rashab) found out about this, he rebuked the Rebbe severely. Some time later, he said to him: "I had months of *avodah* [to fix it] (apparently to rectify that no harm should come from it. The narrator)."

**9.** In the year of mourning, [13](#_ftn13) *l"a*, when the Rebbe would finish: "Rabbi Chananya ben Akashya, etc.," before *Kaddish d'Rabbanan*, he would make a practice of leaning on his hand and saying something in a whisper.

Later, the Rebbe related that he would say a few lines from the *Tanya* at that time. [14](#_ftn14)

#### 7

**10.** The Rebbe said that in *davening* on days when we do not say *Tachanun*, we do not strike the chest when saying "Selach lanu." [15](#_ftn15)

**11.** The Rebbe (Rashab) was once abroad and met with many "gute Yidden." [16](#_ftn16) Upon arriving home, he brought a gift for the Rebbe: a cane with a silver handle, [17](#_ftn17) on which he had spent the remainder of the money he had. The Rabbanit asked him if he really needed to spend his remaining funds on that, and the Rebbe (Rashab) replied to her that now, he had come to see who he (the Rebbe) was. [18](#_ftn18)

**12.** To put on four pairs of *tefillin* [19](#_ftn19) requires a body that is extremely clean. Because, regarding matters that the Torah has obligated, such as the *tefillin* of Rashi and Rabbeinu Tam, [20](#_ftn20) since "the Torah was not given to ministering angels," [21](#_ftn21) the Torah takes the matter upon itself; whereas for a matter that only a few people do, and which the Torah did not obligate everyone to do, the personal responsibility is greater. And in addition to this, due to the nature of the *tefillin* of Shimusha Rabba and Ra'avad, they require an extremely clean body. [22](#_ftn22)

#### 8

I found it printed [23](#_ftn23) that the great Chassid, etc., R' Hillel of Paritch, [24](#_ftn24) put on four pairs of *tefillin*, and that witnesses testified before the author that the sons of the Tzemach Tzedek put on four pairs of *tefillin*. There were also Chassidim in our generation who made a practice of putting on four pairs of *tefillin*, such as R' Yitzchak Matmid, [25](#_ftn25) R' Tzvi Hirsch Gurary, [26](#_ftn26) and others. As for me—I was afraid, until the Rebbe told me to put on four pairs of *tefillin*, [27](#_ftn27) and I began to put them on, for the matter was on the "shoulders" of the Rebbe.

The Rebbe told me then that he himself would order the *tefillin*, so that the matter would be done in secret. [27](#_ftn27)

At the time *Hayom Yom* was printed, the Rebbe agreed to reveal the order of putting on the four pairs of *tefillin*, and the matter was printed in *Hayom Yom*. [28](#_ftn28)

In the verse [29](#_ftn29) "Shomer tam u're'eh yashar ki acharis le'ish shalom" (Observe the innocent and watch the upright, for the end of that man is peace), the four pairs of *tefillin* are alluded to. [30](#_ftn30) The *tefillin* of Rabbeinu Tam are alluded to in the word "tam." The *tefillin* of Rashi—in the word "yashar." The *tefillin* of Shimusha Rabba—in the word "shalom," Rav Sar Shalom, the author of Shimusha Rabba. [31](#_ftn31)

The *tefillin* of Shimusha Rabba and especially of Ra'avad are on a higher level than those of Rashi and Rabbeinu Tam. Therefore, there is no opinion that holds one should recite a *bracha* over them. [32](#_ftn32)

The *tefillin* of Rashi are the level of *mochin d'Imma*; the *tefillin* of Rabbeinu Tam are *mochin d'Abba*; and the *tefillin* of Shimusha Rabba and Ra'avad are *Keter*. [33](#_ftn33) And therefore, they are too lofty to be "drawn down" through a *bracha*.

#### 9

**13.** When some of *Anash* were stranded in Germany, they turned with a question as to whether it is permissible to make *tzitzis* by machine. I asked the Rebbe—since the Tzanzers are stringent. [34](#_ftn34) The Rebbe told me that when the refugees arrived in Russia in the year 5675, they did not have *talleisim* or *tzitzis*. They asked the Rebbe (Rashab), and the Rebbe (Rashab) sent a messenger to the Ginzburg factory, and they made *tzitzis* there by machine, and afterwards he said that one may recite a *bracha* over them. [35](#_ftn35)

**14.** I never heard the Rebbe be particular about the title "the Holy" in relation to the Baal Ohr HaChaim or the Shelah.

When the Rebbe related [36](#_ftn36) that the Alter Rebbe was a "Shelah Yid," that he davened with a Shelah Siddur and with the *kavanos* of the Shelah, he did not add the word "the Holy."

**15.** The Rebbe related that when the Ruzhiner was a child and was learning Chumash with his teacher, he would anticipate and ask the teacher all the questions that Rashi points out.

When he learned the verse [37](#_ftn37) "Vayachlom v'hinei sulam mutzav artza, etc.," the teacher said to him: "Nu, why don't you ask?" And he told him Rashi’s question: "It should have been written 'descending and ascending'?" The Ruzhiner answered: "One does not ask questions on a dream."

**16.** At the time of his *bris milah*, the Rebbe cried, as is the way of infants. His grandfather, the Rebbe (Maharash), said to him: "Why are you crying? When you grow up, you will be... and you will say Chassidus in a clear language." This is recorded in the Rebbe’s *Reshimas HaMaasar* [38](#_ftn38) with a blank space after the word "you will be." From Chassidim, I heard that he said "you will be *Rebbe*." According to this, it is understood why there is a blank space in the Rebbe’s notes.

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

## 10

. . . In one of his letters[1](#_ftn39) regarding the passing of his father, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, writes that the tzaddikim who protect the land—even after their passing—"not only do they not separate from their flock, but furthermore, they prostrate themselves before the footstool of the exalted throne, to stand before the glory of the Almighty, high and exalted, to protect the people of Yeshurun."

All of this is true as well regarding the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory.

However, we, for our part, must maintain and strengthen our hiskashrus and connection with him with even greater intensity and vigor. By studying the maamarim, sichos, and letters, and by delving deeply into the instructions contained within them—as well as the specific instructions we have received—we will then walk "in the straight path that he taught us, and we will walk in his ways forever and ever"[2](#_ftn40) . . .

**Menachem Schneerson**

*18 Shevat, 5710*

## With the help of Heaven. From the Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Yisro, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar, 5730

#### 11

(Unedited)

**A.** The Rebbe once told a story (while he was in Riga) about the Tzaddik Rabbi Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev, who said before his passing:

There were Tzaddikim who, before their passing, promised they would not enter Gan Eden until they brought about the coming of Moshiach. In the end, they were tricked and bribed with "sugar cake"... But I—concluded the Tzaddik of Berditchev—will not let myself be tricked.

But in the end—the Rebbe concluded—they tricked him, too. They said "Kedushah" in Gan Eden, and the Tzaddik of Berditchev immediately jumped into Gan Eden...

(And the Rebbe concluded:)

Since the Rebbe knew and told this story, he certainly ensured and promised that for him, it would not be so.

The Rebbe will *certainly* bring Moshiach[1](#_ftn41).

**B.** The difference between other Tzaddikim and the Rebbe can be explained according to what is explained in Chassidus[2](#_ftn42) regarding the difference between the *mesiras nefesh* of Rabbi Akiva and the *mesiras nefesh* of Avraham Avinu:

Rabbi Akiva sought and desired *mesiras nefesh*, as he said, "All my days I was distressed... when will it come to my hand that I may fulfill it?"[3](#_ftn43) Avraham Avinu, by contrast, did not seek *mesiras nefesh*; rather, his *avodah* was to *publicize Elokus in the world*, and he engaged in this with total self-surrender and devotion, to the extent that when the situation demanded it, he was prepared to sacrifice his life.

In other words: Rabbi Akiva sought *his own benefit*—but for him, the greatest good was the transcendence of *mesiras nefesh*. Consequently, this is not *mesiras nefesh* in its truest sense. Avraham Avinu, however, sought nothing for himself (not even *mesiras nefesh*); he was *surrendered and devoted with his entire essence* to publicizing Elokus in the world, and this is *mesiras nefesh* in its truest sense.

#### 12

The same applies to our current situation:

For all the Tzaddikim who promised before their passing not to enter Gan Eden until they brought about the coming of Moshiach, it was a matter of *mesiras nefesh*: they were prepared to *forgo* even Gan Eden for the sake of the benefit of Yisrael. But the Rebbe—since he has no existence for himself at all, but is surrendered and devoted with his entire existence to the entirety of Yisrael—his action to bring Moshiach for the benefit of the entirety of Yisrael is not "mesiras nefesh," but rather his *entire existence*.

And therefore: the other Tzaddikim could be "bought off" with matters of "revelations," but the Rebbe cannot be bought with revelations. Therefore, the Rebbe will certainly bring Moshiach.

**C.** And it should be added:

Even after his passing, having ascended to a much greater height, it remains relevant to him to bring about the coming of Moshiach *in the world below* just as it was before his passing. On the contrary, after his passing, the "below" is even more relevant to him, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh[4](#_ftn44) in his explanation of the Zohar’s[5](#_ftn45) statement, "A Tzaddik who has departed is found in all worlds more than during his lifetime"—that "even in this world of action... he is found more."

It should be noted that the Alter Rebbe wrote this concept (that even in this world he is found more) in connection with the passing of the Tzaddik Rabbi Menachem Mendel of Horodok, who is not counted among the Nesi'im of Chabad[6](#_ftn46). From this, it is understood *a fortiori* regarding the Rebbe, that even after his passing he is found in this world more than during his lifetime, and what happens here below is of the utmost relevance to him.

Since this is the case, they will not be able to persuade him otherwise, and he will certainly bring Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

*

**D.** In the *maamar* of Yud Shevat, there are several wondrous matters[7](#_ftn47) that, at first glance, appear to have no connection to the content of the *maamar*, and now we understand them well!...

[The Rebbe concluded with a blessing that we should merit the fulfillment of the prophecy[8](#_ftn48), "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," with the Rebbe among them and at their head.]

## 13

It is well known what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh (Letter 27) to comfort with double measure those who are "crushed, sighing and groaning"[1](#_ftn49), that the Tzaddik "has left life... for all the living, for he is the soul of all the living, bound to his soul... in each and every one according to the level of their true connection and their love, the pure, true love."

The Alter Rebbe explains there the concept of *hishtatchus* (visiting the gravesite), noting that "even those who did not know him or recognize him during his lifetime, but who studied the holy books he left as a blessing after him, and who derive benefit from the light and radiance of his Torah and are strengthened through this in their *avodas Hashem*... they are certainly also called his students... for they believe in that Tzaddik and receive from him the light of his Torah... the branches are drawn to their root."

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained in a letter that "the intensity of the yearning for *hiskashrus* can only be satisfied when one studies the *maamarim* of Chassidus that the Rebbe says and writes, for merely seeing his face is not enough."

And in a second letter, he elaborates for "one who asks, 'In what does my *hiskashrus* to you consist, since I do not know you face-to-face?' The true *hiskashrus* is through the study of Torah: when he studies my *maamarim* of Chassidus, reads the *sichos*, connects with my friends, *anash*, and the *talmidei hatmimim*—may they live—in their studies and their *farbrengens*, and fulfills my request by reciting Tehillim[2](#_ftn50) and keeping to the times for study, this is the *hiskashrus*."

And when we study his Torah and his *sichos* and walk in this straight path that he has taught us, then "as water reflects the face... and spirit brings spirit and draws forth spirit, and his spirit stands within us literally... so that even in this world of action, *hayom la'asosam*, he is found even more." And just as he stood and served here, so too he stands and serves above...

**Menachem Schneerson**

*Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5710*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## From a Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Terumah, Parshas Zachor, 8 Adar, 5750

#### 14

**A.** Regarding the joy of a chassan and kallah, the Rebbe brings in the maamar of Yud Shevat[1](#_ftn51) the words of the Gemara[2](#_ftn52): "They said about Rabbi Yehuda bar Rabbi Ilai that he would take a branch of myrtle and dance before the kallah... Rav Shmuel bar Rav Yitzchak would juggle three [branches, throwing one and catching one[3](#_ftn53)]... Rabbi Zeira said: 'His foolishness has helped me' [i.e., his joyous antics]."

The maamar explains that this "foolishness" is above the intellect—a very high and wondrous level. For when a man and woman merit it, the Shechinah dwells between them[4](#_ftn54); the man is *Eish* (fire) with a *Yud*, and the woman is *Eish* with a *Hei*. When they merit it, they become *Y-H* (and it manifests in the building of an everlasting edifice). Thus, this is a high level, and therefore he merited such lofty revelations.

This matter applies to every chassan and kallah—that when they build their home on the foundations of Torah, the Rebbe promises that it will be an "everlasting edifice," an eternal home, in the words of Chazal[5](#_ftn55), "Netzach, Selah, Va'ed," for "wherever it is said 'Netzach, Selah, Va'ed,' it has no end forever."

**B.** The Rebbe demands and insists that the building of a home on the foundations of Torah must be in such a way that all matters of the home—not only the matters of holiness within it, but also the mundane matters—are permeated with Torah.

In this connection, there is a story the Rebbe told[6](#_ftn56) regarding the difference between a misnaged and a Chassid:

There were two brothers. One was a Chassid who was poor, naturally, and had daughters. The other was a misnaged, who was wealthy and had sons. When the Chassid’s daughters reached marriageable age, he decided to turn to his brother, the misnaged, to ask for help in marrying them off. When the brothers met, the misnaged took the Chassid and showed him his spacious and large house,

#### 15

which had many rooms, saying, "This room is my private room, in this room I sleep, in this room I eat, and in this room I receive guests," and so on. Afterward, the misnaged asked his brother, the Chassid: "Well, what is your opinion of my house?" The Chassid answered him: "I am amazed that you are able to live in such 'scattering of the soul'—a special room for everything. In this room you sleep, in this room you eat, and in this room you study Torah and perform mitzvos. I," says the Chassid, "have only two rooms, and I am unable to divide them into special places for sleeping, eating, and the performance of Torah and mitzvos..."

A Jewish home is not divided into different parts—one part special for matters of holiness and the rest for mundane matters; the Torah must permeate, and does permeate, the entire home.

**C.** A parallel to this is in one's personal avodah each day—that the avodah of tefillah must permeate and affect the entire day.

Sometimes a Yid might be inspired in his heart that at the time of tefillah—at the very least—he will have only thoughts of holiness, but after tefillah, during his business, he does not care so much. But the truth is—as the teachings of Chassidus demand—that the avodah of tefillah must permeate and affect the entire day[7](#_ftn57).

—It is told of the son of the Tzemach Tzedek, after whom the Rebbe was named, that he would go to the shul to hear *Barechu*, *Kedushah*, and the *Chazarat HaShatz*, and afterward he would daven in private. When asked about davening with a minyan, he replied that he strives to gather and collect his *ten powers of the soul* and daven "in a minyan"[8](#_ftn58).

**D.** The *koach* for this—that Torah permeates the entire home, and tefillah permeates all the matters of the day—is continued by the *Rebbe* through the teachings of Chassidus, which is compared to water (in addition to the general concept of Torah, which is compared to food[9](#_ftn59)), through which the food is moved in a way that it reaches and permeates all parts of the body[10](#_ftn60).

—They tell of the Chassid R' Elchanan Dov Morozov[11](#_ftn61), whom someone once asked regarding the Rebbe N"E and Moshe Rabbeinu, "Whom does he hold of more?" He answered: *The Rebbe*, because, were it not for the Rebbe, how would his faith in Moshe Rabbeinu look...

And in this matter, there is a difference between the Rebbe and the previous Rebbes—that the previous Rebbes

#### 16

had elder Chassidim ("altere Chassidim") who would influence the younger ones, and the younger ones would go out into the world to spread these things among simple Yidden, but the Rebbe had to do everything by himself!

**E.** The *koach* that the Rebbe continues through the teachings of Chassidus is continued and given to us even now, without any change on his part, and also on our part there should not be a change where we would think that the Rebbe is not with us, chas v'shalom.

—Those who knew the Rebbe during his thirty years of Nasi know that the Rebbe would not leave his Chassidim to remain alone on Shabbos Parshas Zachor, for example, when they need to fight against Amalek...

The only change that has occurred for us is that in the past, someone might have thought that upon entering the Rebbe, he could tell the things he wanted to tell *and hide* the things he wanted to hide from the Rebbe. But now, it is clear to all that the Rebbe knows even the things that are hidden within us, for in the past the Rebbe was clothed in a physical body, whereas now, being above the limitations of the physical body, he is entirely spiritual[12](#_ftn62).

And on the other hand, since "a Tzaddik who has departed is found in all worlds *more than in his lifetime*"[13](#_ftn63), "that even *in this world of action* he is found more"[12](#_ftn62)—certainly the Rebbe leads the entire world, and Anash in particular, and arouses great mercies, etc., just as it was until now, and even more so, with greater strength and greater intensity.

And just as until now it was settled ("opgeleygt") in each of us that the Rebbe will lead us toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu—it must be settled that way even now.

And the event that occurred, etc.—is only to our *physical eyes*, and is only a *test* (one of the tests of the birth pangs of Moshiach that must occur before the coming of the Redeemer), whose entire purpose is *to hide and conceal the truth*,

—although it still requires explanation as to why, according to *Torah*, one must now say Kaddish, etc.—

And the intent of the test is for the sake of overcoming and standing in the test, whereby we push away and nullify the concealment and hiding *and the truth is revealed* (as explained in the discourses of Chassidus[14](#_ftn64)).

Therefore, through strengthening the hiskashrus by studying his Torah and fulfilling his instructions (both

#### 17

the instructions for the many, and especially the instructions given face-to-face in yechidus) in actual practice, we will merit immediately (since we are in the footsteps of Moshiach) to "see ourselves with the Rebbe" with *physical eyes*, and the Rebbe will lead us to the Geulah.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of 10 Adar (Conclusion of the "Shloshim"), 5710

#### 18

– At a gathering of Anash, may they live –

Unedited

The Rebbe’s physician once said that he has no standing as a doctor when it comes to the Rebbe. As a doctor, he cannot comprehend the Rebbe’s physical life.

The truth is that the Rebbe’s life is a spiritual life—"The life of the Tzaddik is not a fleshly life, but a spiritual life"[1](#_ftn65).

From this, it is understood that for the Rebbe, there is no difference between the state and situation that existed previously and the state and situation now.

Even now, the Rebbe is with us in physicality.

The Rebbe said[2](#_ftn66]: The hiskashrus to me is through studying my maamarim of Chassidus, and fulfilling my request by reciting the daily Tehillim, and the like.

The Rebbe’s words—regarding the hiskashrus to him—remain in full force even now.

**********

## With the help of Heaven. From the Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Tetzaveh, Shushan Purim, 5710

#### 18a

(Unedited)

Those who say that "histalkus" means that the Rebbe has departed from us—they are "wild men" (*vilde mentchen*) who do not know what they are talking about...

In his maamar entitled *Basi L’Gani*—the maamar given in preparation for the day of the histalkus[1](#_ftn67)—the Rebbe explains the statement of the Zohar[2](#_ftn68): "When the sitra achra is subdued, the glory of the Holy One, blessed be He, *istalek* (is exalted/ascends) in all the worlds." Would anyone interpret the term *istalek* here as a literal departure, Heaven forbid?!

The Rebbe explains that "istalek yikara d’Kudsha Brich Hu" indicates the drawing down of light in the most sublime level, the aspect of *sovev kol almin*, and this drawing down is referred to by the term *histalkus* because of its quality of transcendence.[3](#_ftn69) From this, it is understood that the same applies to the "histalkus" of the Rebbe.

—And this should be connected to the concept of "Shushan" Purim, "from the expression *Shushan Emek Ayuma* [the rose of the valley]," which is the aspect of "like a rose[5](#_ftn71) among the thorns."[6](#_ftn72) It is explained in the *Kuntres* for Purim[7](#_ftn73) that when the thorns prick the rose, it awakens in the rose an added fragrance until it consumes the thorns.[8](#_ftn74) That is to say, it is precisely through the concealment and hiddenness of the descent below (analogous to the thorns pricking the rose) that a most sublime revelation is brought about (analogous to the added fragrance produced in the rose)—a revelation of the aspect of *sovev kol almin*.—

From this, it is understood that there need not be any lack, Heaven forbid, in one’s *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe. The Rebbe Rayatz said that the advice for *hiskashrus* is to close one’s eyes and bring to mind one of the *yechidus* sessions with the Rebbe. And now, when everyone is privileged to enter the Rebbe’s room, this is even easier.

Nevertheless, we want and need the Rebbe literally, below ten *tefachim*...

#### 18b

The Rebbe’s father, the Rebbe Maharash, asked his father, the Tzemach Tzedek, regarding that year about which it was said that it was the "end" (*ketz*): How is it possible that Moshiach did not come? He replied: But the *Likutei Torah* has been printed![9](#_ftn75) The Rebbe Maharash responded to his father, the Tzemach Tzedek: But we want and need Moshiach literally, below ten *tefachim*![10](#_ftn76)...

## 19

...There are two matters associated with the second of Nissan: a) The yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe [Rashab], of blessed memory, and consequently[1](#_ftn77) b) the day upon which his only son, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Nasi and leader of our generation—assumed his position.

Each and every year, these matters are reawakened at their appropriate times[2](#_ftn78). It is easily understood by the discerning mind that in the thirty years that have passed until now—thirty second-of-Nissan days (5680–5709)—there has been an ascent upon an ascent, thirty levels of elevation[3](#_ftn79). This is explained according to the words of our Sages, that even after passing, the tzaddikim go from strength to strength, and a tzaddik who has departed is found in all worlds—and in this world as well—even more than during his lifetime. Therefore, his influences upon all those who are connected to him are also increasingly elevated. In order for these to be received internally, the "vessels" of those connected to him must also be more refined.

Especially at this time of year, on the upcoming second of Nissan, it is incumbent upon each and every person connected to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to strengthen their hiskashrus to him—following the paths he taught us in his letters, sichos, and sayings—with greater intensity and greater strength.

One must contemplate and firmly establish in one’s mind and heart that our shepherd, our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has not, Heaven forbid, abandoned his flock. Even now, he stands and serves in the holy, protecting them and bestowing upon them everything they require, both materially and spiritually...

**Menachem Schneerson**

*25th of Adar, 5710*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. From the Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel-Pekudei, Mevarchim HaChodesh and Erev Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5750*

#### 20

In the final *Hemshech* [1](#_ftn80) that the Rebbe wrote, he clarified everything ("he provided for everything") and therein he also hinted at everything [2](#_ftn81).

In its conclusion (in the *maamar* for the 2nd of Nissan [3](#_ftn82)), the Rebbe explains the concept of *Netzach* [4](#_ftn83), stating that the *middah* of *Netzach* is rooted in the very essence of the soul, above all [other] powers. This is why we see that in order to achieve victory in war, one spends the treasures that have been hidden and sealed for generations [5](#_ftn84), and the king himself stands in the thick of the battle, risking his life. All of this is done for the sake of winning the war, and from this it is understood how deeply *Netzach* touches the soul.

The Rebbe says this in relation to our current time—the final time before the *Geulah*, the time of the completion of the *birurim*. As the Rebbe wrote in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah*, now is the time before the *Geulah*, and the *avodah* now is specifically through the path of *Netzach* and *kabbalas ol*.

In order to win the war, they spent the "treasures that have been hidden and sealed for generations"—these are all the matters and stories that the Rebbe revealed during the

#### 21

recent time, which had been hidden and sealed for generations, back to the generation of the Baal Shem Tov and his teacher, the author of *Chai* [6](#_ftn85).

The fact that the Rebbe revealed all these matters constitutes an act of "spending" in the literal sense, for no one is taking these matters to heart as they should, and therefore it is a literal squandering—all for the sake of victory.

Since all of this did not suffice, the Rebbe adds in the *maamar* that "the king himself stands in the thick of the battle." This is how the Rebbe acted as well; he did not occupy himself only with lofty matters, but dealt with and handled everything himself, even the simplest of things. He himself stood in the thick of the battle.

Had we been worthy, all these matters would have been enough to win the war, and the Rebbe would have already led us toward Moshiach. But since we did not dedicate ourselves to him as necessary, even this was not enough, and then, as the Rebbe adds in the *maamar*, the king risks his life.

(The Rebbe wept bitterly and finally concluded:) Since the Rebbe does not write anything more than this

#### 21a

in the *maamar*, and a *maamar* is Torah, the ruling of the Torah is that now this is sufficient. One must only gird oneself with strength and *gevurah* to win the war, and the Rebbe will lead us toward Moshiach.

## With the help of Hashem. Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5710

#### 21b

Unedited

It is told of one of the Chassidim that whatever subject he would speak about, he would always conclude with the concept of creation *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing).

This is how it should be for every Jew as well: whatever subject one speaks about, one should always conclude with a matter that pertains to his *neshamah*.

## B's"D. Sicha of the First Day of Pesach, 5710

#### 22

– After davening in the hall of the Rebbe Rayatz, n"e –

Unedited

In the past, when all the doors were closed (and people were not allowed to enter), everyone would gather and push their way in; yet now, when all the doors are open, they do not come.

There were, indeed, some who came to see what was happening after they had conducted their own Seder, but not one of them brought their "Afikoman" with them to eat it in the same room where the Rebbe would conduct the "Sedarim"[1](#_ftn86), and to continue the Seder there until the opening of the door for Eliyahu Hanavi.

– It is known[2](#_ftn87) that Eliyahu Hanavi can be in several places at one time only when he does not come himself, but rather only a spark of him; however, when he comes himself (not merely a spark of him), he is then in only one place, as we find at the time he needed to save Rav Hamnuna Sava, for whose sake he had to come himself, and therefore he could not be in another place at that time.

(And the Rebbe shlita concluded:) Could there be a greater and more sublime revelation of Eliyahu Hanavi than in the room where the Rebbe conducted the "Sedarim" for ten years?!...

And even after the histalkus—we find[3](#_ftn88) regarding Rabbeinu Hakadosh that after his histalkus, *he would come to his home* on Friday night (and similarly on the night of Yom Tov) and recite Kiddush, thereby exempting the many[4](#_ftn89).

## From the Sicha of Acharon Shel Pesach, 5710

#### 23

**A.** It is stated in the Gemara: "The Sages taught: At the time of his passing, Rebbe said to his children, 'I am in need of you... a lamp shall be lit in its place, a table shall be set in its place, a bed shall be made in its place.'"

The explanation of this is as follows:

"Passing" (*petirah*) also means a transition from one place to another, from one matter to another, from one type of avodah to another—similar to the term *Haftarah*, which is a *petirah* and transition from the Torah to the Prophets. Likewise, regarding the "passing of Rebbe," it means a transition to a place and a mode of avodah that is incomparably higher. As our Sages said, "The tzaddikim have no rest, neither in this world nor in the World to Come, as it is written, 'They go from strength to strength,'" meaning they constantly ascend from one level of elevation to the next.

The novelty here is that "at the time of his *passing*, Rebbe said, *'I am in need of you'*":

Since at the time of his "passing," he begins a mode of avodah that is entirely incomparable, one might think that he no longer has any connection to us.

Rebbe clarifies this at the time of his passing by saying, "I am in need of you": Even though I am now ascending to an entirely higher order of avodah, nevertheless, I remember you, and I will remember you wherever I may be. And more than that, even for me, in the highest of elevations, your avodah is relevant—"*I am in need of you*," meaning, not only do the children need him, but even more, he needs the children.

**B.** Therefore, all the matters for which it was customary to turn to Rebbe remain in their place—"a lamp shall be lit in its place, a table shall be set in its place, a bed shall be made in its place":

Generally, people would come to Rebbe (for *yechidus*) for two types of matters: *tikkun* (rectification) and spiritual sustenance, and *tikkun* and physical sustenance (though not material). Each category is divided into three details—lamp, table, and bed.

#### 24

*Yechidus* regarding physical matters is divided into three things: children, life, and sustenance (*banai, chayei, u’mezonei*), which correspond to the lamp, table, and bed: "Life" is the "lamp," as it is written, "The lamp of Hashem is the soul of man." "Sustenance" is the "table," and "children" are the "bed."

And all these things "stand in their place"—even after his passing, Rebbe can answer, and he answers just as before, and he bestows influence now just as before.

The same applies to *yechidus* regarding spiritual matters—which are divided into the three categories of lamp, table, and bed:

"Lamp" refers to the totality of the mitzvos, as it is written, "For a mitzvah is a lamp." "Table" refers specifically to Torah, which, in addition to being a "garment" like other mitzvos, is also "sustenance." And in addition to matters connected with proper conduct according to Torah (table) and mitzvos (lamp), there is also the rectification of the state of a person's fall—one who has sinned, caused a blemish, and strayed from the path because a "spirit of folly" entered him, placing him in the state of one who is lying down, where the head is on the same level as the feet. This state is included in the "bed." More specifically, this is connected with rectifying the blemish in matters of *shemiras habris* (and likewise *shemiras halashon*, which are interconnected), and specifically the sins that are a general separation between him and Hashem—which must be rectified so that "his bed will be complete."

And these matters also "stand in their place"—even in a state of fall and blemish, one should not think that he is completely severed and that no connection can exist with Rebbe after his passing. Rather, he must know that even now, Rebbe answers questions regarding the rectification of blemishes and the fall of man, just as before.

**C.** One might ask regarding this:

It is known that for the sake of an answer in *yechidus*, there must be some connection

#### 25

to the person, at least in the most subtle of subtleties, as in the well-known story regarding the Mitteler Rebbe.

If so, it is understandable in the past, when Rebbe was in a physical body in this world, that since he was clothed in a body, there was at least a connection in the most subtle of subtleties, as told about the Mitteler Rebbe. But now, since he has no such connection, how can he answer such things?

**D.** The answer to this is by way of a preface, addressing those who ask: How is it at all appropriate to ask of Rebbe, given that this is a matter of an "intermediary"?

Others ask this in connection with matters of *yiras shamayim*. A certain *mashliach* used to take a *pidyon* when asked to deliver one regarding physical matters, but he would not take a *pidyon* regarding spiritual matters, saying that even the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not do this, as the saying goes, "Everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven."

The answer to this:

Just as "Israel, the Torah, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are all one"—meaning, not only are Israel connected to the Torah and the Torah to the Holy One, Blessed be He, but they are literally "one"—so too is the connection between Chassidim and Rebbe. It is not like two things becoming united, but rather they become literally "all one." Rebbe is not an "intermediary that separates," but an "intermediary that connects." Consequently, for a Chossid, he, Rebbe, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are all one.

—I have not seen this stated explicitly in the teachings of Chassidus, but this is a "feeling." Consequently, whoever wants to feel this way will feel it, and whoever does not—I do not wish to argue with him; let him have what he has.—

Consequently, there is no room for the question regarding an "intermediary," since this is the *Atzmus* Himself, as He placed Himself ("*vi er hot zich areingeshtelt*") into a body.

This is similar to the statement of the Zohar, "Who is the face of the Master, Hashem? This is Rashbi," or as

#### 26

we find that at the time of a mission, even an angel is called by the name of Hashem, or as Moshe Rabbeinu said, "And I will give grass."

Likewise, there is no room for the question of how he answers regarding matters of "below" and the like, because the connection between Rebbe and Chassidim is an essential connection ("*a atzmius'diker farbund*"). And therefore Rebbe said: Wherever I may be—I am in need of you.

**E.** Rebbe is with us as in the past. He is in his room and hears us *farbrenging* here.

If so, why are we *farbrenging* here? Because it is his will that we *farbreng*.

Once, Rebbe turned on the microphone in his room and heard the *farbrengen* here. It is the same now, and to a greater extent, of course.

**F.** In *Sefer Chassidim* it is brought that Rabbeinu HaKadosh would come every Erev Shabbos at twilight to his home in his Shabbos clothes, make Kiddush, and exempt the masses.

Now, too, is the time of twilight after Mincha, and Rabbeinu HaKadosh comes to make Kiddush, and also remains for the night.

**G.** This winter, I once entered Rebbe's room. He was sitting, leaning on his hand, immersed in thought, and he told me that he wished to travel to Eretz Yisrael. I said to Rebbe: How is it possible to travel, when there is so much work here? He thought for a moment and said: "Nu, a beautiful idea."

In his thought, he was already in Eretz Yisrael. The bones of Yosef were brought to Eretz Yisrael.

**H.** Once, a Chossid came from a distant place and asked Rebbe to say a *maamar* of Chassidus. Rebbe answered him that he says Chassidus on Shabbos. The Chossid replied that when he comes to Rebbe, it is Shabbos for him. And then Rebbe said Chassidus.

#### 27

Even now, through proper *hiskashrus*, it is possible for everyone, every day and at every time, that it should be Shabbos, and Rebbe comes, makes Kiddush, and exempts the masses—meaning, he bestows influence upon them as if they had made Kiddush themselves, but—even more than that—Kiddush with his *kavanos*, and consequently with his holiness.

## With the help of Heaven. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Shemini, Mevarchim HaChodesh Iyar, 5710

#### 28

A. It is explained in one of the maamarim of the renowned Chossid, R. Hillel of Paritch, that the general concept of *galus* exists because of the mixture of good and evil. Conversely, in a level that is entirely good, the concept of destruction (*churban*) is not applicable. The maamar concludes: "As was said by the late R. Y. A. in the name of the Alter Rebbe, that before lofty souls such as Rashbi, the Beis Hamikdash was not destroyed at all."

Regarding the greatness of Rashbi, we find in the Zohar that he brought about rainfall through the recitation of Torah, unlike Choni HaMe'agel, who required prayer. The difference between them is that the action of Choni HaMe'agel (prayer) is within the realm of worldly matters, through speech and petition, because the world was in need of rain. Rashbi, however, was essentially disconnected from worldly matters [as is stated in the Gemara that Rashbi said, "Is it possible that a person plows... and sows... and what will become of Torah?"], but when he was told that a world exists and that the world is in need of rain, his action was performed through the *recitation of Torah* (which is above the world). Consequently, the *hemshech* (drawing down of energy) was effected, even into this physical world.

Since the primary focus of Rashbi in Torah is *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah, which was revealed through him)—which is a level that is entirely good, the "Tree of Life," and not the "Tree of Good and Evil"—it is understood that within Pnimiyus HaTorah (the core of Rashbi’s essence), the concept of destruction does not apply (just as it did not apply to Rashbi himself). Consequently, in this regard, there must be, in several matters, a state similar to the time of the Beis Hamikdash.

**B.** Regarding the timing: as we now come from the festival of Pesach:

Concerning the reception and absorption of the revelations that were manifest during the time of the Beis Hamikdash during the pilgrimage, as the saying goes, "Just as he comes to see, so he comes to be seen"—it is stated in *Likutei Torah* that "from every festival and Yom Tov, there was drawn down... until the next festival."

#### 29

Just as in the time of the Beis Hamikdash, vitality was drawn from the revelation of "coming to see and be seen" during the festival of Pesach until the next Yom Tov, so too is it now. The drawing down of vitality comes from the revelation of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* that was revealed during the festival of Pesach—the *maamarim of Pesach* that have now been published—and this revelation must provide vitality until the next revelation that will be manifest when the next festival arrives.

By way of introduction, one might raise an objection: these maamarim are not new; they existed previously, and if so, this is not a revelation. But the truth is that the printing and dissemination itself is a revelation.

On 12 Tammuz 5692, the Rebbe Rayatz said: When one repeats a maamar of Chassidus sixty times, one "hears" the essence. This is how the Rebbe (Rashab) would sometimes conduct himself regarding the maamarim of his father, the Rebbe Maharash.

I asked the Rebbe then: Was the repetition of the maamar in each of the sixty times with additional explanation? He replied: Not necessarily. I added: Is there also an increase in comprehension? He replied: Certainly, an effect is also produced in comprehension, and it is possible that the effect of the sixtieth time compared to the fifty-ninth is like the effect of the fifty-ninth compared to the first!

Thus, it turns out that a maamar which the Rebbe Maharash said in private and in public, and many times—no less than twice [as is known the custom of the Rebbe Maharash—frequently—that first he would say the maamar to his sons, or to the Rebbe (Rashab) in private, and afterwards he would say it in public (and sometimes in reverse order, first in public and then in private)], and afterwards it was repeated many times—nevertheless, each time, both in its repetition and even at the sixtieth time, a new revelation was drawn down.

From this, it is understood also regarding the maamarim of the festival of Pesach mentioned above—that since they have been published, and certainly through *Hashgacha Pratis*, this is a *new revelation*. Consequently, one must receive and absorb this revelation and live with it until the next Yom Tov.

**C.** In accordance with this, one must begin with a matter from the maamarim of Pesach:

In the maamar for Pesach, it is stated that the singing of the angels (their prostration) is the nullification of their materiality.

#### 30

Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: regarding angels as they exist above, what relevance is there to such "materiality" that requires nullification?

The matter is as explained in the *Hemshech* of Rosh Hashanah: in every thing there is matter and form, which are body and soul, and similarly with angels. Therefore, even though the materiality of angels does not cause confusion, nevertheless, since it is not nullified with the same nullification as their soul, it is necessary to nullify it through song, which is the nullification of their materiality.

**D.** By way of introduction: the discussion regarding the service of the angels is primarily to explain the matter in terms of the *avodah* that pertains to us.

I emphasize "pertains to us" based on the response of the Rebbe Rayatz to someone who asked him two questions—one question regarding matters of *avodah*, *ahavah*, and *yirah*, and a second question regarding the service of the angels. The Rebbe Rayatz answered the first question, and regarding the second, he wrote to him that since *the service of the angels* does not pertain to *his avodah*, he would not answer that question.

Similarly in our case, the main point is the explanation in *avodah* that pertains to us—as will be explained regarding a similar matter that we find in the parsha of the week, Parshas Shemini.

**E.** The beginning of the parsha—"And it came to pass on the eighth day"—is in the greatness of the eighth day of the *miluim* (inauguration) relative to the greatness of the seven days of the *miluim*, in which the establishment of the Mishkan was completed and the *Shechinah* descended:

During all seven days of the *miluim*, Moshe would set it up and dismantle it, and on that day—the eighth day of the *miluim*—he set it up and did not dismantle it.

The establishment of the Mishkan during the seven days of the *miluim* also constitutes an eternal matter, because any thing that is done according to the command of the Torah is an eternal matter.

—And therefore: even though any knot that one intends to untie is not a permanent knot, nevertheless, when this knot is made according to the command of the Torah, it can be said that it is considered—in several respects—a permanent knot, similar to the concept of "His mitzvos are dear to Him," for since it is done according to Torah, it is an eternal matter. Its actual existence below is within a specific time, but its essence is eternal.

#### 31

And furthermore: even when the untying of the knot (which one intends to untie) is according to Torah, nevertheless, the knot—while it exists—is considered an eternal matter, and the untying—in its time—is also an eternal matter; that is, each one in its time is an eternal matter. This is similar to what is explained in *Tanya* that "this unification above is eternal forever and ever, but below it is subject to time."

With this, the matter of the knot of the *tefillin* is resolved, according to the opinions that hold that every day one must untie the knot and make it anew, that nevertheless it is a permanent knot.

But even so, this is not comparable to the establishment of the Mishkan on the eighth day—which he set up and did not dismantle in actual fact.

Especially since on the eighth day there was a lofty matter that did not exist at all during the seven days prior—"And a fire went forth from before Hashem and consumed upon the altar, etc.," that the *Shechinah* descended to Israel.

And in addition to the beginning of the parsha regarding the greatness of the days of the *miluim*, the parsha continues regarding the death of the two sons of Aharon, and continues with the command, "Do not drink wine or strong drink, etc., when you come into the Tent of Meeting, etc.,"—"those who were intoxicated with wine entered the Sanctuary... after their death, He warned the survivors not to enter the Sanctuary intoxicated with wine"—which is also a lofty matter, as is known, that the death of the two sons of Aharon was a matter of *ratzo* (running) without *shov* (returning). And since it was necessary to warn and negate such *avodah*, it is understood that *Bnei Yisrael* were then at an extremely lofty level, to the point that they needed to be warned against *kilos hanefesh* (the soul expiring) in actual fact.

According to this, an explanation is required for what is written at the end of the parsha regarding the prohibition of eating creeping things and swarming things, which a person’s soul finds repulsive, which even from the perspective of human intellect is extremely disgusting—for seemingly: after such lofty matters (at the beginning and continuation of the parsha), what is the need to warn about such a thing? And furthermore, the warning about this is only from the perspective of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke)—"For I am Hashem who brings you up from the land of Egypt to be your G-d," "on the condition that you accept My mitzvos"?

**F.** A similar example we find also in the daily *shiur* in *Tanya*:

#### 32

After the lengthy explanation that every person of Israel can come *through contemplation* to fear Hashem (at least *yirah tata'ah*), the daily *shiur* adds that "just as with a king of flesh and blood, the essence of fear is from his inwardness and vitality and not from his body... (even though) his inwardness and vitality are not seen by the eyes of flesh, only *by the eyes of the intellect* through seeing with the eyes of flesh his body and his garments, for he knows that his vitality is clothed within them... exactly so must he fear Hashem through seeing with the eyes of flesh the heavens and the earth and all their host, in which the *Ohr Ein Sof* is clothed to give them life." And it adds further in the *hagah* (gloss), that "even one who has never seen the king and does not know him at all, nevertheless, when he enters the king's courtyard and sees many ministers and dignitaries bowing to one man, awe and fear will fall upon him."

And after this—at the conclusion of the daily *shiur*—it adds: "And also to be a constant remembrance... *kabbalas ol malchus shamayim*, etc."

And seemingly: since it is in the ability of everyone to come to fear through contemplation—what is the need for *kabbalas ol*? Especially since *kabbalas ol* and *yirah* are close and related to each other in their essence and their actions?

**G.** Similarly, one must understand also in the maamar for the festival of Pesach:

The order of things in the maamar in explaining the details of the *avodah* of *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah* is *from above to below*: first it explains the matter of *chayah*, and afterwards *neshamah*, and afterwards *ruach*, and afterwards *nefesh*—the *avodah* in actual fact by way of *kabbalas ol*. And nevertheless, it concludes afterwards with the matter of *yechidah*.

And seemingly, in order to conclude with the level of *yechidah*, an inverse order would be more appropriate, from below to above, especially since this order also fits the interpretation of "Tithe so that you may become wealthy" (with which the maamar begins), as it explains at the end of the maamar that "you may become wealthy" is the revelation of the level of *yechidah*?

**H.** Parenthetical note:

The truth is that it is not possible to ask questions of the Rebbe regarding the order of from below to above or from above to below, as he is above the limitations of above and below, and from the perspective of "the impossible of impossibilities," questions are not applicable at all.

And as is known, the task of the Rebbes is preparation for the coming of Moshiach, because, at the coming of

#### 33

Moshiach it is written, "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh shall see it together," that is, they will see ("and see") *Elokus* with the physical eye of flesh, and the preparation for this is done by the word of Hashem being revealed to everyone through a physical body that is seen by the eyes of flesh face-to-face, for the response of the Rebbe [which was usually in "jargon" (Yiddish), and from time to time he would also mix in a word in English or Russian, and the like] is in a manner that "the spirit of Hashem spoke in me and His word was upon my tongue."

—This matter pertains especially to the current situation: just as in the past it was ingrained in everyone who entered for *yechidus* that the Rebbe is a *neshamah klalis* (a general soul) [not a general of details, but a general in essence, which is above details], and upon entering he would be completely nullified [for, if he was not nullified, it is not an entry for *yechidus*, or it is similar to the matter that "even at the time of the sin, he was in faith with Him, may He be blessed"], so too must it be ingrained now, without questions. And to note also from what is explained in the daily *shiur* in *Tanya* regarding the fear of the king, that "the essence of fear is *from his inwardness and vitality* and not from his body," and regarding his inwardness and vitality, nothing has changed.

Indeed, even though the Rebbe is above limitations and order, and questions are not applicable, nevertheless, the maamar was given to us to learn and understand specifically with intellect, comprehension, and understanding, and consequently it is required that it be in a manner of order. And similarly regarding the questions in the daily *shiur* in *Tanya* and the parsha of the week, as above.

**I.** And it can be said that the point of the explanation in all of this is:

*Kabbalas ol*—on one hand, is the lowest level, below contemplation; that is, at first, *avodah* is required in a manner of contemplation, but sometimes contemplation does not have the power to effect its action, and then there is a need for the *avodah* to be in a manner of *kabbalas ol*.

And on the other hand—*kabbalas ol* is the most lofty level, above contemplation in a manner of understanding and comprehension, because comprehension is a limitation, whereas the Essence, which is without limit, is not grasped in comprehension and in the multiplicity of details within it.

—And on the contrary: the Essence, from the perspective of its simplicity, shines also in comprehension and comes in many ways and in a multiplicity of details, but it is not grasped in this, and after the perfection of comprehension, it is recognized and felt that this is not the essence of the matter—

#### 34

Whereas *kabbalas ol* is in the Essence without limit, and even when it shines in comprehension and there is pleasure in it, nevertheless, its essence is *kabbalas ol* which is above all matters.

And more specifically:

The need for *kabbalas ol* (at the lower level) is from the perspective of the body—that because of the concealment and hiding of the materiality of the body (as mentioned above (section G) that even with angels there must be the nullification of their materiality), a situation is possible where contemplation does not effect an action, and therefore there is a need for *kabbalas ol*.

And on the other hand—for the positive—that since the root of the body is from a place and level that is above intellect, comprehension, and contemplation, therefore its connection is in essence to matters that are above comprehension, etc., which is the matter of *kabbalas ol* (at the higher level).

**J.** According to this, one can explain the order in the daily *shiur* in *Tanya*, that after contemplation it concludes with *kabbalas ol*—in which are included the two extremes of *kabbalas ol*: the *kabbalas ol* that is necessary for the *avodah* in practice when contemplation does not effect its action, and also the *kabbalas ol* that is after contemplation, which is above intellect and comprehension.

And it can be said that this matter is hinted at also in the conclusion of the daily *Tanya* *shiur* (after the matter of *kabbalas ol*)—in the words "as is written in another place":

Seemingly—what is the point: if he does not want to add explanation—he should have concluded "and the intelligent will understand," and the like; and if his desire is to ease the understanding of the learner by having him find an explanation in another place—he should have noted the place where the matter is explained with additional explanation?

And it can be said—by way of wit—that he gave us a hint by writing "as is written in another place," that after the explanation in any place that one studies, there will always remain "another place," a loftier level, in which the comprehension is in a loftier manner.

And similar to the story that is brought in the *Siddur* of the Maharid [which even though it was not brought in the books of

#### 35

Chassidus, nevertheless, the instruction of the Rebbe is known in such cases that for the sake of benefit in *avodah* "it does not matter"...] regarding the holy Rabbi R. M. M. of Horodok, that "he said before the Alter Rebbe that he sees in 'Atah Hareisa' a hundred interpretations and cannot fulfill them in action, therefore he wanted to prevent himself from saying the verses, and the Alter Rebbe replied to him regarding this: the rule is that in every place where his eyes see from afar, he cannot stand himself there on that place, and when he comes to that place, then he will see with his eyes another place far from him, and if so, when you fulfill the hundred interpretations, then you will see many more interpretations, and there is no end to the matter."

And the reason for the matter—as stated—is that comprehension is in limitation, whereas the Essence, even though it shines in comprehension, is not grasped in it, whereas *kabbalas ol*, even when it shines in comprehension, is in the Essence without limit.

**K.** According to this, one can explain also regarding the order of the parsha of the week:

Even though the beginning of the parsha is in lofty matters (the eight days of the *miluim* and *kilos hanefesh*), the parsha concludes with the matter of *kabbalas ol*—"For I am Hashem who brings you up from the land of Egypt to be your G-d," "on the condition that you accept My mitzvos"—from the perspective of the greatness of the elevation of *kabbalas ol* which is above all matters.

And on the other hand, this matter is stated regarding the prohibition of eating creeping things—in which is emphasized the greatness of the necessity of *kabbalas ol*, because, without *kabbalas ol*, one can over the course of time fall to the status and situation of eating creeping things, G-d forbid.

And from this is understood also the practical outcome—that in all situations and at all levels there is a need for *kabbalas ol*.

**L.** And this is also the explanation of the order of things in the maamar for the festival of Pesach:

The reason that it explains the matters of *avodah* in the order of from above to below, contemplation and afterwards *kabbalas ol*, is because the main thing for him is the matter of *avodah* in practice, and therefore, even though *ab initio* there must be contemplation, nevertheless, when contemplation does not effect an action, there is a need for *kabbalas ol*.

And after it concludes with the *avodah* that is from the perspective of the level of *nefesh*, whose matter is *kabbalas ol*, it adds and continues and concludes with the level of *yechidah*—in which is emphasized the greatness of *kabbalas*

#### 36

*ol* which is above comprehension, from which one comes to *yechidah* (the one who receives from one small spark, a *yachid*), which is the matter of "Tithe so that you may become wealthy."

## With the help of Heaven. From a Sicha on the night of 2 Iyar, 5710

#### 37

**A.** We begin with a *devar malchus* — as explained by my father-in-law, the Rebbe [1] — "with a word of the Rebbe":

In the *maamar* for the festival of Pesach, on the verse "On this very day, all the hosts of Hashem went out from the land of Egypt" [2], my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains the reason why, at the time of the Exodus, the Jewish people were called by the name "hosts of Hashem." It is because they were then at the level of a "host" (*tzava*), whose *avodah* is (not merely the work of a servant, but) such that they stand at their post with *mesiras nefesh* (unlike a servant, who, even if he performs his work with great toil, does not do so with *mesiras nefesh*). They "guarded themselves to be distinguished [3] in that they did not change their names, their language, or their dress [4], and they stood at their post with the utmost strength" [5].

Someone asked me (by letter): Seemingly, there is a contradiction in this matter within the *Midrashim* of our Sages—for the statement that "they did not change their names, their language, or their dress" contradicts the statement [6] that "these were idolaters and those were [idolaters]..."?

Simply put, one could say that this does not refer to actual idol worship, but rather to the matter of *shituf* (associating the name of Hashem with others). At the time of the Exodus (before the Giving of the Torah), they had the status of *Bnei Noach*, who are not prohibited from *shituf* (as is written in the *Shaar HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, in the *mitzvah* of the oneness of Hashem [7]). However, in the inner dimension of things, this is not a sufficient answer, for it is not plausible that Scripture would praise them with the title of a *host* who stand at their post with *mesiras nefesh* for the faith of Hashem, at the very same time that they were involved in *shituf*.

Therefore, we must say that they certainly had complete faith, and there is proof of this: "They did not say, 'How shall we go out into the wilderness without provisions?' Rather, they *believed* and went" [8]. Rather, it is that from the side of the *Sitra Achra*, foreign thoughts arose against the faith in Hashem, as explained in *Tanya* [9], but this does not, Heaven forbid, weaken the strength of the faith that comes from the essence of their souls.

#### 38

— Once, a Jew entered the Tzemach Tzedek and complained that doubts in faith were falling into his thoughts. The Tzemach Tzedek asked: "And what does it bother you?" He replied: "Rebbe, I am a Yid!" The Tzemach Tzedek answered him: "Then it is good..." And in such a manner was the status and situation of the Jewish people at the time of the Exodus.

\*

**B.** In a *sicha* for Lag B'Omer 5701 (printed in the *Kuntres Lag B'Omer HaShtah* [10]), it is stated that Lag B'Omer is in the *Sefirah* of *Tiferes*, *Tiferes* within *Tiferes*. The explanation of this [11] is that in addition to the order of *Sefiras HaOmer* from "above to below," from *Chesed* within *Chesed* to *Malchus* within *Malchus*—according to which order it turns out that 2 Iyar (this day) is *Tiferes* within *Tiferes* and Lag B'Omer is *Hod* within *Hod*—there is also an order from "below to above," from *Malchus* within *Malchus* to *Chesed* within *Chesed*. According to this order, it turns out that 2 Iyar (this day) is *Hod* within *Hod*, and Lag B'Omer is *Tiferes* within *Tiferes*.

The matter can be explained briefly:

The intent of *avodah* from above to below is so that through it there will be an elevation from below to above. Therefore, the intent of the elevation from below to above is concealed within the *avodah* from above to below.

And likewise regarding *Sefiras HaOmer*: Since it follows and is a continuation of the Exodus, which is connected with the *avodah* of *tzaddikim* from above to below (unlike Elul and Tishrei, whose matter is the *avodah* of *baalei teshuvah*, from below to above) [12], it is also in the manner of from above to below, and within this, the intent of the elevation from below to above is concealed.

Therefore, the order of *Sefiras HaOmer* in a revealed and public manner is from above to below, and within this, the order of from below to above is concealed in a *makif* (encompassing) manner [13].

And more specifically—regarding *Tiferes* and *Hod*:

*Tiferes* and *Hod* are related to one another, for both are related to beauty [14]. Also, it is known [15] that the *Tiferes* of the higher level becomes a *Keter* (crown) for the lower level. In our case, when the higher level contemplates the beauty (*Tiferes* within *Tiferes*) that will be achieved through the lower level, this causes it to desire to descend

#### 39

to the lower level, even though it does not yet belong to it. Then, it is drawn into the lower level (*Hod* within *Hod*, as explained in the *Siddur*, *Shaar Lag B'Omer* [16]).

Therefore: In practice and in revelation, the order is that the higher descends to the lower—*Tiferes* within *Tiferes* and then *Hod* within *Hod*. But from the perspective of the intent concealed within the descent below—the beauty that will be achieved through the lower level—the order is *Hod* within *Hod* (the descent below) and then *Tiferes* within *Tiferes* (for through the descent below, the perfection of beauty is achieved) [17].

**C.** In the *Siddur Torah Or*, it is printed for the twenty-ninth day of the Omer: "*Hod* within *Chesed*," and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, corrected it and wrote in his *Siddur*: "*Chesed* within *Hod*."

And according to what is known [18] that everything in the world is by Divine Providence, and especially matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*—it must be said:

The *Nasi* of the Jewish people, in the time of exile, and especially in the footsteps of *Mashiach*, must *write* (similar to what is explained in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Masei* [19] regarding the interpretation of the verse [20] "And Moshe wrote") the *Chesed* within *Hod* [21].

\*

**D.** Regarding the text of the *pidyon* (petition) that one gives to the Rebbe—if I had the strength, I would remove the text that writes "from the source of mercy, etc., in the manner of 'those who bring mercy,' as explained in the *teshuvah* of the Mahariv, of blessed memory," because:

1) "In the manner of 'those who bring mercy,' as explained in the *teshuvah* of the Mahariv, of blessed memory"—is an *explanation of the permission* to give a *pidyon* to a Rebbe (which seemingly is a matter of an intermediary), based on what is explained in the *teshuvah* of the Mahariv, of blessed memory [22], regarding the saying of "those who bring mercy." Consequently, this does not concern or relate to the text of the *pidyon*, whose purpose is the *request for mercy* ("Please awaken great mercy"), and not an explanation of the permission for it.

2) And regarding the text "from the source of mercy"—there is no need to give the Rebbe an "address" from where to awaken mercy; he knows himself from where to awaken mercy... And perhaps his desire is to awaken mercy from a level even higher than the "source of mercy."

#### 40

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, indeed wrote this text [23], but that is his conduct, and it is no proof that we—who do not understand the matters of a Rebbe ("*Rebbe'ske zachen*")—must write so.

— A few days ago, a *yungerman* came to me and told me, with excitement, that once my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told him that through being connected to him, he would be connected (through him) to the One to whom he (the Rebbe himself) is connected...

Being that he was excited, I did not want to cool him down, but in truth, this does not concern us (to whom he—the Rebbe—is connected). We are connected *to him*, and for us, there is nothing higher than that ("*Hecher fun dem iz far undz nito*").

An example of this: Regarding a limb in the human body, it is appropriate to say that it draws its vitality from the liver, from the heart (which is above the liver), and even from the brain (which is above the heart as well), but there is no place to say or think about drawing vitality from the brain of another person. A living limb that desires its life and does not want to be a withered limb, Heaven forbid, must receive vitality from its own brain. And likewise regarding the connection to the Rebbe, who is the head (brain) and the crown of our generation.

\*

**E.** Receiving influences from the *Nasi* of the generation is also connected with the obligation of repayment, just as a borrower is obligated to repay the loan to the lender. And the obligation of repayment is not in a way that he pays the debt and is finished ("*opgetzalt un patur gevoren*"), but rather, that through repaying the debt, they give him more on credit [24]. And likewise in the analogy, that they give him more powers, and he is obligated to repay them, and so on.

(The Rebbe turned to the *temimim* and said:)

Each and every one of you must know that you are obligated to repay my father-in-law, the Rebbe, with your own essential powers, the level of *Chayah Yechidah*.

By way of introduction:

There is a common denominator in all the influences that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, bestows—the saying of *Chassidus*, answers to questions, etc., and even financial support and the like—that in all these matters, the influence comes from his own essential powers, *Chayah Yechidah*.

— They asked [25] me in what the Rebbe's greatness was expressed compared to other great figures of

#### 41

the Jewish people? And I answered: Every one of the great figures had a specific matter in which he was occupied and in which his greatness lay, whereas the Rebbe was occupied *with all matters*, from the most sublime matters to the most simple matters (and in the language of our Sages [26], "a great matter is the *Maaseh Merkavah*, a small matter is the *Havayos* of Abaye and Rava"), from the revelation of the secrets of secrets of the Torah of *Chassidus*, to the putting on of *tefillin*, the keeping of *Shabbos*, etc., and even in physical matters, such as financial support. And to all these matters, he was devoted and dedicated *with his entire essence*, with his *Chayah Yechidah* [27].

[This question was asked by two *bochurim* (who have *semicha*...), and upon hearing the answer, they took out a notebook and wrote down the answer, saying: "Now we know what the Rebbe is." — "They have the Rebbe on paper"...] —

Indeed, the common denominator that all the influences are from the level of *Chayah Yechidah* is from the perspective of the *Mashpia* (the one who influences), but regarding the influence itself, and also regarding the recipients, there are differences in levels.

And in this matter, there is a special advantage for the students—that they receive the *Chayah Yechidah* of the Rebbe, and therefore, they are also obligated to repay *with their own Chayah Yechidah*.

And even though it is impossible to compare the repayment with their *Chayah Yechidah* to the *Chayah Yechidah* of the Rebbe, this is similar to what is explained in *Chassidus* [28] regarding the matter of "with all your *me'odecha*" [29], that even though it is "your *me'od* (very/might)," through this one draws down the true *Me'od*, without limit in essence.

**F.** Repaying the debt with the *Chayah Yechidah* is expressed in a movement of going out from limitations—both his own limitations ("*aroysgeyn fun di aygene hagbolos*"), and (all the more so) the limitations of the matters of the world.

Certainly, everyone has private matters that are demanded of him, but there is also a general matter that belongs to all the students—that they must be in a state of *separation from the matters of the world*, "And we are distinguished, I and Your people" [30]. That is, every student, when walking in the street, it should be noticeable that he is different ("*eppes andersh*") from the world.

— At the time of my father-in-law, the Rebbe's, arrival in the United States, there were complaints against him (not about the study itself, but) about the lack of order and discipline according to the custom of the world in the conduct of the *Yeshiva*. "This is a wild conduct ('*a vilde hanhaga*')," they claimed against him—

#### 42

which diminishes and cheapens ("*es macht billig*") the value of the entire environment. One Jew—a G-d-fearing man, specifically—wrote to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the study in the *Yeshiva* in itself is good, let them study even twenty hours a day, but the study must be in a manner of *order*. And why must they sway ("*shoklen zich*") and shout during the study, and why don't they establish the order practiced in the world, that when a student wants to ask a question he must first raise his finger, and the like? But the truth is, as mentioned, that it must be in a manner of separation from the world, above limitation.

**G.** And a special empowerment on this day—2 Iyar:

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, chose the day of 2 Iyar, *Tiferes* within *Tiferes*, as the day to begin writing the *Sefer Torah* for the welcoming of *Mashiach Tzidkeinu* [31].

— There is also a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from the day of 2 Iyar 5702 regarding the writing of the *Sefer Torah*, which I will give to be copied and publicized [32]. —

And according to what is known [33] that every Jew has a letter in the *Sefer Torah*, as hinted in the acronym of "Yisrael," "*Y*esh *S*ishim *R*iboh *O*sios *L*eTorah" (There are six hundred thousand letters to the Torah) [34], then 2 Iyar, the day of beginning the writing of the *Sefer Torah*, is similar to the day of birth, and consequently also the beginning of the *avodah*, of every Jew.

**H.** And regarding the practical aspect—for with my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the main thing was the *avodah* in practice—I suggested that everyone take upon themselves two things:

The first matter—regarding himself, to take upon himself some matter through which his connection to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, will be strengthened.
