And the second matter—regarding the other, to take upon himself to influence at least one Jew, whoever it may be, a *bochur* or a *yungerman*, to bring him closer to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and to the ways of *Chassidus*, to be deepening in *Chassidus* and occupied in the *avodah* of prayer [35].

**I.** The beginning of the action of bringing the other closer to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and to the ways of *Chassidus* can be through various matters, including also through telling stories of wonders

#### 43

and the like, but the purpose must be to bring him closer to *Chassidus*, which is the *essential* matter, the *Chayah Yechidah*, of the Rebbe, unlike matters of wonders which are only his *extension* [36].

The main connection is not connected with matters of wonders and the like, and furthermore, there is no need or benefit in this for the connection—and at both extremes: seeing wonders does not add anything, and the lack of seeing wonders (if a day, a week, or a month passes, and he has not seen a wonder from the Rebbe) does not detract anything. — The truth is, that if one wants, one will see that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, behaved with him also in his natural matters in a way that every single day there were wonders, but there is no need for this at all, and one should not be impressed by it.

— To the Tzemach Tzedek, an *agunah* once came with a mute son to ask for his blessing, and she could not enter the Tzemach Tzedek in any way, and even after she pleaded with the *Rebbetzin*—as all the women who came to the Tzemach Tzedek did—it did not help. The *Chassidim* advised her to write her question in a letter, and give it into the hand of her son, and at a time when there is no one, her son should enter and hide under the table in the room where the Tzemach Tzedek receives for *yechidus*, and when the Tzemach Tzedek enters, he should give him the note. And so it was. And when he gave the note to the Tzemach Tzedek, the Tzemach Tzedek said to him: "Go and tell your mother that your father is in such-and-such a place, *and both of you will be saved*." The son began to speak, and the woman found her husband. And when they told the Tzemach Tzedek—with excitement—that the mute son opened his mouth by saying to his mother the answer of the Tzemach Tzedek, he answered and said: "And how was I supposed to know that the son was mute?!"...

When the *Rebbetzin* of the Tzemach Tzedek—who was a woman of broad understanding (in general, the daughters of the Mitteler Rebbe were women of broad understanding)—heard this story, she was not impressed, and repeated the words of her grandfather, the Alter Rebbe: "In Mezritch, wonders rolled under the table, but no one had the time to bend down and pick them up..." —

Indeed, regarding the other, if there is a need, one can begin to bring him closer also through telling stories of wonders, but the purpose must be to bring him closer to *Chassidus*, as mentioned above.

**J.** And if someone thinks that when he takes upon himself (in addition to his own matters of *avodah*) to occupy himself also with the other, he will waste his time and through this will detract from his own *avodah*, and likewise other claims of this sort—one should not fear these claims at all, because:

#### 44

First of all—when someone sees that his fellow is drowning in the sea, he does not make calculations at all, and tries with all his might to save him [38]. And likewise regarding the action with the other, that when one needs to save him, one does not make any calculations.

And in addition to this, not only does the action on the other not detract from the *avodah* with oneself, but on the contrary, through the action with the other, one adds even more in the *avodah* with oneself, as the Sages interpret [39] the verse [40] "Hashem illuminates the eyes of both" (in addition to the greatness of the elevation of the action on the other, as our Sages said [41], "Whoever teaches his fellow's son Torah, Scripture considers it as if he made him").

One must occupy himself with both matters: with the study of *Chassidus* and with the *avodah* with oneself, and also with the action on the other.

To one of the *yungerman* who came to me, I said that they must extinguish the fire that is raging in the street, and when the *yungerman* replied that this is a business for businessmen and diamond merchants, whereas he must occupy himself with the study of Torah, and after he studies for fifteen years he will be a "great *posek* in Israel," and then he will have something to boast about... — I answered him: "When there is a fire, one does not make calculations." And as for his worrying that there should also be "learners," the blessing of the Alter Rebbe will certainly be fulfilled, that "learners will be among *Chassidim*." And *a fortiori*: If the "insolent ones" whom the Alter Rebbe *did not want* to be among *Chassidim*—exist, then the "learners" whom the Alter Rebbe *wanted* to be—will certainly be.

**K.** I heard [42] a story from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, about the Alter Rebbe, which contains a lesson and instruction regarding the action with the other:

Once on Yom Kippur after the *Shacharis* prayer, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe took off his *tallis* and *kittel*, and went to the edge of the city, and chopped wood and cooked soup for a woman who had just given birth and lived there. [When they asked the Alter Rebbe why he needed to do this himself, could he not have sent another person? He replied: "In a case of danger to life, there is a law of 'a *mitzvah* is best performed by the greatest'," and I did not find anyone greater.]

This story—concluded my father-in-law, the Rebbe—was not spoken about at all times. There was a time when they spoke about it, and there was a time when they did not speak about it, and certainly they did not want to publicize it.

And nevertheless, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, told this story to me, knowing "*az ich vell zich nit aynhalten*" (that I will not be able to restrain myself) from telling it to other Jews, with the addition of explaining the lesson and instruction from this story.

And one must explain the content of the story in *avodah*:

The level of the Alter Rebbe when he was wrapped in a *tallis* and *kittel* (similar to an angel [44]), on Yom Kippur, and after the prayer—cannot be estimated. And despite the greatness of his level, the Alter Rebbe took off the *tallis* and *kittel*, and went to the last house at the edge of the city, near the field, which indicates the most final level in holiness, which is close to the *kelipah*, "Esav... a man of the field" [45]—in order to help the woman who had given birth and the newborn, that is, to make another Jew ("*machen noch a idn*") [46].

This story constitutes a lesson and instruction for the entire congregation of *Chassidim* regarding the greatness of the necessity and the obligation in the *avodah* with the other. And therefore, everyone must take upon himself both regarding the *avodah* with himself, and regarding the *avodah* with the other, to bring him closer to the Torah of *Chassidus* [47].

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

## 46

It is stated in the Zohar (Vol. III, 288a) that on the day of his hilula, which is the day of Lag B’Omer, Rabbi Shimon opened and said, "I am to my Beloved, and His desire is upon me." [He continued,] "All the days that I have been bound to this world, I have been bound in one bond to the Holy One, blessed be He, and because of this, now, 'His desire is upon me.'"

It is well known that the explanation of the term "opened" as commonly used in the Zohar—that is, that he opened the channel of influence regarding this matter—means that then, others are also able to attain it. Just as in the generation of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, even children revealed the secrets of the Torah because Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, of blessed memory, opened the channel of influence of the inner dimension of the Torah.

And although, who is he and where is he whose heart would dare to approach the level of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai? Yet, Hashem has bared His holy arm and illuminated us through our teacher the Baal Shem Tov and his holy disciples, our holy Rebbes, the Nesi'im, may their merit protect us—up to and including my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—with the teachings of Chassidus. This [teaching] opens the gates of the chambers of Chochma and Binah and provides a path whereby *each and every one*, according to his own measure, can approach the holy to serve Hashem *with his mind and his heart*.

And on the day of the hilula of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, Lag B’Omer, which occurs every year, when this matter of "opening" is aroused, this day is uniquely suited to strengthen oneself and add courage in the study of the inner dimension of the Torah and in internal avodah. For, as my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote, these channels were opened by the master of the hilula until the coming of the righteous redeemer, speedily in our days, amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*Pesach Sheni, 5710*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## Sicha of Motzaei Pesach Sheni, 5710

#### 47

**1.** This farbrengen, which takes place after the Maariv prayer on the night of the 15th, still pertains to Pesach Sheni (the 14th), for the offering and eating of the Pesach Sheni are like the offering and eating of the first Pesach: the offering takes place on the 14th, and the eating is on the *night of the 15th*[1].

One should add regarding the connection of Pesach (Sheni) to the 15th of Iyar—that "on that day (the 15th of Iyar) *the matzah they brought out of Egypt was finished* ('And they baked the dough which they brought out of Egypt into cakes of matzah...')[2] and they required the Mohn."[3]

[Regarding the descent of the Mohn, we find a discussion[4] as to whether it actually began to descend on the 15th of Iyar, or if its actual descent began on the 16th of Iyar (and on the 15th of Iyar they were merely promised, "Behold, I will rain down for you bread from heaven...")[5]. However, regarding the matzah they brought out of Egypt—by all accounts, it sufficed for them until the 15th of Iyar.]

*

**2.** The essence of Pesach Sheni in the Sefiras HaOmer is *Chesed sheb'Hod*.

In the Siddur in which the Rebbe Rayatz prayed in his final years, it was printed by mistake as *Hod sheb'Chesed*, and the Rebbe Rayatz corrected it in his Siddur, writing *Chesed sheb'Hod*.

[The Rebbe Rayatz also used to mark and draw a sign in his Siddur after the counting of each night—even though he certainly did not need to seek methods to negate the fear of forgetfulness, a matter relevant to simple people, but not to the Rebbe[6].]

And according to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov[7] that everything is by Divine Providence and contains a lesson and instruction in Avodas Hashem [and as discussed above[8], that everything must be relevant to Avodas Hashem—which is why the Rebbe Rayatz did not answer a question regarding the service of the angels

#### 48

because it is not relevant to our Avodah]—one must explain the content of the matter that it was printed in the Siddur as *Hod sheb'Chesed* by Divine Providence, and the Rebbe Rayatz corrected it to *Chesed sheb'Hod*[9].

**3.** To begin with, let us explain the difference between *Chesed sheb'Hod* and *Hod sheb'Chesed* during the days of the Omer. *Chesed sheb'Hod* is on Pesach Sheni, which is called a *Yom Tov* (and in the language of the Mishnah[10]: "Pesach Katan"), while *Hod sheb'Chesed* is (not on a Yom Tov, but) on *Chol HaMoed*—which seemingly is difficult to understand:

*Hod sheb'Chesed*—its essence is *Chesed*, which is on the *right* line. And within the right line itself—at the beginning of the line (in relation to the middos, or in its middle, in relation to the general line as it begins from the mochin), its essence is *influence and revelation*, and even influence and revelation *in practice* (Netzach, Hod, Yesod), which is the concept of *Hod sheb'Chesed*.

Whereas *Chesed sheb'Hod*—its essence is *Hod*, which is on the *left* line. And within the left line itself—at the end of the line, its essence is *Gevurah and concealment*.

How is it possible that *Chesed sheb'Hod*, at the end of the left line, is a Yom Tov, while *Hod sheb'Chesed*, whose essence is Chesed at the beginning of the right line, is only Chol HaMoed?!

The explanation is as follows:

When one is in close proximity to the Yom Tov of Yetzias Mitzrayim, when the revelation of Chesed shines—revealed Chesed—then *Hod sheb'Chesed* suffices, the lower level of Chesed (regarding practice), and therefore it is not a Yom Tov but Chol HaMoed.

But as one moves further away from the revelation of the Yom Tov and arrives at a status and situation of concealment, which is the concept of Gevurah—including also Hod, which is a branch of Gevurah—one cannot suffice with *Hod sheb'Chesed* (since the Chesed is not revealed). Rather, there is a need to reveal the *Chesed* within the Hod; that is, the inner intent of the concealment (Hod, which is a branch of Gevurah) is revelation (Chesed). And on the contrary—it is a higher revelation, which, due to its great stature, is a Yom Tov (higher than *Hod sheb'Chesed*, which is only Chol HaMoed).

**4.** Based on this, one can explain the content of the correction made by the Rebbe Rayatz from *Hod sheb'Chesed* to *Chesed sheb'Hod*:

The fact that in the printing of the Siddur, *Chesed sheb'Hod* was missing by Divine Providence, proves that there was some *kitrug*—due to the intensification of the darkness of Galus—against the revelation of Chesed within the matter of Gevuros.

#### 49

And the correction for this was made by the Rebbe Rayatz, the Nasi of Yisroel at the end of the time of Galus—by writing "Chesed sheb'Hod" in his Siddur, he acted to ensure that there would be a revelation of the Chesed within the matter of Gevuros, that the inner intent of the concealment should be revealed, through which one arrives at a higher revelation.

*

**5.** This matter also constitutes a lesson, instruction, and empowerment regarding our current status and situation:

Despite the concealment of the histalkus and the ascent on high, we must know that the hiskashrus and dveikus that existed until now—for those who had the merit to see the Rebbe, whether those who saw the Rebbe many times, or those who saw him a few times or even once[11], and even for those who only merited to receive a letter, or heard from the Rebbe through studying his maamarim and sichos—the hiskashrus remains with them in full force, and there is no room for weakness...

(The Rebbe cried, and then continued:)

The Rebbe Rayatz said[12]: The teachings of Chassidus have acted so that the Rebbe is not isolated, and Chassidim are not isolated ("der Rebbe iz nit elent, un Chassidim zaynen nit elent"). That is, the Rebbe watches over and is concerned with every single detail in the lives of the Chassidim. And even now, when he is on a higher level, he watches over and is concerned with every single detail in the lives of the Chassidim (as discussed above[13]). Consequently, there is the empowerment to continue in all the matters that the Rebbe demands and requires of us.

And on the contrary: since the intent of the concealment is for the sake of revelation, we must now engage in all the matters that the Rebbe demands *with added strength*[14].

**6.** During the war, many Jews from various circles ("fremde iden") would come to the Rebbe in connection with the situation in Europe, and the Rebbe would urge that the Jews of America must—alongside their gratitude to the Ribono shel Olam that they are not in the valley of tears—do everything in their power to help the Jews of Europe. Once, a Jew who was a great scholar came to the Rebbe and asked:

#### 50

If the intent of creation is indeed for the sake of Yisroel, is it possible that the Ribbono shel Olam allows that wicked one, yimach shemo, to burn many Jews on the pyre, and specifically the choicest among them?! The Rebbe replied: When one wants to strike a person in such a place that the entire body feels not only the pain but also the shame, one strikes him on the "face"[15]...

—It is told about the Rebbe himself that when he studied in "cheder" by the melamed R' Shimshon[16], he had to suffer for the sake of the other students. When one of the students behaved improperly, the melamed would call the Rebbe and threaten him with punishment, saying that even though he (the Rebbe) did nothing, nevertheless, when the other students see the conduct with him, it will instill awe and fear in them, and they will improve their behavior[17].—

(And the Rebbe concluded:) We must feel the strike on the "face" *in the entire body*, and as a result, add strength and courage in all the matters that the Rebbe demands.

*

**7.** It is known as a saying of the Rebbe Rayatz[18] that the essence of Pesach Sheni is that it is never lost ("es iz nito kayn farfalen"); one can always rectify, even one who was tamei, one who was on a distant journey, and even "lachem," who was so by his own will—nevertheless, one can rectify.

This saying also constitutes a lesson and instruction regarding hiskashrus to the Rebbe:

There are those who were never by the Rebbe. There are also those who actually saw the Rebbe, and not just once but many times, but nothing was effected within them, so that in truth they were never by the Rebbe; "zey hoben nit derhert," and it only seems to them that they saw the Rebbe.

And since this is so, they might think that now it is already lost.

To this comes the instruction from Pesach Sheni—that even those who did not offer the first Pesach, and even if the reason for this is their own fault ("lachem"), they can rectify the past by offering Pesach Sheni. And likewise in our case, that even those who until now did not have the recognition and feeling, etc., can from here on recognize and feel ("derhern"), and thereby rectify the past as well.

#### 51

And the reason for this—as stated—is that the Rebbe is not isolated and the Chassidim are not isolated, and through the power of the Rebbe that is present with the Chassidim, one can also now recognize and feel, even if until now they did not recognize and feel.

**8.** And among the methods for this—is to visualize the Rebbe's face:

Anyone who was by the Rebbe in yechidus—should visualize for himself the Rebbe's face as he entered to him in yechidus. And those who did not see the Rebbe, should visualize the Rebbe's face through a picture.

Visualizing[19] the Rebbe's face is similar to and in the likeness of *seeing* his face, which has an advantage over studying his Torah, similar to the advantage of sight over hearing[20].

And the contemplation of the visualization of the Rebbe's face will awaken them to arrive at recognition and feeling ("derhern"), even if until now they did not have recognition and feeling.

**9.** Seemingly, there is room for wonder: How is it possible that in the past, when he was in yechidus, etc., there was no recognition and feeling, and specifically now there will be recognition and feeling?!

The answer to this—is that we find a parallel in the words of our Sages[21], "A person does not stand upon the mind of his Rebbe until forty years," from which it is understood that after forty years, "he stands upon the mind of his Rebbe":

The intent is not that now, after forty years, one must see his Rebbe and hear from him words of Torah, and then he will stand upon his Rebbe's mind, but rather, that after forty years, "he stands upon the mind of his Rebbe" regarding the matters he learned from his Rebbe forty years ago. Even though at the time, when he saw his Rebbe and learned from him, he did not descend to the depth of his mind, nevertheless, after forty years he merits to stand upon the depth of his mind.

And likewise in our case: even if at the time he did not have recognition and feeling, nevertheless, it can be now—through visualizing the Rebbe's face—recognition and feeling.

And in any case, whether there is recognition and feeling or not, this is not our business, and we must do what is incumbent upon us.

It is a clear matter that the Rebbe's intent will come to fruition in any case ("dem Rebbens kavana vet zich say-vi oysfirn"), but in order that this matter should be with Chesed and Rachamim, we must strive and do what the Rebbe demands and requires of us, to contemplate and contemplate again, and a covenant is made for *ta'amulah*—

#### 52

*ta'amulah* also regarding oneself—that it does not return empty[22], and eventually the contemplation will effect its action in a manner of recognition and feeling ("derhern").

*

**10.** In addition to the general instruction from the essence of Pesach Sheni that it is never lost, there is also a lesson and instruction from the reason for the tumah because of which they could not offer the first Pesach ("And there were men who were tamei by a human corpse and could not perform the Pesach on that day, etc."[23])—that we find several opinions regarding this[24], as follows.

And one must explain the lesson and instruction from the opinion that "those men... were engaged in a *meis mitzvah*":

A *meis mitzvah*, "one of Yisroel who was cast on the road (a corpse) and has no one to bury him"—"a Kohen who encounters him on the road, he must become tamei to him, even a Kohen Gadol is obligated to become tamei to him and bury him"[25], even when the Kohen is going to slaughter and offer the Pesach. And because he becomes tamei to him, he will not be able to offer the Pesach, as in our case, that "those men (who were tamei by a human corpse)... were engaged in a *meis mitzvah*."

And likewise in spirituality, when one encounters in the street one of Yisroel who is a "corpse" in spirituality, chas v'shalom—one must engage with him (become tamei to him) in order to bring him out of this status and situation, to act upon him in simple matters like putting on tefillin and keeping Shabbos, even though because of this he will lack in his own Avodah, that he will not study Chassidus with the proper depth, will not daven at length, and the like, just as those engaged in a *meis mitzvah* could not offer the Korban Pesach.

[And one should add a lesson and instruction regarding engaging with the "corpse" in spirituality—from the law of *eglah arufah* (in which it is said[26], "when a corpse is found, etc.") in which one goes (also) after the *near* (as it is said[27], "and it shall be the nearest city, etc.")—that one should not be impressed by the fact that he is in a status and situation of a "corpse," that he is mostly bad, but rather one must look at him as he is from the side of his *neshamah*, which is *near* to Elokus, "embraced and attached to You"[28], and therefore one can and must bring him near to Elokus[29].]

#### 53

And the truth is that in the end, nothing will be lacking from his Avodah because of the engagement in a *meis mitzvah*—for this is the general concept of Pesach *Sheni*, that even those who became tamei because of the engagement in a *meis mitzvah* will be able to offer the Korban Pesach.

—It is told about a Jew from the family of the Beis HaRav, who was not clever, and in addition was also a "shlimazel," in everything he put his hand to he did not succeed. Once, they collected a sum of money for him so he could engage in some business, and in the meantime, he met a Jew from the neighboring town who told him that he urgently needed a sum of money to settle the dowry so he could marry off his daughter, and he went and gave the entire sum for *hachnasas kallah*... In the end, the Ribbono shel Olam paid him for this, and he became a very wealthy man, among the wealthiest in all of Russia.

**11.** And one must also explain the lesson from the opinion that "those men... were the bearers of the *aron* of Yosef"23:

And to begin with, let us note the precision of the language "*aron* of Yosef"—for one is not buried in an *aron* (coffin)[30], and the language "bones of Yosef" (as the language of the verse[31]) is more appropriate—according to what is said in the Zohar[32] that "it is not necessary to enter an *aron* except for a tzaddik who knows in his soul... that he did not sin in that holy covenant from his youth and has guarded it properly, and if not, it is not necessary for him to enter an *aron* and blemish the *aron*," "the side of holiness is called the *Aron HaBris*," "in Yosef what is written[33] 'and he was placed in an *aron*... because he guarded the holy covenant... he was worthy to enter an *aron*."

And regarding our matter:

When we speak about the "aron of Yosef"—the instructions and commands of the Rebbe Rayatz, the Yosef of our generation—we must engage in carrying the *aron* of Yosef with full force ("nit opshtellen zich far kayn zach"), and even when sometimes it seems that from the side of matters of holiness, keeping the Shulchan Aruch, and the like, one should behave differently, it does not concern us, and we must engage in carrying the *aron* of Yosef.

[And to note, that it is possible that his calculation that one should behave differently is a deceitful calculation, which is the concept of "ona'ah" in Avodas Hashem—which is one of the interpretations of the matter of "yonati tamati"[34], from the word *ona'ah*[35]—that it seems to him that this matter is from the side of holiness, even though it is not according to the truth, etc.]

#### 54

For the sake of carrying the *aron* of Yosef, one must sometimes arrive late to a "maamar Chassidus" or to a "Kedusha Parade," and nevertheless there should be no falling of spirit from this ("es darf nit harn"), since one is engaged in fulfilling his shlichus and his holy command.

But, the truth is, that when one fulfills the will and shlichus of the Rebbe, one loses nothing—just as for the "bearers of the *aron* of Yosef" a special command of Pesach Sheni was given.

—When the Rebbe said the maamar "Ta'amu U'Re'u" on the 13th of Tishrei, 5693[36], several shluchim whom the Rebbe had sent to a certain place were not present, and when they returned from their shlichus, the Rebbe repeated the maamar for them again[37]. And from here we see that when one goes to fulfill the shlichus of the Rebbe, one loses nothing[38].

*

**12.** The instructions of the Rebbe Rayatz are like the *takanos* that Moshe instituted for Yisroel, such as, "Moshe instituted for Yisroel that they should inquire and expound on the matter of the day, the laws of Pesach on Pesach, etc."[39]

And to begin with, let us explain the precision of the language "Moshe *instituted* (tiken) for Yisroel," and not "commanded" and the like—for, *mitzvos*, their obligation is from the Torah, and they depend on and come from above, whereas *takanos*, their obligation is from the words of the Scribes, and they depend on and come from below, for the sake of the rectification of the lower realm, to rectify one's soul, which is why they are called by the name "*takanos*," from the word *tikkun* (rectification)[40].

#### 55

[And to note, that even in *mitzvos* there is an emphasis regarding the clarification of the lower realm, which is why their fulfillment must be specifically in the way of nature.

And based on this, one can understand the well-known story[41] with the Alter Rebbe while he was in prison, that when they were transferring him from place to place in a boat, he wanted to sanctify the moon, and when he asked the officer—who was a great wicked one—to stop the boat, and he did not agree, the boat stopped on its own, and after it continued to travel, he asked the officer again to stop the boat, and after he asked several times, the officer relented and stopped the boat, and then the Alter Rebbe sanctified the moon—seemingly: since it was in the power of the Alter Rebbe to stop the boat by himself, why did he need to ask for the favor of the officer to agree of his own will to stop the boat? And the explanation for this—as one understands through studying the teachings of Chassidus[42]—is that this is a special matter ("a gantzer inyan") in Avodah, that the fulfillment of a mitzvah must be as it is clothed in the way of nature specifically, for the sake of the clarification of the lower realm.

And this matter is emphasized more regarding *takanos*, whose entire essence is from below, for the sake of the rectification of the lower realm, as mentioned above.

—Once, one of the Chassidim came to the Rebbe to ask for advice for a rectification in a certain matter, and after the Rebbe gave him his advice, the Chassid argued that it would be difficult for him to fulfill this advice, and he wanted an easy piece of advice, similar to the story[43] that the Alter Rebbe healed an entire community with a piece of matzah shemurah and a cup of water... The Rebbe answered him: Why do "kunzen" (tricks) when one can manage without "kunzen"?! And on the contrary—according to Chassidus, the Avodah must be according to nature specifically].

And just as "Moshe instituted for Yisroel," there are also the *takanos* of the heads of the thousands of Yisroel in every generation, "the extension of Moshe in every generation"[44], whose essence is to rectify one's soul, etc. And likewise regarding the *takanos* of the Rebbe Rayatz, the extension of Moshe in our generation, such as the *takanah* of studying the *Chitas* (Chumash, Tehillim, Tanya) lessons, and the like[45].

## Sicha of the Night of Lag B’Omer, 5710

#### 56

**A.** Based on the teaching of our Sages [1] that "there is nothing that is not hinted at in the Torah," it is understood that the significance of Lag B’Omer is also hinted at in the Torah.

In the teachings of Chassidus, two hints for Lag B’Omer are brought: (1) In the verse [2] "Ad HaGal HaZeh" (This heap is a witness) [3], and (2) in the verse [4] "Gal Einai V’Abita Niflaot MiToratecha" (Uncover my eyes that I may behold wonders from Your Torah) [5] — where "Gal" (uncover/heap) shares the letters of "Lamed-Gimel" (Lag, 33) [B’Omer].

It can be said that this also hints at the great necessity of studying and disseminating the teachings of Chassidus (the essence of Lag B’Omer, the giving of the Torah of the *pnimiyus haTorah* [6]) specifically in these days, as will be explained.

**B.** By way of introduction:

"Ad HaGal HaZeh" was said when Lavan caught up with Yaakov as he pursued him. At that time, "they took stones and made a heap... and Lavan called it Yegar Sahaduta, and Yaakov called it Gal-Ed... This heap is a witness... if I do not pass over to you this heap, and if you do not pass over to me this heap... for evil" [7].

Regarding Lavan’s pursuit of Yaakov, it is stated in the *sefarim* [8] that the true reason was [not as Lavan imagined, that he was pursuing Yaakov to harm him, Heaven forbid, but] because at the conclusion of Yaakov’s work in Charan, there remained with Lavan sparks of holiness (*nitzotzei kedushah*) that had not yet been refined by Yaakov. Therefore, Lavan pursued Yaakov to give him the *final sparks of holiness* that remained with him, so that the refinement and elevation of the sparks of holiness would be completed.

The parallel in our days—the *ikvesa d’Meshicha*—is as the Rebbe Rayatz [9] said, "Behold, he stands behind our wall" [10]. After the work of refining the sparks of holiness in all the exiles up to this final exile, we must refine the *very last sparks* (similar to the refinement of the final sparks at the time of the departure from Charan). Then the prophecy will be fulfilled [11], "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the land," with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

**C.** Since we are at the end of the exile and are refining the very last sparks, the great necessity for the revelation and dissemination of *pnimiyus haTorah* is understood:

In previous generations, they could postpone ("*oplegen*") the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* with the claim that it was a study belonging only to *tzaddikim*, those of high standing, etc.—even though this was not a true claim even then. But in these days, as we emerge from exile (Charan) toward the redemption, and we must complete the very last sparks, the dissemination of *pnimiyus haTorah* must be done in a way that even simple people engage in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*.

This is emphasized by the work of the Rebbe Rayatz in disseminating the teachings of Chassidus in the recent period:

The Baal Shem Tov and the Maggid acted and revealed the general relevance of *pnimiyus haTorah* to all Bnei Yisrael. The Alter Rebbe acted and revealed that even the *grasping* of *pnimiyus haTorah* belongs to all Bnei Yisrael (unlike the prevailing view until then that "the *tzaddik* shall live by his faith" [12]—not *yichyeh* (shall live), but *yechayeh* (shall give life) [13]). And the Rebbe Rayatz acted and revealed that even those of the *lowest capacity for comprehension* belong to the study of the teachings of Chassidus. Therefore, in the recent period, the Rebbe Rayatz printed *maamarim* of Chassidus even in *Yiddish*, for those of the lowest capacity for comprehension [14].

The reason for this is that in these days we must complete the very last sparks and bring about the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, and therefore we must increase the revelation and dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus, through which "the Master, this King Mashiach, will come" [15].

**D.** We should add an explanation regarding the connection and relevance of *pnimiyus haTorah* to the matter of the "Gal" (heap) [16]:

Even though for the work of *birurim* (refinements), and especially the refinement of the lowest sparks, the refiner (Yaakov) must descend and clothe himself in the garments of the one being refined (Lavan), nevertheless, there must be a separation and partition between them to prevent the undesirable influence of the one being refined upon the refiner—and this is the concept of the "Gal": "I will not pass over to you... (and) you will not pass over to me... for evil" [18].

There is a need to engage in the affairs of the world—eating, drinking, and the like—to refine the body, the *nefesh habehamis*, and one’s portion in the world. However, at the time of the act, it must be in a manner of separation from the materiality of the world, to know that aside from the work of *birurim*, there is no connection between them. Through this, one does not receive influence from the world; rather, on the contrary, one makes the world a vessel for *Elokus*, as hinted in the language of the verse [19], "And G-d saved the livestock of your father and gave it to me."

The power to create the "Gal" is (especially) through *pnimiyus haTorah*, because through the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* one arrives at the understanding and recognition that "there is nothing else besides Him" [20], that the entire reality of the world is *Elokus*. Through this, one acts so that the world becomes a vessel for *Elokus*, up to the perfection that will be revealed with the coming of Mashiach (through the study and dissemination of *pnimiyus haTorah*), as it is written [21], "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh together shall see that the mouth of Hashem has spoken."

**E.** And another matter regarding the "Gal"—in connection and relevance to the day of Lag B’Omer:

A "Gal" is made of stones, as it is written, "They took stones and made a heap." Its meaning in *avodah*—as is known [22]—is that "stones" (*avanim*) refers to letters (*osiyos*), where the main emphasis is not on understanding and comprehension, but on the strength (*tokef*) of *kabbalas ol*. In the present case, the "Gal" that separates between holiness and the affairs of the world is made of stones, meaning, not through understanding and comprehension, but specifically through *kabbalas ol*.

And this is the connection of the "Gal" to the day of Lag B’Omer—because the essence of Lag B’Omer is in the *sefirah* of *Hod*, and in *Hod* itself, *Hod sheb'Hod*, which is not in a manner of understanding and comprehension, but in a manner of *hoda'ah* (acknowledgment/submission) [23], which is the concept of *kabbalas ol* [24].

*

**F.** In a *sicha* of Lag B’Omer 5701 [25], the Rebbe Rayatz says that Lag B’Omer is in the *sefirah* of *Tiferes*, *Tiferes sheb'Tiferes*—according to the order of the *sefirah* counting from below to above: *Malchus sheb'Malchus*, *Yesod sheb'Malchus*, and so on. According to this, Lag B’Omer is *Tiferes sheb'Tiferes* [26].

The meaning of the two orders in the *sefirah* counting in *avodah* is: From above to below—from the perspective of revelations—is the *avodah* that is according to intellect and reason, through understanding, comprehension, and *taanug* (*geshmak*). And from below to above—is the concept of *kabbalas ol*, where the *avodah* is not from the perspective of understanding, comprehension, and *taanug*, but from the perspective of *kabbalas ol* alone.

The explanation for the two matters in Lag B’Omer, *Hod sheb'Hod* (according to the order of above to below) and *Tiferes sheb'Tiferes* (according to the order of below to above), is that when the *avodah* is in a manner of *hoda'ah* from *kabbalas ol* alone (*Hod sheb'Hod*), through this specifically one arrives at the ultimate refinement and beauty (*Tiferes sheb'Tiferes*).

**G.** From this we also learn regarding the connection to the Rebbe:

The matters and powers that the Rebbe gives us ("everyone who gives, gives with a generous eye" [27]) are the perfection of beauty, "*Tiferes sheb'Tiferes*." However, in order to receive from the Rebbe, there is a need for the prerequisite of dedication and giving to the Rebbe through *kabbalas ol*, "*Hod sheb'Hod*."

The Rebbe gives with a generous eye even to those who are not worthy, but it is impossible to make demands of the Rebbe while doing nothing oneself ("not dipping a finger in cold water"). One must begin the *avodah* with one’s own strength through *kabbalas ol*, and then the Rebbe gives according to his (the Rebbe’s) powers, not according to the value of the *avodah* at all.

At the time of the Exodus from Egypt, there was an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) on its own, without the need for a prerequisite of *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below). But at the Giving of the Torah, the order was established that all matters must come specifically through *avodah*, and afterward, they give from above not according to the value of the *avodah*.

This is similar to what is told in the *Midrashim* of Chazal [28], that when Rabbi Chanina ben Dosa asked the angels to lift a large stone to Jerusalem for him, they said to him: "On the condition that you place your hand and finger with us." He placed his hand and finger with them, and they were found standing in Jerusalem.

And likewise in the present case: We must dedicate ourselves to the Rebbe through *kabbalas ol* that is above intellect and reason, "*Hod sheb'Hod*," and when the Rebbe sees the effort, dedication, and giving, etc., then he gives according to his powers, "*Tiferes sheb'Tiferes*."

*

**H.** It is known [29] that the Mitteler Rebbe would go out to the field on Lag B’Omer, and they would see many miracles then regarding barren women who, through his blessing, were blessed with male Chassidic children.

[At other times when they would come to him to ask for a blessing for children, he would send them to his brother, R. Chaim Avraham [30], and R. Chaim Avraham would put on his hat (or *streimel*), etc. This was not the case on Lag B’Omer; when he went out to the field, he would personally receive the requests and bless them with male Chassidic children [31].]

The explanation for this can be said:

The going out to the field—this should be explained according to the parable of the "King in the field" brought in the *drushei Chassidus* [32] regarding the month of Elul. When the King is in the field, "anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted, and he receives everyone with a pleasant countenance," unlike when he is in his royal palace, "they do not enter except with permission, and even then, only the chosen of the people and the select few."

The difference between them is that in his royal palace, the revelation is *more elevated*, because he is revealed as he is in all his internal matters. In the field, the revelation is *for everyone*, so that everyone can greet him and see him. And this is the very reason: because he is not revealed in all his internal matters as he is in his royal palace, but rather *descends from his level* and goes out to the field, therefore the revelation can be for everyone.

This is the reason the parable of the "King in the field" is said regarding the month of Elul—because then the revelation is for everyone [33].

Based on this, the content of the Mitteler Rebbe’s going out to the field on Lag B’Omer can be explained:

Regarding the "Gal" of Lag B’Omer—the partition at the end of the boundary of holiness to separate against the *chitzonim*—the relevance to the "field," the place of the *chitzonim*, is emphasized: "Esav... a man of the field" [34]. This is the concept of going out to the field on Lag B’Omer—which indicates the descent to the lowest level in holiness, where there is a need for a "Gal" (Lag B’Omer) to separate against the *chitzonim*.

This is the reason that while in the field he would show miracles, which is not his primary matter; rather, on the contrary, this is a descent from his level [35]—like the parable of the King who, while in the field, is not revealed in all his internal matters.

The intention of the descent in his going out to the field is so that through this, male Chassidic children will be born.

**I.** This matter—going out to the field to produce male Chassidic children—is also emphasized by the Rebbe Rayatz upon his arrival in America:

By way of introduction to the explanation of what is written [36], "And he descended to Egypt, compelled by the word," seemingly, since Yaakov knew that this descent was "by the word," he certainly wanted to fulfill the word and was not "compelled"—for the desire is from the perspective of the higher intention within the word. But regarding the descent itself, it is in a manner of being "compelled."

And likewise regarding the descent of the Rebbe Rayatz upon his arrival in America—that from the perspective of the greatness of the descent of the lower hemisphere compared to the upper hemisphere regarding the Giving of the Torah [37], it is in a manner of being "compelled." However, such was the higher intention, "by the word," as he said [38] that his coming here is for the work of spreading Torah, etc.

In the style mentioned—that his coming here is a going out to the field to produce male Chassidic children:

Going out *to the field*—not just a departure from the King’s palace to the capital city, or to a city in general, but specifically going out to the field—from the perspective of the greatness of the descent of the lower hemisphere.

(And the intention in this is) for *male* children—who will conquer the world, as the saying goes [39], "It is the way of a man to conquer," and *Chassidic*—who do not demand that they be given 310 worlds... but go with *mesiras nefesh*, as the saying goes [40], "A *chassid* burns them, a *tzaddik* buries them." A "*chassid*" puts himself in danger of harm resulting from burning his fingernail clippings to prevent a suspected danger to a pregnant woman who might walk over the clippings (even though his own harm from burning the clippings is closer than the suspected danger to a pregnant woman if the clippings were exposed and taken from their place of burial), because he does not think of himself, and does everything for the benefit of the other [41].

**J.** And in such a manner must also be the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s mission—"And he descended to Egypt, compelled by the word":

It is difficult, indeed, to go out to some city in order to conquer it.

How can one—he argues—go out to such a town where he will not even have anyone to speak with about the Rebbe... since not one of the people there has any concept of such matters, and consequently, it is a very great descent.

And nevertheless, knowing that this is the mission of the Rebbe, "by the word," one must put oneself aside and fulfill the mission, "and he descended to Egypt."

And *kal v'chomer*: For the Rebbe himself, this was a much greater descent, not according to the value at all, and nevertheless, "and he descended to Egypt,"

—including the fact that the Rebbe engaged with him... and not only that, but even at a time when the Rebbe had pain from him, he showed him a smiling face... The Rebbe told me—at the end of the last summer, when speaking about matters of *yechidus*—that it costs him his health ("*es nemt gezunt*"), but it is not noticeable... —

All the more so *for him* (the *shaliach*), that from the perspective of his level, it is not such a great descent... — certainly, he must fulfill the mission of "and he descended to Egypt."

The Rebbe did not look for easy things for himself, and he does not look for easy things for us either. He himself went through all the matters with *mesiras nefesh* [42], and he demands *mesiras nefesh* from us as well.

And therefore, everyone must put himself aside and engage in fulfilling the mission for the benefit of the other [43].

**K.** The truth is that by putting aside one’s own self to fulfill the mission of the Rebbe to engage in the benefit of the other, one also gains regarding his work with himself.

The explanation for this:

When one works at his *avodah* with his own strength—he is not sure that he will succeed and hit the truth. He can delve into a *maamar Chassidus* for several hours and not grasp the truth of the matter. But when one engages in the mission of the Rebbe—he will certainly arrive at the truth, since he is not going with his own strength, but with the strength of the Rebbe.

We do not know the extent of it: A Jew who for many years did not put on *tefillin*, when he saw the Rebbe at the time of eating the *kezayis* of *matzah*, faith was planted and established in his heart!

And likewise in the present case: It is possible that the study of Chassidus is not having its effect, and suddenly, when he begins to fulfill the mission of the Rebbe, all matters are activated within him, since he is not going with his own strength, but with the strength of the Rebbe.

And all this—aside from the greatness of the elevation in engaging in the benefit of the other, like the well-known story with the Tzemach Tzedek, who tried for a long time to see our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe after his passing, and did not succeed. When he gave money to a Jew as a *gemach* (loan), he merited to see our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe and hear several matters from him [44].

*

**L.** Continuing from what was said above regarding the descent in going out to the field to produce male Chassidic children—one should bring a sort of example for this in connection to *Maseches Sotah*, which it is customary [45] to study during the days of the *Sefirah*, a page a day:

It is stated in the *Gemara* [46] that "Chana said before the Holy One, blessed be He, 'Master of the Universe, if You see, good, and if not, You will see. I will go and seclude myself before Elkanah my husband, and since I will be secluded, they will make me drink the *sotah* waters, and You will not make Your Torah a lie, as it is said [47], "And she shall be clean and shall conceive seed."'"

It is found, then, that there is a way to merit children ("and shall conceive seed") through a matter of descent ("I will go and seclude myself"), and the parallel in the present case is the descent to go out to the field so that male Chassidic children will be born.

And more deeply:

Chana’s seclusion ("I will go and seclude myself")—since it is not from the perspective of a lack of modesty, Heaven forbid, it is not a descent, but rather a part of the order of *avodah* which is in a manner of a descent for the sake of an ascent.

Similar to what we find regarding R. Zeira, who fasted one hundred fasts to forget the *Talmud Bavli* so that he could study the *Talmud Yerushalmi* [48]. The forgetting of the *Talmud Bavli* is not a descent, but rather such is the order of *avodah* that before the ascent to a more elevated level (*Talmud Yerushalmi*), there must be a nullification of the previous level (*Talmud Bavli*) [49], as explained regarding the matter of "A *tzaddik* falls seven times and rises" [50], that "between one level and another, before he reaches a level higher than it, he is in a state of falling from his first level, etc." [51].

Based on this, one can explain the conduct of the Rebbe Rayatz to make a mark in his *Siddur* after the *Sefirah* of every night [52]. Even though he certainly did not need to seek advice to rule out a fear of forgetting—a matter that belongs to simple people, but not to the Rebbe—it is certainly not a matter of descent, Heaven forbid, but rather an order in the *avodah* of a *tzaddik* who strives that even from the perspective of a lower level, a state of forgetting should not be possible.

*

**M.** Continuing from what was discussed above regarding the fulfillment of the mission of the Rebbe—there is a lesson and instruction from the general matter of *Sefiras HaOmer* [53]:

*Sefiras HaOmer* has no *tashlumin* (make-up); if one forgot and did not count all day, he cannot count the next day with a blessing [54]. Unlike the festival of *Shavuos*—it has *tashlumin* for all seven days; if one did not offer the sacrifices on the festival of *Shavuos*, he can offer them during the days of *tashlumin* [55].

The reason for the difference—simply—is because the obligation of the sacrifices on the festival of *Shavuos* is not for seven days, but for one day only. If they did not offer them on this day, they can complete them during the days of *tashlumin*, which in themselves do not have an obligation, except as *tashlumin*. Unlike *Sefiras HaOmer*, where the obligation is for all 49 days; it is not possible that a certain day would be *tashlumin* for the day before it, since this day itself is obligated in *Sefiras HaOmer*.

Similar to the *mitzvah* of Torah study, which has no *tashlumin*—since the obligation of Torah study is every day and every moment, his study is from the perspective of the *obligation* of this day and this moment (and it is sufficient that he exempts himself), and not as *tashlumin* for the day and moment before it.

From this it is also understood that there is no *tashlumin* for the spiritual *avodah* of *Sefiras HaOmer*, the refinement of the *middos*, that one cannot complete the deficiency of the *avodah* of this day through the perfection of his *avodah* tomorrow—because the order of *avodah* is in a manner that from day to day there must be an addition in elevation after elevation. As the saying of [56] the Chassid R. Gershon Dov [57], who was accustomed to say every night: "*Morgen darf men oifshteyn gor an anderer*" (Tomorrow one must wake up completely different). And since if he had done his *avodah* on this day, his *avodah* tomorrow would have been in a more elevated manner, he cannot complete the deficiency of the ascent that could have been his through his *avodah* on this day.

And likewise regarding the mission of the Rebbe—that the fulfillment of this mission is a duty incumbent upon everyone at all times, and when one misses one day of fulfilling the duty, he cannot complete this duty at another time, which in itself has the duty of fulfilling the mission.

**N.** And another lesson from *Sefiras HaOmer*—regarding the *manner* of fulfilling the mission of the Rebbe:

The obligation of *Sefiras HaOmer* is not like the counting of *Shemitin* and *Yovelos* which is done by the *Beis Din*, but an obligation on every individual of Israel as a detail—"that there should be a counting for each and every one" [58]. However, the counting itself can be in two ways: (a) everyone counts the days that have passed in his own counting, (b) everyone counts the days that have passed from the offering of the *Omer* by the *Beis Din*.

And there is a practical difference—regarding one who crosses the dateline during the days of the *Sefirah*, that because of the change of days, his counting changes from the counting of the Bnei Yisrael living in that place (as one asked me regarding Australia) [59].

And one can explain the content of the matter in spiritual *avodah*:

The parallel to the difference between the offering of the *Omer* for all of Israel by the *Beis Din* and the *Sefiras HaOmer* by each and every one—is the difference between the action for all of Israel that is done by the Rebbe, a general soul that includes the entire generation, which is like the offering of the *Omer* by the *Beis Din*, and the action for the benefit of the other that is done by each and every one who fulfills his mission of the Rebbe, which is like the counting of each and every one, his own calculation in fulfilling the mission.

And the parallel to the two ways of counting (counting the days that have passed for him, or counting the days that have passed from the offering of the *Omer* by the *Beis Din*) are two ways in the calculation (counting) of fulfilling the mission of the Rebbe:

There is a way that everyone makes his own private calculation—what he has accomplished in Torah and *avodah*, regarding himself and regarding the other.

And there is a way that everyone makes a calculation that relates to the *Nasi* of the generation (like the counting for the offering of the *Omer* by the *Beis Din*)—to what extent he is fulfilling the mission of the Rebbe. That is to say, his own standing and situation, "*vos tut zich mit zein neshamah*" (what is happening with his soul), does not concern him, but rather, the fulfillment of his mission of the Rebbe. And furthermore: in the fulfillment of the mission of the Rebbe itself, the degree of his success does not concern him, but rather, the very fact that he must fulfill his mission of the Rebbe.

And the lesson from this—that one should not make personal calculations ("*eigene cheshbonos*"), but rather, dedicate oneself completely to the Rebbe, and then all matters are done with the strength of the Rebbe (as mentioned above in section K).

*

**O.** What was said above that through dedication to the Rebbe all matters are done with the strength of the Rebbe is in force even after the passing—as the Rebbe promised [60] that the leaders of Israel "will not separate from their flock," and furthermore, "*Tzaddika d'itpatar ishtachach b'cholei almin yatir mib'chayei*" (A *tzaddik* who has passed is found in all worlds more than in his lifetime) [61].

—On Lag B’Omer 5692, I was in Riga for the engagement of my sister-in-law, the Rabbanit Sheina. The Rebbe said then a *maamar* on the verse "A Song of Ascents, behold how good and how pleasant." For the festival of *Shavuos*, the Rebbe traveled to Landaurow, where the wedding took place. At that time, the Rebbe was not satisfied with the state of his health, and he related [62] that his father, the Rebbe Rashab, told him: Why are you broken in spirit ("*vos bistu azoi tzubrachen*")—regarding the state of health and the like—it is written [63] "When the living creatures were lifted... the wheels were lifted." When there will be "the lifting of the living creatures," spirituality, then automatically "the wheels will be lifted," physicality.

And likewise in the present case: When one dedicates himself to the Rebbe and fulfills his mission, which is the concept of "the lifting of the living creatures," then automatically "the wheels will be lifted," that abundant influence is drawn also in physicality, and especially regarding the physical matters connected with the mission, the maintenance of the institutions, and the like.

**P.** Regarding this matter, there is also a lesson from the conduct of the Rebbe:

In the *Reshimas HaMaasar* (from the year 5687) [64], the Rebbe tells about his thoughts regarding his family members that caused him low spirits, and he concludes: "Stop thinking—it flashed in my mind—and like a flash of lightning it shone in my thoughts... After all, everything is from G-d... They depend on me and I depend on Him who spoke and the world came into being... And in this moment... I ascended to the heights of heaven in lofty thoughts... and in the merit of the holy ancestors..." (letters of thought). And likewise in the continuation of the *reshima* [65]: "I am not permitted to think such thoughts that cause low spirits... The place and the time demand... courage of heart and elevation of spirit... through contemplation... in the image of the face of the Holy of Holies, the splendor of my father, the Rebbe, *ztzvkllh"h*..." (letters of thought)... "*Abba, Abba Kadisha*..."

The Rebbe gives advice—that when one sits in "prison," in a state of low spirits, etc., then the advice is to connect to the Rebbe through visualizing his holy face.

From time to time, everyone must visualize the holy face of the Rebbe, and remember the things he heard from the Rebbe. — Even those who did not see the Rebbe can visualize his holy face through a picture, and learn from his teachings.

We must know that we have an "*Abba Kadisha*"... and consequently, there is nothing to worry about!

And through this, there will be even more addition in receiving the influences from the Rebbe—in accordance with his promise that the shepherds of Israel "will not separate from their flock"—in everything that is needed, both in spirituality and in physicality, with children, life, and abundant sustenance.

**Q.** And in this, there is also an addition through going and prostrating oneself at the *Ohel* [66]—

where the place that the lowest part of the person is found (and in the present case, the body that is buried in the dust) is where the connection with the level of *Yechidah* in the soul is made.

In the text of the prayers that one says at the time of going to the *Ohel*—as printed in *Maaneh Lashon*—we say: "In the merit of the *Tannaim* and *Amoraim*... whose dwelling is firm, and in the merit of the *tzaddikim* buried in this place." And from this it is implied that at the *tziyun* of a *tzaddik*, other *tzaddikim* are also found, *Tannaim* and *Amoraim*, etc., including and especially (in connection to Lag B’Omer) the Rashbi.

And therefore, I suggest that tomorrow, on the day of Lag B’Omer, the day of the *hillula* of the Rashbi—a day of his joy, the greatest joy [67], like the joy of a wedding, a *hillula* (unlike the day of the passing of Moshe Rabbeinu, which some observe) [68]—everyone should travel to the *Ohel*, where the Rashbi is also found.

(The Rebbe *shlita* concluded with a blessing) [69].

## B"H

#### 69

On this day last year—or, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, "On the sixth day, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday, of the week of *Ki Savo el Ha'aretz... v'shavtah ha'aretz Shabbos la'Havayah"*—the Rebbe wrote[1](#_ftn315) to Anash and the *talmidei hatmimim* settling in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. After informing them that "I have instructed the administration of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch to send you a Sefer Torah," he wrote that the receipt of the Sefer Torah should serve as:

"A sign of constant remembrance in your minds and hearts, to order all your private and communal lives according to the Torah, as taught to us by our holy forefathers and Rebbes, of blessed memory. To educate your sons and daughters—may they live—in its path, without any compromises, and to emanate its spirit—the spirit of the Israel of old—onto the rest of your brethren, the children of Yisrael—may they live—both those who are near and those who are currently far, by influencing them to guide them on the path that ascends to the House of Hashem. This is the path of Torah study with *yiras shamayim* and the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. [All this] through a genuine *kiruv* that stems from *ahavas Yisrael* and the *midos* of Chassidus, which are according to the Torah of the words of the living G-d.

And may each and every one of you be a lamp to illuminate the darkness of the *galus* in which you and we find ourselves, with the light of Hashem, until Hashem fulfills His promise through His holy prophets to let us hear the voice of the messenger announcing salvation: 'For Hashem has comforted His people,' and 'Hashem goes before us' to gather our exiles and redeem us with an eternal redemption."

Now, every single day we receive the Torah, and every single day we bless "Giver of the Torah," for He gives it to us every day[2](#_ftn316). This is true with even greater intensity on the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah for the entire year.

On this festival, and in the days preceding and following it, we must contemplate the words of the Rebbe quoted above with greater depth—a contemplation that leads to positive action throughout the entire year in all the matters enumerated and detailed in his letter.

#### 70

And may the voice of the call of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory[3](#_ftn317)—which emerges from the depths of his soul—always be heard in our ears, our minds, and our hearts: *What are we waiting for? We are delaying the Geulah! It is already Erev Shabbos after midday!*

**Menachem Schneerson**

*The sixth day, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday, of the week of Ki Savo el Ha'aretz... v'shavtah ha'aretz Shabbos la'Havayah, the year 5711,*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Behar-Bechukosai, Mevarchim HaChodesh Sivan, 5730

#### 71

**A.** In this week’s parsha, the prohibition against giving (and taking) *ribis* (interest) is stated, and it concludes, "I am Hashem your G-d, Who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim... to be a G-d unto you." The *Sifra* states: "From here they said: Whoever accepts upon himself the yoke of *ribis* accepts upon himself the yoke of Heaven, and whoever casts off the yoke of *ribis* casts off the yoke of Heaven... for whoever acknowledges the mitzvah of *ribis* acknowledges the Exodus from Mitzrayim, and whoever denies the mitzvah of *ribis* is as if he denies the Exodus from Mitzrayim."

We must understand what the special connection is between the mitzvah of *ribis* (more so than other mitzvos) and the Exodus from Mitzrayim and the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven.

Regarding the connection of *ribis* to the Exodus from Mitzrayim, Rashi explains (based on the *Gemara*): "'I am Hashem your G-d, Who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim'—'I distinguished between the firstborn and one who is not a firstborn; so too, I know and will exact retribution from one who lends money to a Jew with *ribis* and says, "It belongs to a non-Jew."'"

However, this explanation only accounts for the connection of *ribis* to the Exodus from Mitzrayim in the specific case where one lends with *ribis* and claims, "It belongs to a non-Jew." Even then, it does not apply if the reason he says this is because he fears that if the borrower knew the money belonged to a Jew, he would not want to borrow, or that the *Beis Din* would not permit the loan. It is only when he thinks that Hashem does not distinguish—*chas v'shalom*—that the money is his, that this constitutes a denial of the Exodus from Mitzrayim, in which Hashem did distinguish, etc. Yet, this still does not explain the connection of the *general* mitzvah of *ribis* to the Exodus from Mitzrayim.

Furthermore, we must understand the connection of *ribis* to the yoke of Heaven.

There are commentators who suggest that when one lends money to another Jew without *ribis*, not thinking about profit, he thereby reveals his *bitachon* (trust) in Hashem and his acceptance of the yoke of Heaven—the command to assist a Jew without taking profit. Conversely, one who lends with *ribis* reveals that he does not trust in Hashem, and that he is casting off the yoke of Heaven.

#### 72

However, this explanation is difficult to understand:

1) The matter is not related to the "yoke of Heaven," but rather to the *middah* of *bitachon*.

2) A lack of *bitachon* is not connected to the matter of *ribis*, but rather to *gemilus chasadim*. Before the verses regarding the mitzvah of *ribis*, it is stated in the parsha: "If your brother becomes poor... then you shall support him," meaning one must lend to him without taking profit. When someone does not want to lend money without taking profit, out of concern for his livelihood, and prefers to trade (and profit) with all his money—every penny he has—he is indeed revealing that he lacks the *middah* of *bitachon*, yet he is not transgressing the prohibition of *ribis* (since he did not lend at all).

**B.** The content of accepting the yoke of Heaven—which finds expression in the fulfillment of mitzvos—is the participation from Above in the *avodah* of the Jewish people.

It is well known that the interpretation of the blessing on the mitzvos (which we recite before performing them) is: "*Asher kidshanu b'mitzvosav*—Who has sanctified us with *His* mitzvos," for even Hashem fulfills the mitzvos. There are two aspects to this: (a) The fulfillment of mitzvos Above that *precedes* the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Jewish people, as the Sages say, "What He does, He tells the Jewish people to do," and (b) the fulfillment of mitzvos Above that is *brought about* by the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Jewish people, as the Sages say, "Whoever reads the Torah, Hashem reads and studies along with him," and this applies to mitzvos just as it does to Torah.

It is understood that the fact that the fulfillment of mitzvos Above is brought about by the mitzvos of the Jewish people is not because there is any equivalence between them, for a created being has no value relative to the Creator; rather, it is because it arose in His will, may He be blessed, that the mitzvos performed by the Jewish people should, as it were, effectuate something Above.

We must understand: What is the reason for this will, that the *avodah* of the Jewish people below should influence, as it were, Above, despite the infinite distance?

The matter of the fulfillment of mitzvos Above that *precedes* the *avodah* of the Jewish people below is understood: by "what He does," He gives the power "to the Jewish people to do"—the giving of power for the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Jewish people. But what is the explanation for why the actions of the Jewish people should cause the same to be done Above?

#### 73

**C.** To understand this, we must first preface an explanation of the general matter of *avodah*:

On the face of it: Why must there be a system where the *avodah* of the Jewish people is required? Hashem could give all the *hashpaos* (influences) from Above, by way of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from Above). Especially according to what is known, that the intent of creation was "to bestow good upon His creations," for Hashem is the ultimate good and "it is the nature of the Good to bestow good"—and from the perspective of "bestowing good," all creations (and certainly the Jewish people, who are the essence and purpose of creation, for the sake of the Jewish people and the Torah, which are called the beginning) should receive all *hashpaos* even without *avodah*?

The explanation for this is: When is an influence truly "good"? When it is given to the recipient as a reward ("earned"), and not for free. When a person is given a free gift without his own effort, it is called "*nahama d'chisufa*" (bread of shame). And since "it is the nature of the Good to bestow good," Hashem desires to give the Jewish people the true good, and therefore He established that they should receive the *hashpaos* only through *avodah*.

With this, we can understand the reason why the *avodah* of the Jewish people effectuates something, as it were, Above:

When a person receives a reward (an influence) for a certain *avodah* (not as a free gift), but this *avodah* brings no benefit to the payer (the *mashpia*), this reward is still categorized as "*nahama d'chisufa*," because the recipient knows that the *avodah* for which he was given the bounty holds no benefit, and consequently, he is not entitled to any reward for it.

Therefore, the system was established from Above that the *avodah* of the Jewish people should effectuate something Above (the same mitzvos performed below) so that the reward would not be categorized as "*nahama d'chisufa*" at all: their *avodah* is beneficial Above—they are worthy of receiving a reward in exchange for the *avodah*.

**D.** And another reason:

*Avodah* that in and of itself brings no benefit—even when one receives

#### 74

a reward for it—lacks all vitality and sweetness, and therefore it is very difficult to perform the *avodah*, and it is very exhausting—backbreaking labor.

[The Rebbe Rayatz explained this with a parable: A nobleman hired a farmer and commanded him to "work" with a scythe, moving it back and forth in the nobleman's room just as he does in his work in the field, and he promised him a wage for the "work." At first, the farmer agreed, but after working for a short time, he regretted it, arguing: "*Rabotu nie vidot*"—the work is not visible (it yields no results).]

Therefore, it was established from Above that the *avodah* of a Jew is beneficial Above, and the knowledge of this gives "vitality" and sweetness to the *avodah*. Furthermore, this knowledge gives the strength to stand against the *yetzer hara*, which argues: "What does it matter to Hashem if you put on *tefillin* or not—*chas v'shalom*—if you daven at length, and the like?"—because he has the feeling that the *avodah* touches upon His very Essence and Being, as it were.

**E.** Since all the *hemshechos* (drawings down) from Above come through the *avodah* of the Jewish people, just as it is regarding the specific *hemshech* of each individual mitzvah—that the mitzvah Above is performed by the very mitzvah that the Jewish people perform—so too is it regarding the general essence of the matter: in order for the *avodah* of the Jewish people to influence Above, there must be a specific *avodah*. And this *avodah* is the mitzvah of *ribis*.

*Ribis* means: receiving profit for money given as a loan, that is, receiving a reward for the fact that *in the past* the money was his (even though now the money has already left his possession and entered the possession of the borrower), and by lending it in the past, he (the lender) then gave the borrower the possibility to trade with it.

And caution regarding *ribis* means: receiving profit only from what belongs to him *now* (which is the content of "*heter iska*": part of the money remains the lender's, but he gives it to the borrower only *as a deposit*, and he receives profit only from the portion that belongs to him *even now*. And similarly—renting an animal or tools).

Just as a Jew conducts himself with a second Jew, so too do they conduct themselves with him from Above: if he transgresses the prohibition of *ribis*, taking profit now because he gave money *in the past*, they conduct themselves with him from Above in such a way: his *avodah* now is, as it were, without

#### 75

participation from Above; there is only the giving of the "money"—the power—the fulfillment of mitzvos Above—*before* he begins the "commerce," the engagement in his *avodah*, which is the *power* to perform his *avodah*. But when he fulfills the mitzvah of *ribis*, they conduct themselves with him in this way from Above as well: not only do they give him *the power* for his *avodah* at the outset, but they participate with him from Above in the *avodah* itself—"Hashem reads and studies *along with him*."

And this is the connection of the mitzvah of *ribis* to the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven and the Exodus from Mitzrayim: the mitzvah of *ribis* constitutes a general content (and system) through which Hashem becomes, as it were, a partner to the Jew in his *avodah*—the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven (the fulfillment of mitzvos). And by being connected with Hashem, he goes out from all the constraints and limitations—the Exodus from Mitzrayim.

**F.** "The *tzaddikim* are like their Creator":

Just as it is the way of Hashem not only to give the power for the *avodah* of Torah and mitzvos at the outset, but also afterward, when the Jewish people fulfill mitzvos in practice, He fulfills those same mitzvos, so too is the conduct of *tzaddikim*, and especially the *Nesi'im* of the Jewish people—who are the intermediary *connecting* the Jewish people with Hashem—that not only do they give power to their *shluchim* to carry out their mission, but they themselves also perform the same *avodah* that they assigned to their *shluchim*.

#### 76

Such conduct was seen openly, especially with the Rebbe Rayatz: not only did he send *shluchim* and give them the power to act in strengthening Yiddishkeit in general and the dissemination of the *maayanos* in particular, but he also always (not only in the early years, but also in the later years, after he had raised students and students of students, *who* were capable of performing the *avodah*) dedicated himself to this *avodah*.

This serves as a lesson to all who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps: they should not be satisfied with the fact that they have raised students who are already engaged in spreading Torah and disseminating the *maayanos*, calculating that since the *avodah* of their students stems from their own influence, they too, the *mashpi'im*, will receive the additional light drawn down by the *avodah* of the students, and therefore they do not need to engage with others now, but rather engage in Torah for themselves. Such conduct—receiving "profit" (additional light) in exchange for *avodah* of the *past*—is (in a subtle way) a matter of *ribis*. They must always engage not only with themselves, but also with others: to perform the same *avodah* that is required of their students.

And the reward for the conduct of caution regarding *ribis* is that even in their own *avodah*, they will merit the participation of the Rebbe Rayatz, the *Nasi* of our generation, and through him—since he stands between Hashem and you—the participation of Hashem, the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven, through which they will experience the matter of the Exodus from Mitzrayim, that they will go out from all their constraints and limitations.

***

**G.** At the conclusion of the parsha, it is said: "He shall not inquire between good and bad, and he shall not exchange it; and if he does exchange it, then it and its substitute shall be holy."

The Rambam explains: "It seems to me that what the verse says, 'then it and its substitute shall be holy'... the Torah descended to the depths of human thought and the nature of the *yetzer hara*, for the nature of man tends to increase his possessions and spare his money, and even though he vowed and sanctified [an animal], it is possible that he regretted it and would redeem it for less than its value... and if you were to give him permission to exchange bad for good, he would exchange good for bad and say it is good; therefore, the verse closed the door before him so that he would not exchange, and penalized him if he did exchange, saying, 'then it and its substitute shall be holy.'"

That is to say: even though from the strict letter of the law it should have been permitted to exchange "bad for good,"

#### 77

nevertheless, since "the Torah descended to the depths of human thought, etc.," that "if you were to give him permission to exchange bad for good, he would exchange good for bad and say it is good," the Torah decreed and forbade exchanging (even) "bad for good."

From here there is proof to decide the debate regarding the definition of a "decree" (to forbid something that is in itself permitted because of something else)—that this is not (only) an addition by the Sages, but even in the Torah itself there are prohibitions that are in the category of a decree, as in the present case, where the prohibition to exchange bad for good is a *decree* so that he will not exchange good for bad and say it is good.

**H.** And the explanation of the matter in *avodah*:

Sometimes one can make a calculation that it is better to engage in a different *avodah*, because it is "better" than the one he is being asked to engage in, and therefore—he argues—he wishes to exchange the bad for the good.

For example: when one is asked to engage in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, someone might argue that anyone can engage in such simple matters, while he should engage in more lofty matters, such as the study of *Chassidus*, and the like. And similarly, conversely, when one is asked to engage in the study of *Chassidus*, someone might argue that he is not worthy of it, he himself does not understand it so well, and consequently, it is better that he engage in other matters of *avodah*.

That is to say, the argument is that he wants the sacrifice—the general *avodah* of drawing close to Hashem—to be "better," an *avodah* that is more lofty, or an *avodah* that for him is "better" because he is more capable and suited to it.

And regarding this it is said, "He shall not inquire between good and bad, and he shall not exchange it"—that he should not exchange even the bad for the good, as follows.

**I.** And by way of preface:

It is possible that his desire to exchange the bad for the good is because of a *mistaken calculation* that comes from the advice of the *yetzer*, and in truth, the *avodah* he is being asked to perform is the "better" one.

—Once, a lumber merchant from California entered for *yechidus* to the Rebbe Rayatz, and after the Rebbe Rayatz answered his questions regarding

#### 78

the lumber business, he also asked regarding the education of his children, and he did not receive the answer and instruction of the Rebbe Rayatz. The Rebbe Rayatz said to him: "Consider this: regarding the lumber business—which I have never engaged in—you traveled from afar to ask for my advice, yet regarding the education of children—which is my business and the business of my ancestors—you do not accept my suggestion?!"...

And similarly in our case: since the Rebbe Rayatz assigned him a certain mission, it is clear that this mission is the "better" one for him, and not as it seems to him—through the advice of the *yetzer*—that it is better that he exchange it for another *avodah*.

Furthermore:

Even if the truth is as he says, that it is better that he exchange it for another *avodah*, bad for good—nevertheless, "He shall not inquire between good and bad, and he shall not exchange it."

**J.** And the reason for this—because "the Torah descended to the depths of human thought and the nature of the *yetzer hara*... and if you were to give him permission to exchange bad for good, he would exchange good for bad and say it is good":

The Sages said: "Such is the craft of the *yetzer hara*: today he says to him, 'Do this,' and tomorrow he says to him, 'Do this,' until he says to him, 'Go worship idols, etc.'"

The Rebbe Rayatz explained: The *yetzer hara* does not come to a person to tell him to commit a sin—*chas v'shalom*—for then he would certainly not listen to him; rather, when he is studying Torah and fulfilling mitzvos, he says to him, "Do this," meaning, "I too—the *yetzer hara*—agree that you should study Torah and fulfill mitzvos, because your study is so important that Hashem and the heavenly entourage take pleasure in your study..."
