—The "agreement" of the *yetzer* is expressed by the fact that he introduces his *yeshus* (ego) into the *avodah* of Torah study and mitzvah fulfillment, even though he wraps himself in a cloak of holiness, saying that his intention is for the sake of Heaven. "The necessity of your study," the *yetzer* explains to him, "is not for you, so that you will sit in *Gan Eden*, for even if you sit in *Gehinnom*, Hashem and the heavenly entourage will come there to hear your *chiddushei Torah*... rather, it is for the perfection of *Gan Eden*, because when the Patriarchs and all the *Tanna'im* and *Amora'im* will be in *Gan Eden* and you will not be there, then there will be a lack in the perfection of *Gan Eden*..."—

And after he says to him "Do this," that he "agrees" to the matters of Torah and mitzvos from the perspective of his *yeshus*, he can come and say "Do this, until he says to him, 'Go worship idols, etc.,'" that is,

#### 79

that the interference of *yeshus* in the *avodah* is the root from which can develop the situation where "he says to him, 'Go worship idols, etc.'"

And the advice for this—is to fulfill the mission that was assigned to him without making any calculations, "He shall not inquire between good and bad, and he shall not exchange it," out of *bitul* and acceptance of the yoke.

And this matter is the foundation for the general *avodah*—as it continues and concludes: "These are the mitzvos that Hashem commanded Moshe to the children of Israel at Mount Sinai."

*

[The following matters—their connection to the content of the *sicha* is not remembered:]

**K.** The Chassid R' D.T. used to study *Mishnayos* with his grandson. Once, when the grandson did not understand his grandfather's explanation of the words of the *Mishnah*, R' D.T. replied and remarked: "*Heilige osiyos*" (Holy letters)...

**L.** When the Rebbe Rayatz left Vienna, he was accompanied to the train by several German Jews ("*Deitsche Yiden*"). When the time for the train's arrival approached, one of them looked at his watch and said to the Rebbe: "*Noch ein minute*" (One more minute). The Rebbe replied and remarked after him: "*Ken men noch teshuvah ton*" (One can still do *teshuvah*).

**********

## Sicha of Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5710

#### 80

**A.** In the teachings of Chassidus it is brought and explained based on the words of our Sages, "Any person who does not have a house is not a person," meaning that a "house" is connected with the perfection of a person.

That is to say: Although a person has three types of needs—food, clothing, and a house—there is nevertheless a special quality in a house upon which the perfection of a person specifically depends, to the extent that "any person who does not have a house is not a person."

As we see tangibly, the need for "food" exists also in the vegetable kingdom; the need for "clothing" does not exist in the vegetable kingdom, but it is relevant to animals as well. However, the need for a "house" relates specifically to the perfection of *a person* (unlike animals, for even when they have a house, as it is written, "Even the bird has found a house," it is not in a way that touches the reality of the bird, such that one would say that if it did not find a house, it is not a bird).

**B.** The difference between food, clothing, and a house—as explained in the discourses of Chassidus—is that food is an internal matter that becomes blood and flesh of one’s own flesh; clothing is a surrounding matter (*makif*), but a close *makif* that is made according to the measure of the person; and a house is a distant *makif* that is not made according to the measure of the person.

Their corresponding concepts in *avodah*:

Food, the internal—indicates *avodah* that is according to intellect and reason, where the *avodah* is only according to the obligation of the intellect, which is the matter of internality.

Clothing, the close *makif*—indicates that the *avodah* is (also) in a manner of *bitul* that is above intellect, which is the matter of the *makif*. However, even this *bitul* that is above intellect is according to intellect—meaning, the intellect mandates that one must nullify the intellect and perform also things that the intellect does not mandate. This is the matter of the close *makif* that is made according to the measure of the person, meaning that even at the time of *bitul* (the *makif*), he remains in his reality (the measure of the person).

#### 81

And a house, the distant *makif*—indicates *avodah* that is entirely above intellect, *bitul* in essence, and upon this depends the true perfection of a person.

**C.** The matter of the "house" for Chassidim is the surrender and giving over (*ibergeben zich*) to the Rebbe.

This matter is relevant and touches both upon entering to the Rebbe (for *yechidus*)—which is not from the side of intellect, but from the side of his essential reality that is above intellect, like a son who is drawn to his father; and upon the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s words—where the fulfillment is not from the side of intellectual obligation, but from the side of *bitul*. Therefore, one fulfills even things that are not understood by the intellect at all. Furthermore, even things that are understood by the intellect must be fulfilled in the same manner that one fulfills things that are not understood by the intellect, for in such a manner specifically lies the true quality of fulfilling the Rebbe’s words.

— Once, a "contractor" entered to the Rebbe Maharash for *yechidus*. For years he had lived alone in Petersburg due to problems of *shalom-bayis*, until his relatives convinced him to return to his home. On his way home, he traveled to Lubavitch to receive the blessing of the Rebbe Maharash. In the course of conversation, he told the Rebbe that he had a business proposal from one of the generals in Petersburg, and after he returned home and established *shalom-bayis*, he would travel to Petersburg to finalize the deal. The Rebbe Maharash said to him: "Travel immediately to Petersburg and finish the deal, and afterwards return to your home." The contractor was astonished at the Rebbe’s words: How could it be that while he was on his way to return home after an absence of several years, the Rebbe would urge him to turn back to finish a deal?!... What was the reason for the haste?!... After the Rebbe repeated his words a second time, he said to the Rebbe: "As the Rebbe says, so I will do, but perhaps the Rebbe will tell me the reason?" The Rebbe replied: "If you knew the reason, you would be a 'Rebbe' yourself..." When the contractor arrived in Petersburg, he met the general as he was leaving his house for a long trip abroad. He immediately went up with the general to his house and they finalized the deal, from which the contractor later became wealthy! Then he understood the reason the Rebbe had hurried and urged him so much; had he arrived a few moments later, he would have lost the entire deal.

Seemingly, it is not understood: What would it have mattered to the Rebbe Maharash to tell him the reason he was urging him to travel to Petersburg to finish the deal?

The explanation for this is—as stated—that even in matters that are according to intellect, the fulfillment of

#### 82

the Rebbe’s words must be from a place of *bitul*. Therefore, he did not want to tell him the reason, so that he would fulfill his words from a place of *bitul*, which is the true perfection of a person, the matter of the "house."

**D.** All of this is emphasized most strongly regarding the "house" of the Rebbe Rayatz—as it is a *general house*, for all of Klal Yisrael.

When the Rebbe Rayatz entered his house for the first time, he went into the *shul* and *beis medrash* and said: "May it be the will that the prayers should be with an internality, and that one should daven with this true, internal *avodah* taste."

Seemingly: When speaking about buying a residential house—what do the prayers, etc., have to do with it?

The explanation for this is because the house is a general house for Klal Yisrael, for the one who entered to live in this house is a general soul whose occupation is in the matter of *tefillah*—from the word *chibur* (connection), to connect all of Klal Yisrael to their Father in Heaven.

**E.** During the ten years that the Rebbe Rayatz lived in this house, a portion of the debt for the payment of the house still remained, and consequently, the acquisition of the house was not entirely complete. From this, one can understand the greatness of the merit of that Jew whom the Rebbe Rayatz enabled to redeem the house by settling the entire debt, through which the house was acquired and became the property of the Rebbe Rayatz completely.

The truth is, the very fact that the Rebbe Rayatz left the debt and waited ten years for the arrival of this Jew to redeem the house is itself a great merit.

The Rebbe does not want to receive from everyone. There are those whom the Rebbe wants to receive from, and there are those whom the Rebbe does not want to receive from.

— Once, a certain Jew wanted to give the Rebbe a "maamad," and the Rebbe did not want to accept from him, saying: "A *maamad* is given by *Chassidim*." That Jew replied and said to the Rebbe: "I will be a Chassid," to which the Rebbe replied: "That is not how one begins."

From this, one can understand the greatness of the merit of this Jew for whom the Rebbe Rayatz waited ten years, and whom he allowed to redeem the house.

#### 83

**F.** The Rebbe Rayatz once said that he did not come "to receive" but "to give."

From this, it is understood that besides the greatness of the merit that this Jew received to redeem the house, his action in redeeming the general house also acts in such a way that the Rebbe gives him *hashpa'ah* regarding his private house. For the *hashpa'os* of the Rebbe exist even now, and even though in the interim the event of Yud Shevat occurred... it does not affect the *hashpa'os* of the Rebbe that exist even now, and even now he did not come "to receive" but "to give."

— I received a letter from one of the Chassidim in which he writes regarding the Rebbe Rayatz: "Der Rebbe zol gezunt zein" (May the Rebbe be healthy). I truly enjoyed this expression. And the truth is indeed so, because his health was not from physical matters, but from spiritual matters [and as it is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that "the life of the Tzaddik is not a fleshly life but a spiritual life, which is faith, fear, and love," and in our case, the life of a Tzaddik who is a shepherd of Israel is also from good tidings of the activities in strengthening Yiddishkeit, love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel], and in such health there is no interruption [and on the contrary: after the *histalkus* it is with greater strength, since the limitations of the physical body are nullified, as explained in the aforementioned *Iggeres HaKodesh*]. Consequently, it is appropriate to say "Der Rebbe zol gezunt zein." It is just that there are those who are embarrassed to say so, and that Chassid did away with the embarrassment and wrote according to the truth.

However, if this is so—that now the Rebbe is not limited and is found in every place—how do we dare to sit here and *farbreng*? Rather, this is because not only does the Rebbe not mind that we *farbreng*, and that "Yossel" distributes *mashke*, etc., but on the contrary, it is the Rebbe’s will (as he said several times) that we should *farbreng*. — Once, the Rebbe wanted to hear from his room upstairs how they were *farbrenging* in the *beis medrash* downstairs, but he feared that his coming downstairs would cause a disruption of the order, so he activated the "intercom" through which he could hear upstairs what was happening downstairs, and he listened to the *farbrengen*. — And although out of respect for him it is forbidden to speak in his presence, the general matter of "You shall surely set a king over you," "that his awe should be upon you," depends on physical matters—meaning, when his internality is seen through a physical garment, in his body and his clothing, and similarly in his belongings, that one does not use his scepter, etc.—and in our case, this does not apply.

#### 84

And let us return to our subject—that even now the Rebbe did not come "to receive" but "to give," and consequently, besides giving the merit of redeeming the house, he gives and influences what is needed for him in his private house.

And in addition to all this—the Torah promised, "Tithe so that you may become wealthy."

**G.** Based on what was said above regarding the greatness of the merit, etc., it is understood that one must strive to finish the matter with the greatest possible speed, for the greater the quality of the matter, the greater the effort of the *Yetzer Hara* to prevent it; therefore, one must hasten and finish the matter.

The story is known that the Alter Rebbe once "snatched" the portion of fish that was intended for the Maggid, and from this he had great benefit. — Seemingly, it is not understood: since the end proved the beginning that it was intended for him, why did he need to snatch it? Rather, as stated, the greater the quality of the matter, the more one must hasten and snatch it immediately. And if these things are said even regarding Tzaddikim, regarding simple people it is all the more so.

To what is this comparable? To a merchant who is offered a fair business deal from which he can profit much at once; he certainly will not delay in doing the business and settle for a slow profit ("bit-by-bit"). The matter depends only on the talent of the "broker" to explain to him the nature of the business. And so it is in the *nimshal*, in our case.

**H.** The truth is that the Rebbe Rayatz gives (not only the merit, but also) the *kochos* to do the matter; one must only *begin* to act with his own strength, and then the Rebbe assists and gives the necessary *kochos*.

Similar to what is told in the Midrash of our Sages regarding Rabbi Chanina ben Dosa, who wanted to bring a large stone up to Jerusalem: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, prepared for him... angels... He said to them, 'You bring up this stone for me.' They said to him... 'on the condition that you place your hand and finger with us.' He placed his hand and finger with them, and they found themselves standing in Jerusalem."

And similarly in our case—that by placing a finger ("az m'leigt nor tzu a finger"), they assist from above to complete the matter, even to the true perfection—to bring this house to Jerusalem, as our Sages said, "The synagogues and houses of study in Bavel are destined to be established in Eretz Yisrael," and Jerusalem is destined to spread throughout all of Eretz Yisrael, and Eretz Yisrael is destined to spread throughout all the lands.

#### 85

**I.** An additional merit fell to the lot of that Jew who merited to settle the remainder of the debt and redeem the house of the Rebbe Rayatz—the merit to print the *Sdei Chemed*.

— The author of the book *Sdei Chemed* was a Sephardic Jew, a great Tzaddik, but he did not have the merit to be a Chassid. —

For the publication of the *Sdei Chemed*, it would have been appropriate to hold a special *farbrengen*.

[R. Y. R. asked the Rebbe to say something on the *Sdei Chemed*, and the Rebbe said to him to open one of the books to any page he wished, and he opened to "Ma'areches Daled Minim." The Rebbe looked into the book for a few moments, and then said:]

It is discussed here regarding the custom practiced among Bnei Yisrael when buying an *esrog*, that one does not pay immediately but after a time.

— This is how the Rebbe Rayatz also used to conduct himself. The *esrogim* for the Rebbe were brought by R. Yisrael Jacobson [now this is no longer a secret, and certainly the evil eye will not rule over it, because of the connection to the Rebbe, and in the language of our Sages, "I come from the seed of *Yosef*, over whom the evil eye does not rule"], and some time after Sukkos, R. Yisrael Jacobson would give the Rebbe a report regarding the *esrogim*, and then the Rebbe would pay for the *esrogim*. In the first year of my arrival here, I asked the Rebbe that they should pay R. Yisrael Jacobson before Sukkos, so that it would be "yours" completely, and the Rebbe did not want to (it goes without saying "who carried it out"...).

At the beginning of his words, the *Sdei Chemed* brings that one must be careful to give the money immediately, because regarding an *esrog* there is an obligation from the Torah that it must be "yours," and by Torah law *money* acquires, whereas *meshichah* (pulling) acquires only by Rabbinic law. And he continues to explain that the opinion of the *poskim* is that a Rabbinic acquisition is effective for Torah matters. And he adds that the commitment to pay money (*zakaf alav b'milveh*) is considered like giving money, and it is also an acquisition of money.

[The continuation of the Sicha in explanation of the details of the discussion on this matter—is missing.]

**J.** And it should be added that the matter of the *esrog* is also connected with what was discussed above regarding the house of the Rebbe Rayatz:

An "esrog" is a "fruit of a beautiful tree," which "dwells in its tree from year to year"—in which is hinted the permanence of a "residential house." And since the *esrog* is the most praiseworthy of all the four species that hint at all four types among Bnei Yisrael [as it is in the Midrash that the *esrog*, which has taste and has scent, corresponds to those who have Torah and good deeds; the *lulav* (palm branches), which has taste and does not have scent, corresponds to those who have Torah and do not have good deeds; the *hadas*, which has scent and does not have taste, corresponds to those who have good deeds and do not have Torah; and the *aravos*, which have neither taste nor scent, correspond to those who have neither Torah nor good deeds], this hints at the "residential house" of the most praiseworthy of all Bnei Yisrael, the Nasi of the generation.

Furthermore:

Even though the "esrog" is the most praiseworthy of all the four species, it is not in a manner of pride and condescension over the other species, but connects with them, as hinted in the acronym of "esrog": "Do not let the foot of pride come to me." And similar to this with the Rebbe Rayatz—that despite the greatness of his level relative to the rest of Bnei Yisrael, he connects with all Bnei Yisrael, and connects them to their Father in Heaven. And this matter is emphasized especially in the "residential house"—that it is not a private house, but a general house for Klal Yisrael (as mentioned in section D).

#### 86

**K.** It is in the power of the Rebbe to instill into a soul powers from a higher soul, and even to replace a soul with a higher soul (similar to what we find in the opposite—in the reason for saying the blessings "that He did not make me a gentile, a slave, and a woman" every day (according to the words of the Kabbalists), which are "over the departure of his soul at night, that the soul of a gentile, slave, or woman did not attach to it").

**L.** The Rebbe once said that there are Jews—"Shulchan Aruch Yidden"—who did not have a "Rebbe," who during *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah* that fell on Shabbos would be conflicted about what to do: to clap hands—it is forbidden on Shabbos (unless with a *shinui*), and on the other hand, one is obligated to fulfill the "law" that "one must rejoice"... They clapped their hands while they were reversed, pinched their cheeks, and sang: "Ich bin freilach, ich bin freilach" (I am happy, I am happy)...

**M.** There is a saying that "money" must be counted, since it is possible for it to have a loss, loss, or addition, but "years," in which it is not possible to have a loss, loss, or addition, are not counted.

## Sicha of the Second Day of Shavuos, 5710

#### 88

**A.** In the *maamar* for Shavuos, titled *Vayospu Anavim B’Hashem Simcha* [1], the Rebbe Rayatz explains the connection between *anavah* (humility) and *simcha* (joy). Not only are they not opposites, but on the contrary, they assist one another.

The core of this explanation is that "in his essential nature, the *anav* (humble person) is firm in his conviction, and everything he does, he does with strong resolve." This is because "the lowliness of the *anav* is not a matter of submission or *bitul* (self-nullification) resulting from him being inherently lowly. The *anav* knows his own worth and knows that these qualities are of great importance; however, because he recognizes the truth, he does not consider them to be his own personal level or achievement." He "recognizes the truth that any goodness he possesses is not from himself, but rather what he inherited from our forefathers. Because of this, there is *bitul*, but this *bitul* is not a matter of lowliness; it is the setting aside of his own selfhood out of recognition of the truth," to the point that "he does not consider himself at all," for in his own eyes he is considered as nothing. This *bitul* (*anavah*) is a vessel for the highest *simcha*.

**B.** We must explain the connection and relevance of *anavah* to the festival of Shavuos:

Regarding the innovation of *Matan Torah*, the *Midrash* [2] states: "It is like a king who decreed and said: 'The people of Rome shall not descend to Syria, and the people of Syria shall not ascend to Rome.' Similarly, when the Holy One, Blessed be He, created the world, He decreed and said: 'The heavens are the heavens of Hashem, and the earth He gave to the children of man' [3]. When He desired to give the Torah, He nullified the first decree and said: 'The lower realms shall ascend to the upper realms, and the upper realms shall descend to the lower realms.'" This means that before *Matan Torah*, there was a separation (*gezeirah* in the sense of a partition, "a cut") between the Upper and the Lower, which is the concept of "Rome" and "Syria"—"Rome" representing the loftiness of the Upper, and "Syria" representing the Lower. At *Matan Torah*, the partition between the Upper and the Lower was nullified, and consequently, the Lower became connected and related to the Upper [4].

More specifically—as explained in the first *maamar* of Shavuos (titled *V’Chol Ha’am Ro’im*) [5]—at *Matan Torah*, the concept of *ha’alaah* (ascent) from below to above was innovated. Until *Matan Torah*, all revelations were by way of *is’arusa d’leila* (arousal from Above) on its own, and not through *is’arusa d’letata* (arousal from below), through the *avodah* of the lower being, because the lower being had no connection (*farbund*) to this. Even the Patriarchs, who fulfilled the entire Torah before it was given [6], their fulfillment was in a spiritual sense. That is to say, even the *mitzvos* they performed physically did not effect the drawing down of *kedushah* into the physical (the physical object with which they performed the *mitzvah*) in a literal sense. Therefore, after the performance of the *mitzvah*, the physical remained as it was before its performance, and the drawing down was only in the spiritual realm [7]. But at *Matan Torah*, when the *Torah* and *mitzvos* were given in the physical realm, the concept of *ha’alaah* from below to above was innovated—that specifically through *is’arusa d’letata*, there is *is’arusa d’leila*, whereby the lower being becomes related and connected to the Upper.

However, even after the innovation of *Matan Torah* through the ascent of the lower being, one must know that this is not due to the merit of the lower being, but rather due to the Upper (in the manner of a gift or inheritance), for it arose in His will, may He be blessed, that through *is’arusa d’letata* there should be *is’arusa d’leila* [8]. This is the essence of *anavah*: "recognizing the truth that any goodness he possesses is not from himself, but rather what he inherited..."

**C.** The lesson from this for us:

We must know that the qualities and strengths we possess are only what has been given to us by the Rebbe Rayatz. Consequently, we must be in a state of absolute *bitul*, to fulfill the *shlichus* of the Rebbe with full force. As mentioned, the *anav* is, in his essential nature, firm in his conviction, without considering any interference, concealment, or hiding.

The *shlichus* of the Rebbe must be fulfilled without considering anything. One should not consider all the questions and doubts: "Why do we say Kaddish?" "Why do we write 'the Rebbe'?" and so on. One must conduct oneself like an *anav* who is firm in his conviction and does not consider anything.

—A *Chossid* wrote to me that since the *histalkus*, he is very broken, and sometimes, when he is alone, he bursts into tears...

The question is, however, what did he accomplish through his crying? Is this the intention of the Rebbe, who asked him to cry?! It is almost certain that through his tears he accomplishes nothing, except for the matter that our Sages said [9]: "Whoever sheds tears for a worthy person (and all the more so in our case), the Holy One, Blessed be He, counts them and places them in His treasury." But in the meantime, the *avodah* of the Rebbe’s *shlichus* is not being done!

In the words of the Rebbe in the *sicha* of Shavuos [10]: "What are we waiting for? We are delaying the *Geulah*. It is already *Erev Shabbos* after midday."

Through the lack of *avodah*, one is, *chas v'shalom*, delaying the *Geulah*, delaying the Holy One, Blessed be He, delaying the Rebbe, and because of this, *Bnei Yisrael* remain another moment in *Golus*!

**D.** An additional lesson regarding the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s *shlichus* without considering questions and doubts—from the special quality of the second day of *Yom Tov* of Shavuos compared to the second day of *Yom Tov* of other festivals:

The second day of other festivals is to fulfill the custom of our ancestors, who would observe two days of *Yom Tov* due to the uncertainty of the day (*safeka d'yoma*), as they did not know on which day *Rosh Chodesh* was established in *Eretz Yisrael*. This is not the case with Shavuos, because its timing is not dependent on the days of the month (as it is in the *Gemara* [11] that "Atzeres is sometimes five, sometimes six, sometimes seven [days after Pesach]," depending on the timing of *Rosh Chodesh* Iyar and *Rosh Chodesh* Sivan), but rather on the fifty days of the *Omer*. By then, the day on which *Rosh Chodesh* Nissan and the festival of Pesach were established is already known and publicized everywhere. Consequently, the timing of the fiftieth day of the *Omer* is known with certainty. The reason we observe two days of *Yom Tov* is due to the enactment of the Sages not to differentiate between the festivals [12].

In other words: the second day of other festivals is because of *doubt*, whereas the second day of Shavuos is (not because of doubt, but) *l’chatchila* a *Yom Tov* of *certainty* (by enactment of the Sages). That is to say, the *kedushah* of the *Yom Tov* is not due to doubt, but is a certain *kedushah* [13].

This is similar to the distinction between the second day of *Yom Tov* of the Diaspora and the second day of *Rosh Hashanah*—that the second day of *Rosh Hashanah* is not due to doubt, but because "even the *Beis Din* themselves, who would sanctify based on sighting, would sometimes observe two days... these two days are one *kedushah* and one long day" [15].

It can be said that the second day of Shavuos (and similarly the second day of *Rosh Hashanah*) is a *Yom Tov* in its own right, which is not dependent on the first day (due to *safeka d'yoma*). This has a practical implication regarding a minor who becomes an adult on the second day of *Yom Tov*: if the second day of *Yom Tov* is dependent on the first, since he was exempt from the first day, he would also be exempt from the second [like a minor who becomes an adult between the first Pesach and the second Pesach, who is exempt from the second Pesach according to the opinion that it is a makeup for the first [16]]. If the second day of *Yom Tov* is a *Yom Tov* in its own right and not dependent on the first, he is obligated in the second day of *Yom Tov*.

Its meaning in the *avodah* of man—according to the well-known [17] that "safek" (doubt) has the same *gematria* as "Amalek," whose purpose is to cool and cast doubts in *kedushah*. One must nullify the *klipah* of Amalek, not to be affected by questions and doubts that raise uncertainties, but to engage in *avodah* in all matters of *kedushah* (and in our case, in fulfilling the Rebbe’s *shlichus*) with the force of certainty, as emphasized by the second day of Shavuos, whose *kedushah* is a certain *kedushah*.

**E.** Another point regarding this:

Even the second day of Shavuos, which is not due to *safeka d'yoma* but as a matter of certainty, is not from the Torah, but an *enactment of the Sages*. Nevertheless, it has *kedushah* like a *Yom Tov* from the Torah, because the fulfillment of the Sages' enactment is a commandment from the Torah, as it is written [18]: "According to the Torah which they shall teach you," "You shall not deviate from the matter which they tell you," and as it is written [19]: "Ask your father and he will tell you, your elders and they will say to you."

Similarly, regarding the fulfillment of the command of the Rebbe: even if, on the face of it, one might investigate whether it is an obligation from the Torah, from the Rabbis, a detail of the Scribes, or a *hiddur mitzvah*, just as details of the Scribes and *hiddur mitzvah* are included in the Torah's command "According to the Torah which they shall teach you," "You shall not deviate," "Ask your father," so too is it regarding the command of the Rebbe. Consequently, it is like an obligation from the Torah [20].

**F.** Toward Shavuos 5710, the Rebbe Rayatz wrote a special letter to the students of the *Yeshivos* [21]. Among the matters he writes there [22]:

"Shavuos is a time of *eis ratzon* (a time of favor) Above, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, distracts the accuser (*maktrig*) regarding the Jewish people [23], similar to His distraction during the time of the *Tekios* on *Rosh Hashanah* and the holy day of *Yom Kippur*. This means that Shavuos is a time suited to do everything for the benefit of Torah study and *avodah* in *yiras shamayim*, and also to engage in *teshuvah* regarding Torah without interference from the accusing Satan, similar to the time of the *Tekios* on *Rosh Hashanah* and the holy day of *Yom Kippur*." End quote.

To add: in this matter, there is a difference between *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*. On *Rosh Hashanah*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, only distracts and confuses the accusing Satan, whereas on *Yom Kippur*, there is no existence of the accusing Satan at all, as it is in the *Gemara* [24]: "The Satan on *Yom Kippur* has no permission to accuse... The Satan has the *gematria* of 364; for 364 days he has permission to accuse, but on *Yom Kippur* he has no permission to accuse."

According to what the Rebbe Rayatz wrote—that Shavuos is similar to *Rosh Hashanah* and *Yom Kippur*—it can be said that on Shavuos, the Holy One, Blessed be He, distracts the accusing Satan in such a way that there is no existence of the accusing Satan at all.

The aforementioned letter—one must study it, and also publicize it among those who do not know about it.

**G.** And another thing, and this is essential—that the study of the Rebbe’s letter (and similarly all matters of his Torah) must be in the manner of "Whoever says a teaching in the name of its author should see the author of the teaching as if he is standing before him" [25].

By way of introduction—the *Tzemach Tzedek* explains [26] that this statement of our Sages refers to the general matter of Torah study, because "Torah is the teachings of the Holy One, Blessed be He," and one must see "the author of the teaching (the Holy One, Blessed be He) standing before him," remembering that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and whoever reads and studies, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is reading and studying before him [27]. However, the simple interpretation is regarding the *Rav* in whose name one says this matter, that one must visualize the face of the *Rav* "as if he is standing before him."

Also note the well-known story [28] that the *Tzemach Tzedek* commanded to play the *Nigun* of the Four Stanzas of our *Alter Rebbe*, saying that whoever says a thing in the name of its author should see as if the author of the teaching is standing before him, and he himself began to play, and all those gathered searched around them for the *Alter Rebbe*...

From this, it is understood also in our case—that when one studies a *maamar*, *sicha*, *reshima*, or letter from the Rebbe, one must contemplate and remember the image of the Rebbe [including also those who did not see him, that they should visualize the Rebbe for themselves through a picture] as if he is standing before him!

—Once, the *Alter Rebbe* asked his son, the *Mitteler Rebbe*, with what contemplation he prayed on *Rosh Hashanah*, and he replied that he prayed with the contemplation of "And all who stand before You shall bow down." And you, the *Mitteler Rebbe* asked the *Alter Rebbe*, with what contemplation did you pray? He replied, "I prayed with the *shtender* (lectern)" [29]. We do not belong to such matters, but we can at least look at the *shtender* upon which the Rebbe prayed!...

**H.** And one must add regarding the general matter of studying his Torah:

Our Sages said [30]: "Any Torah scholar in whose name a teaching is said in this world, his lips murmur in the grave." And it is in *Maor Einayim* [31] in the name of the *Baal Shem Tov* that "it is possible to say that this is the concept of *hishtatchus* (prostration) at the graves of the *Tzaddikim*, because the speech of the *Tzaddik* is buried and hidden there—his vitality ('in his Torah he lies with his entire essence')—and this student, by entering with his vitality and *mochin* (intellect) into the vitality and *mochin* of the *Tzaddik* that he hid in his words, it is called the attachment of spirit to spirit, and his lips murmur in the grave, etc."

According to this, one can explain what is written regarding Moshe Rabbeinu: "And no man knows his burial place" [32]—"those who stand above, it seems to them below; those who stand below, it seems to them above" [33]—that no one (neither those standing below nor those standing above) took his essence ("his burial place"), and where is he himself (as it is written [32], "And He buried him")—this is in the *Torah*, as it is in the *Zohar* [34]: "His burial is the *Mishnah*."

This matter is especially relevant to those who, for various reasons, cannot go to the holy *tziyon*—that they should know that studying his Torah is like the matter of *hishtatchus*.

And another thing, and this is essential—that since he placed his essence into his Torah, through studying his Torah, one connects to him.

—Someone might think what connection he has to the Rebbe, and the answer to this is that the connection is not from his side (by his power), but from the side of the Rebbe, who in every word and matter that he said or wrote "placed his essence," and therefore, through studying his Torah, one connects to him.

To add, that in the matter of connection through studying his Torah is also included the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s instruction—to those whom he commanded—to teach the *Aleph-Beis*. That teaching *Aleph-Beis* because of the Rebbe’s command is considered as studying his Torah (although certainly one should not be satisfied with this, but one must also study his Torah literally [35]).

**I.** The matter of connection to the Rebbe is not because of this quality or that, but because of his being a "Rebbe."

Once, they asked the *Rashbatz* [36] about the *Admur* (the *Rashab*) *n"e* if he was a master of *Ruach HaKodesh*, and he replied: "What does *Ruach HaKodesh* matter to me? I know he is a Rebbe, and consequently, if a Rebbe needs *Ruach HaKodesh*, he certainly has it, and if he does not need *Ruach HaKodesh*, what is the excitement about *Ruach HaKodesh*?!..."

An example of this: regarding *Adam HaRishon* and Avraham Avinu, even though we find in the words of our Sages the greatness of *Adam HaRishon* to the extent that "his heel dimmed the orb of the sun" [37], nevertheless, our Sages said [38]: "Until Avraham, the world was behaving in darkness, and when Avraham came, it began to shine" [39]. Since the matter of "it began to shine" is relevant to us, the matter of Avraham Avinu is relevant to us, and not *Adam HaRishon*, even though "the heel of *Adam HaRishon* dimmed the orb of the sun." Similarly, regarding our *Rebbeim Nesi'im*, through whom "it began to shine" the revelation of the inner dimension of the Torah, and consequently, to us, the connection to the *Rebbeim* is relevant, and it is not relevant to us if there is someone whose "heel dims the orb of the sun."

A "Rebbe"—is one who is connected with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (Essence and Being) of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed, and consequently, to us, only the connection to the Rebbe is relevant, and through him we connect with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed.

—Someone writes me a letter with praises and exaltations about the Rebbe. Among the praises, he also writes that once, while he was with the Rebbe in Leningrad, the Rebbe stood, and suddenly it seemed to him that the *Admur* the *Rashab* *n"e* was standing before him. — When the Rebbe was in *Eretz Yisrael*, an old Jew who had merited to see the *Admur* the *Maharash* entered to see him, and upon seeing the Rebbe... he fainted, and when they woke him from his fainting and asked him the reason for the matter, he said that upon entering to the Rebbe, he saw in him the *Admur* the *Maharash*...

That *Chossid* who was connected to the *Admur* the *Rashab* or the *Admur* the *Maharash* saw a greatness in that he saw in the Rebbe the *Admur* the *Rashab* or the *Admur* the *Maharash*.

But the truth is, that the resemblance and comparison of the Rebbe to the *Admur* the *Rashab* or the *Admur* the *Maharash* is not what matters; all that matters is only that he is the Rebbe, who is connected with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed, and through the connection to him, one connects with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed.

Someone told me [40]—with excitement—that the Rebbe Rayatz said to him: "Be connected to me, and through me you will be connected to the One to whom I am connected." — That person thought that by saying "to the One to whom I am connected," the Rebbe meant his father, the *Admur* the *Rashab* *n"e*, and the like, and from this was his excitement, etc., but the truth is, that the Rebbe’s intention was for connection with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed!

**J.** Continuing from what was discussed on the 2nd of Iyar [41] regarding the proposal to strengthen the connection by each person taking upon himself two things, regarding himself and regarding another—now, all those who have taken upon themselves [42], should now say "L'chaim."

And those who have not yet taken upon themselves—they too should say "L'chaim," and take upon themselves from now on.

**K.** On the 12th of Tammuz this year, it will be *seventy years* since the birth of the Rebbe Rayatz (5640–5710).

And since at the age of seventy a new period begins, "seventy for *seivah* (old age/wisdom)" [43], a new period must begin in all matters of the *avodah* of the Rebbe Rayatz, which continue as long as his *shlichus* has not yet ended, which is the concept of "a hundred is as if he died and passed away and ceased from the world" [44].

Therefore, one must utilize the time remaining until the 12th of Tammuz and act in the matters of the Rebbe, and toward the 12th of Tammuz, one will need to give an accounting.

**L.** Among the matters that were the desire of the Rebbe Rayatz that the *bochurim* should engage in—traveling on the *shlichus* of the *MLCH* (Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch) during the summer period [45].

Last year, for various reasons, there was a certain weakness in traveling on this *shlichus*, and consequently, one must strive that this year they should complete also what they lacked last year.

The truth is, this *shlichus* has no makeup, just as there is no makeup in Torah study, because the obligation of Torah study is every day and every moment, and every time one studies, he fulfills the obligation that exists at this time in its own right, and not as a makeup for an obligation at a time before it, as discussed above [46].

But, one does not cry over the past; the demand is regarding the fulfillment of the *shlichus* this year as it should be, and the "completion" for last year will be expressed in that they will engage with greater force, and for a longer time.

**M.** Discussed was the distinction between the three matters of Shavuos: (a) "Time of the Giving of our Torah," which is in its strength at all times (Torah is eternal [47]), (b) "Day of the First Fruits," that the *mitzvah* of *Bikkurim* (even though they are not offered on the altar like the two loaves, but are eaten by the *Kohanim*) is relevant only in the time of the *Beis Hamikdash*, (c) the fiftieth day of the *Sefirah*, which depends on the dispute whether *Sefiras HaOmer* in this time is from the Torah or from the Rabbis [48]—in connection and relevance to the *avodah* of man [49].

**N.** Discussed was the one who crosses the International Date Line in the middle of the days of the *Sefirah*, that even though regarding *Shabbos* it is obvious that he does not count for himself ("Six days you shall work... and the seventh day is *Shabbos*" [50]) but relies on the counting of days in that place, nevertheless, regarding *Sefiras HaOmer*, one must be in doubt whether the counting should be as all *Bnei Yisrael* count in that place, or if he must continue in his own counting [51]. And the content of the matter was explained in the *avodah* of man.

**O.** During the days of the *Sefirah*, it is the custom [52] to study *Maseches Sotah*, one page a day: the beginning of the *Maseches*, page 2, is studied on the first day of *Chol HaMoed*, the second day of the *Sefirah* (and not on the second day of *Yom Tov*, which is the first day of the *Sefirah*), and on the second day of *Chol HaMoed* one studies page 3, and so on, until *Erev Shavuos*, when one studies page 49, the conclusion of the *Maseches*.

[The content of *Maseches Sotah* was explained—"And she shall be cleansed and shall conceive seed" [53], "If she was barren, she is remembered" (according to the opinion of *Rabbi Akiva*), and the question (of *Rabbi Yishmael*) "If so, all barren women should be separated and be remembered," and the conclusion that "If she was giving birth with pain, she gives birth with ease, etc., if she was giving birth to black, she gives birth to white" [54]—in the *avodah* of man, in connection to the *Sefirah*].

At the conclusion of *Maseches Sotah*, we learned [55]: "When the Rebbe died, *anavah* and *yiras chet* (fear of sin) ceased. Rav Yosef said to the *Tanna*: 'Do not teach *anavah*, for I am here' (that I am humble—*Rashi*). Rav Nachman said to the *Tanna*: 'Do not teach *yiras chet*, for I am here.'"

And one must understand:
1) Rav Yosef and Rav Nachman are *Amoraim*, and how can they disagree with the *Tanna* and say to him: "Do not teach *anavah*," "Do not teach *yiras chet*"?
2) The statement "Do not teach *anavah*, for I am here," and in the language of *Rashi* "for I am humble"—is seemingly the *opposite of anavah*?
3) What is the reason that Rav Yosef emphasizes the quality of *anavah* and Rav Nachman emphasizes the quality of *yiras chet*?

**P.** It will be understood by introducing what was explained above (Section A) regarding the matter of *anavah*—that "the *anav* knows his own worth, and knows that these qualities are of great importance, but because he recognizes the truth, he does not consider them to be his own personal level or achievement," that "he recognizes the truth that any goodness he possesses is not from himself, but rather what he inherited from our forefathers, etc.," and furthermore, he makes a calculation in his soul that "if these strengths were with another... perhaps he would reveal the strengths more" [56].

Similarly in our case:
Rav Yosef certainly knew the greatness of his merit in Torah study—as he said: "If not for this day that causes (that I studied Torah and was elevated), how many Yosefs are there in the market" [57]—to the point that he was called by the name "*Sinai*" [58], because "the *Mishnayos* and *Baraisos* were arranged for him as they were given from Mount Sinai" [59], and nevertheless, he did not take credit for himself, knowing that all his qualities were given to him as a gift from Above, and in his words: "If not for this day that causes."

And therefore he could say "I am humble"—because the quality of *anavah* is not in contradiction at all to knowing one's own worth, including also the quality of *anavah* itself.

**Q.** According to this, one can also explain the words of Rav Yosef—the *Amora*—to the *Tanna*, "Do not teach *anavah*":

From the side of the humility of Rav Yosef, who recognized that all his qualities were given to him as a gift from Above—he attributed them (not to himself, but) to the *Rebbe*.

It can be said that by saying to the *Tanna* "Do not teach *anavah*, for I am here," he did not intend to disagree with the words of the *Tanna* ("When the Rebbe died, *anavah* ceased") that without a Rebbe there is no longer the quality of *anavah*, but rather, that the fact that "I am here" (that I am humble) proves that "*the Rebbe did not die*."

True *anavah*—knowing one's own worth, on one hand, and absolute *bitul* in knowing that his qualities are not from himself, on the other—is possible only through a *Rebbe*.

**R.** Similarly, one can explain the words of Rav Nachman, "Do not teach *yiras chet*, for I am here":

By introducing the difference between Rav Yosef (*anavah*) and Rav Nachman (*yiras chet*)—that Rav Yosef, being blind [60], from whom the *Yetzer Hara* ceased, was not susceptible to sin [61], and consequently, he does not need *yiras chet*, and therefore, the quality of *anavah* is emphasized in him; whereas Rav Nachman, we find in the *Gemara* [62] that "the mother of Rav Nachman was told by the astrologers: 'Your son will be a thief.' She did not let him uncover his head. She said to him: 'Cover your head so that the *fear of Heaven* will be upon you,'" and therefore, the quality of *yiras chet* is emphasized in him.

[It can be said that even after he covered his head so that he would have *yiras chet*, the matter of "thief" remained with him—in *kedushah*. Similar to what is said at the beginning of the passage [63]: "He who is born under Mars will be a man who sheds blood... either a surgeon, or a thief, or a butcher, or a circumciser," meaning, that he utilizes the trait of "shedding blood" for *kedushah*].

And the power for this—"so that the *fear of Heaven* will be upon you"—is from the Rebbe:

Regarding the quality of a Rebbe, we find that "he did not put his hand under his belt" [64], meaning, that for him there was no difference between lofty matters that belong to *Heaven* and lower matters that belong to *earth* [as we find that "a certain magician said to Amemar: 'From half and above, it is of Ormuzd; from half and below, it is of Ahriman'" [65], that "he was inclined to heresy, that he who created the spiritual did not create the physical, and to this he said: from half and above, where the spiritual vessels of breath are, is the portion of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and from half and below, where the physical vessels ('eating and drinking, etc., being fruitful and multiplying' [67]) are, is the portion of another power"], but rather, even the physical matters (from half and below) were for *Heaven*, and to such an extent, that even though "there did not cease from his table neither lettuce, etc., neither in the summer nor in the winter" [68], nevertheless, "at the time of his passing... he raised his ten fingers toward Heaven and said... I did not derive pleasure (from this world) even with my little finger" [69].

And through the power of a *Rebbe*, that his entire existence and all his matters (even the lower ones) were for *Heaven*—it became also for Rav Nachman (who by his nature "was a thief") the matter of *yiras chet*.

And therefore he said "Do not teach *yiras chet*, for I am here"—that by this he did not intend to disagree with the words of the *Tanna* ("When the Rebbe died, *yiras chet* ceased") that without a Rebbe there is no longer the quality of *yiras chet*, but rather, that the fact that he has *yiras chet* (through the power of the Rebbe) proves that "*the Rebbe did not die*."

**S.** Discussed were the two matters of *anavah* and *yiras chet*, which are the foundations of *avodah*.

Continuing from the matter of *yiras chet*, discussed also was the difference between *Chassidus* and *Mussar*, that when one studies the teachings of *Chassidus* which deals with matters of *Elokus* (Divinity), even if the study did not effect its action, one was in the meantime engaged in matters of *Elokus*, whereas in the study of *Mussar*, etc.

**T.** Discussed was the connection between the *Baal Shem Tov* and King David, who passed away on Shavuos—according to the statement of our Sages [70] regarding the request of King David that the recitation of *Tehillim* should be considered like engaging in *Negaim* and *Ohalos*, which are the most rigorous matters in the Torah (as they said to *Rabbi Akiva*: "What have you to do with *Aggadah*? Go to *Negaim* and *Ohalos*" [71]), and similarly regarding the teachings of *Chassidus*, etc.

**U.** (At the conclusion of the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe *shlita* said:) May the Holy One, Blessed be He, help that the Rebbe Rayatz will come, as he is clothed in a body ["then one will be spared from asking to say *Chassidus*" [72]], and take us out of *Golus*!

—The order is indeed that the resurrection of the dead will be after the coming of *Moshiach* [73], but unique individuals will rise to resurrection before the coming of *Moshiach* [74].

And first and foremost—the Rebbe Rayatz, who will return and be clothed in a body, and come ("it makes no difference in what way, through the door, through the window, or through the roof"...) and gather all *Bnei Yisrael* and declare: "The time has arrived to go out of *Golus*, come, let

## B’s”D. From a Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Naso, 11 Sivan 5710

#### 101

(Unedited)

**1.** When the Bnei Yisrael were in the desert (following the Exodus from Mitzrayim), Hashem provided them with all their needs—both spiritual and physical—ready-made: bread from Heaven (which contained no waste[1](#_ftn465)), water from the well of Miriam, and the Clouds of Glory that would wash and press their garments[2](#_ftn466). The reason for this was that their departure from Mitzrayim into the desert was born of mesiras nefesh: "They did not ask, 'How shall we go into the desert without provisions?' Rather, they believed and followed... 'Going after Me in the desert, in a land not sown'"[3](#_ftn467).

But today, unfortunately, when one approaches a Yid and asks him to give to tzedakah, for example, he immediately begins making "calculations": first and foremost, he must look out for himself; if he gives to tzedakah now, he will lack funds for his own expenses in the coming year. Furthermore, he must ensure he has something to leave for his children after one hundred and twenty years... And in general—he argues—money that I earned with the toil and sweat of my brow, I should give to someone else for tzedakah?!... And regarding the needs of the poor, his argument is: Hashem, who made them poor, should take care of them[4](#_ftn468), and so on.

One must know and remember, as stated, that when one fulfills the will of Hashem without calculations, then Hashem provides for all one's needs, both spiritual and physical.

**2.** The concept that "a person is always liable... whether awake or asleep"[5](#_ftn469) was discussed. In continuation of this, the following was related:

My sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, would sometimes hold a farbrengen on Shabbos with his family. Once, he asked his youngest daughter—when she was a small child of about five years old—whether she knew that on the day of Shabbos all matters must be in a state of holiness, "for it is *kodesh*," "Shabbos... is *holy to Hashem*"[6](#_ftn470). She replied that she certainly knew that the day of Shabbos is holy to Hashem, and she feels this in the eating

#### 102

and drinking of the Shabbos meals, but *during sleep*—and being a small child, she also needed to rest in the middle of the day—she cannot think that the day of Shabbos is holy to Hashem.

The truth is, however, that even during sleep, the holiness of Shabbos must be evident and felt, as mentioned, that a person is liable at all times, whether awake or asleep.

**3.** The statement from the Sicha of the festival of Shavuos 5709[7](#_ftn471) was discussed: "What are we waiting for? We are the ones delaying the Geulah."

**4.** The days of tashlumin (compensation) for the festival of Shavuos were discussed—as the Alter Rebbe writes in his Siddur[8](#_ftn472) that Tachanun is not recited until the 12th of Sivan, inclusive—that in the week following Shavuos, one can rectify and complete that which was lacking, etc.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Shelach, Mevarchim Chodesh Tammuz, 5710

#### 103

(Unedited)

**1.** In this week’s parsha, we are told about the mission of the spies: “Send for yourself men to scout the land of Canaan,” “They went up and scouted,” “They returned from scouting the land… and they reported to them… and they told over,” and when the spies finished their report, “Calev silenced [the people]” (and only after Calev’s words did they say, “We cannot go up… and they spread a slander about the land”).

One must understand: what was the reason Calev needed to silence them, “Calev silenced them”?

The words of the spies were merely *answers*—according to the truth—to the questions Moshe asked them in their mission to scout the land regarding two general matters: (a) Regarding the people, “See… the people who dwell in it, is it strong or weak?”—to which they replied, “The people who dwell in the land are powerful, and the cities are fortified and very large.” (b) Regarding the land, “And what is the land… is it good or bad? Is it fat or lean?”—to which they replied, “It is a land flowing with milk and honey, and this is its fruit.”

Since Moshe sent them to scout the land, they were *obligated* to fulfill the mission and answer all the questions he asked them. (Moshe himself was not obligated to send the spies, as Rashi explains: “Send for yourself—according to your own judgment; I am not commanding you; if you wish, send.” But the spies, once Moshe sent them, were obligated to fulfill the mission and state their answers.)

Since they were obligated to answer and tell the truth about the people and the land, what reason did Calev have to silence them when they were answering *the truth*, even before the continuation of their words, “We cannot go up… and they spread a slander about the land,” *after* “Calev silenced them”?!

Furthermore, one must understand regarding Calev’s conduct: it is written, “They went up in the south and came to Chevron…,” and “Calev went there alone and prostrated himself on the graves of the Patriarchs so that he would not be enticed by his colleagues to join their counsel”—why was the *power of the sender* (who goes on his mission) not sufficient to save him from the counsel of the spies, such that he needed to prostrate himself on the graves of the Patriarchs specifically?

**2.** The explanation for this:

The sin of the spies was that in their answers, they intermingled their own intellect and changed the order of the matters Moshe had told them. Moshe commanded them to see the people first, “Is it strong or weak,” and afterwards the land, “Is it fat or lean.” In their report, they changed the order and put first, “It is a land flowing with milk and honey,” and afterwards, “The people who dwell in the land are powerful.”

The difference between them:

Moshe’s mission was, first, regarding the war and the conquest (“Is it strong or weak”), and afterwards regarding the profit and reward (“Is it fat or lean”), because the main thing for him was the conquest of the war (and not the profit and reward—not for the sake of receiving a reward).

Moreover, he placed “strong” before “weak”—because the mission to conquer the land applies in all circumstances, even if a heavy war is required. Therefore, the mission is *ab initio* with the intent that even though it is strong (and it can also be said that by going with *mesiras nefesh* to fight while it is strong, through that very act it becomes weak).

The spies changed the order and spoke as it appeared to their own intellect: first regarding the reward (“flowing with milk and honey”) and afterwards regarding the war and conquest (“the people who dwell in the land are powerful”). For them, the main thing was the reward (for the sake of receiving a reward), and from that they began to calculate regarding the work of war and conquest: that easy work (weak) is worthwhile for this reward, but harder work (strong) is not worthwhile—to the point that they were liable to err and say that if the work is hard, it is impossible to do, as they said afterwards: “We cannot go up.”

Therefore, when Calev saw that the spies were intermingling their intellect and changing Moshe’s mission, even if only regarding the order of things, he immediately silenced them.

**3.** Based on this, one can also explain the reason Calev needed to *prostrate* himself on the graves of the Patriarchs so as not to be enticed by his colleagues to join their counsel:

Moshe’s mission (the power of the sender) in and of itself does not negate the possibility that the messenger will make a change in the mission by intermingling his own intellect. This is the work of the messenger himself: to set aside and nullify his own intellect and to dedicate himself to the sender to fulfill his mission in a manner of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke).

Therefore, Calev went to *prostrate* himself on the graves of the Patriarchs—for the act of prostration signifies a state where the head and the feet are equal, *in a positive sense*, which is the concept of *kabbalas ol* that is above intellect. With this power, he was not enticed by his colleagues to join their counsel, fulfilling Moshe’s mission without intermingling his intellect, in a manner of *kabbalas ol*.

**4.** The lesson from this for us:

It is known that “the extension of Moshe is in every generation,” and furthermore, “there is no generation that does not have one like Moshe.” In our generation, this is the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory.

From this it is understood that the mission of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, who sent or sends or will send a certain person to a specific place to clarify his portion in the world, is like the mission of Moshe regarding the conquest of the land. For the content of Moshe’s mission in the conquest of the land was to make it Eretz Yisrael, sanctified above all lands, and this is also the content of the mission of the Moshe of our generation in clarifying one’s portion in the world—the place to which the Rebbe, my father-in-law, sent him and gave him the powers to clarify—to make it Eretz Yisrael, *chullin* on the level of *taharas hakodesh*.

Among the lessons we must learn from the parsha of the spies is not to intermingle our intellect and make any change, even a change of order alone, in the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, even when it seems to one that through this change he will succeed more in his mission. For by changing even a little from the words of the Rebbe, one can err to the point of a mistake similar to that of the spies. And *kal v’chomer*: if the spies, of whom it is said, “They were all men, heads of the Children of Israel,” when they changed the words of Moshe, came to err to the point of saying, “We cannot go up”—then people of our stature, all the more so.

As the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said in explanation of the statement of our Sages, “Such is the craft of the Yetzer Hara: today he says to him, ‘Do this,’ etc., until he says, etc.,” that the Yetzer Hara, who is called “the clever one,” does not start by telling a person to commit a sin, for at such a beginning he certainly would not listen to him. Rather, the beginning of his words is, “Do this,” so that when he performs a mitzvah, the Yetzer says to him, “Very good, I also agree that you should do this.” And when he begins to listen to his opinion and counsel—even though the beginning is regarding matters of mitzvah—he is intermingling his own opinion and counsel, and this is the root of “he tells him to worship, etc.”

Therefore, the primary condition in fulfilling the mission is the preservation of the Rebbe’s words, without change and without intermingling intellect, through *kabbalas ol* specifically.

**5.** The empowerment for this, especially now after the passing, is through the matter of prostration—“he prostrated himself on the graves of the Patriarchs,” as follows.

First, the reason why, when we speak about the Rebbe, my father-in-law, we do not say “*Zecher Tzaddik Livracha*” (as is found in Yoma) or “*Nishmaso Eden*”:

On Simchas Torah 5691, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said: “I do not say about my father ‘*Nishmaso Eden*,’ because I am not an address-writer, and furthermore, for me, my father did not pass away, etc.”

Similarly regarding the Rebbe, my father-in-law—one should not say about him “*Nishmaso Eden*,” because: (a) Who is it that can give an “address,” to limit his place to “Gan Eden,” lower Gan Eden or upper Gan Eden, or higher than that without measure? (b) Why should we send him away from us?! He certainly does not want to separate from us, and he is found with us!

For the same reason that we do not say “*Nishmaso Eden*,” we also do not say “*Zecher Tzaddik Livracha*,” because the concept of remembrance (“*Zecher*”) applies only to something distant where the matter of forgetting can occur. This is not the case here, where the matter of forgetting is not applicable, *chas v’shalom*; there is no need for remembrance, just as there is no need for remembrance regarding a living person.

**6.** More specifically:

It is stated in the Gemara: “What is the meaning of the verse, ‘I will dwell in Your tent for worlds’? Is it possible for a person to dwell in two worlds? … Every Torah scholar whose teachings are spoken in his name in this world, his lips murmur in the grave.” Tosafos explains: “When his soul is in the Yeshiva on High, his lips move in the grave as if they are speaking. It is found that at one time he dwells in two worlds.”

A “Yeshiva” (on High or below) is called such only when there is a Rosh Yeshiva with students. Students alone are not a Yeshiva; rather, it is when there is a Rosh Yeshiva who says a “shiur” before the students, and the students repeat the shiur and it comes to them in understanding and comprehension (and even when at first they do not understand, nevertheless, they repeat the words, and in time they will understand with their comprehension).

And in a “Yeshiva” (which includes a Rosh Yeshiva with students)—there is a “Yeshiva below,” in which they study matters of below, and there is a “Yeshiva on High,” in which they study matters of above. Both—the Yeshiva below and the Yeshiva on High—exist both before the passing and after the passing. The difference is only regarding *concealment and revelation*: before the passing, he is found in revelation in the Yeshiva below, and in concealment in the Yeshiva on High; and after the passing, the opposite, that he is found in revelation in the Yeshiva on High, and in concealment in the Yeshiva below. But in the essence of the matter—that even now he is found here, in the Yeshiva below—there is no change at all.

It is written, “From the mouth of the Most High, evil does not emerge.” And since it is impossible for there to be “the good” unless one is found together with the Rebbe, my father-in-law, then certainly he is found with us as before, and the change is only regarding *revelation and concealment*. Previously he was with us in revelation, and now he is found with us in concealment. Therefore, now there is a need to bring proof from the words of the Gemara—that “it is possible for a person to dwell in two worlds,” and for this there is a need for the study of his Torah, “whose teachings are spoken in his name, his lips murmur, etc.” But on the other hand, the fact that now he is found with us in concealment and we need to bring proof for this does not cause any weakening in the essence of the matter at all!

—The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related that someone asked his father, the Rebbe Rashab, about the fact that people speak about angels and spiritual matters in general, how do we know that it is so, for no one has come from there and told how an angel looks, etc.? The Rebbe Rashab replied to him with a parable: To what is this similar? To wise men who are traveling in a wagon harnessed to horses and are speaking about angels. Just because the horse thinks that the purpose of the trip is for the straw found in the place to which they are traveling, and the wagon driver thinks about the payment of money for the trip in order to support his household (a thought more refined than the horse’s thought)—does that mean the words of the wise men about angels have no value?! … The same applies here: the lack of our knowledge in lofty matters—since our knowledge is literally material, or even more refined, but nevertheless material—does not cause any change at all in the essence of the matter.

**7.** An additional empowerment for this is through the prostration—“he prostrated himself on the graves of the Patriarchs”:

The matter of prostration is going to his grave with the knowledge “that here he is…” and one visualizes the form of his face… and through this, strength and might are added to the *hiskashrus* (connection), and to the fulfillment of his mission without changes and calculations at all.

—When one hears from Moshe, the Moshe of our generation, a command and instruction *one time*, then over time there can be a weakening and coldness, an intermingling of intellectual calculation, and the like (as in the sin of the spies). Therefore, the advice is to strengthen the *hiskashrus* through prostration.

Included in this is also the matter of prostration in spirituality—as is stated in the book *Maor Einayim* in the name of the Baal Shem Tov, that the matter of prostration in spirituality is through the study of the Torah of the Tzaddik, in which he placed his entire essence (“on this he gave himself and in this he gave himself over”), similar to what we find in the Zohar regarding Moshe, that “his burial is *Mishnah*.”

From this it is understood that also through the study of the Torah of the Rebbe, my father-in-law—the matter of prostration in spirituality—strength and might are added to the *hiskashrus* and to the fulfillment of his mission as required.

\*

#### 109

**8.** Regarding the aforementioned matter—fulfilling the mission of clarifying one’s portion in the world to make it Eretz Yisrael through the strength of the *hiskashrus* to the Moshe of our generation—there is a special empowerment on Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh *Tammuz*:

The special character of the month of Tammuz is that it is the *season of heat*, as the saying goes, “Wine, even in the season of Tammuz, is cool to me.” In other seasons, the matter of coolness is not attributed to the “donkey” specifically, for it is possible that the coolness is due to the lack of the strength of the heat. Only in the season of Tammuz, the season of heat, is the coolness attributed to the “donkey” specifically, for his coolness (“is cool to me”) at a time of the strength of the heat is an indication of materiality (“donkey”).

Its character in spiritual service—as it is written, “For Hashem Elokim is a sun and a shield,” and in the season of Tammuz is the strength of the heat of the “sun of Hashem.”

**9.** The matter of this:

The matter of heat is a virtue in service, as is stated in books of *mussar* and Chassidus that all matters of the service of Hashem must be with warmth specifically.

Furthermore: according to what is known that the purpose of creation is for the sake of Yisrael, as the saying goes, “*Bereishis*—for the sake of Yisrael who are called *reishis*,” and within Yisrael themselves, it is for the sake of the matter of Torah that is in Yisrael (“for the sake of Torah and for the sake of Yisrael”). That is, the purpose of creation is so that Yisrael will fulfill the Torah, as it is stated in Maseches Berachos, “The entire world was created only to serve this one,” and similarly in Maseches Kiddushin, “They were not created except to serve me, and I was not created except to serve my Creator”—it is understood that the matter of heat that was created in the world for the sake of Torah and Yisrael is essentially in matters of Torah and service.

And although seemingly coolness was also created with the purpose of bringing benefit to service—there is a difference between coolness and warmth. Warmth is a positive reality, which comes from the side of vitality specifically, whereas coolness, whose reality is a deficiency, where in the absence of vitality and movement, coolness is naturally created. And since its reality is only a deficiency, it is not appropriate to say that the purpose of its creation is for the sake of Torah, since it is not a creation, unlike warmth, as mentioned above.

**10.** To add: in truth, the matter of vitality and warmth needed to be in holiness specifically, and the reason there is vitality and warmth also in matters of the world is so that there would be the matter of *bechirah* (choice). For if the matter of vitality and warmth were only in holiness, there would be no matter of *bechirah*. Therefore, there needed to be vitality and warmth also in other matters.

An example of this:

It is stated in a *maamar* of the Rebbe Rashab that “in the future, the form of the bodies of the nations will be like animals, and now it is for the sake of *bechirah*, etc.” That is: the difference between a human and an animal is that a human walks in an upright posture (and consequently the brain is above the heart, and therefore it rules over it), and the heart is above the feet, unlike animals, for whom everything is equal. Based on this, it should have been for the nations of the world as it is for animals; why were they created in an upright posture? The explanation is that if they had been created like animals, there would be no place for the matter of *bechirah*. Therefore, they were also created in the form of a human, but they are not at all in the stature of a human, and it is Yisrael specifically who are in the stature of a human, for it is written, “You are *Adam* (human).”

—I heard from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, that someone asked the Rebbe Rashab (I believe) about the matter of *shmiras habris* (guarding the covenant), and the Rebbe Rashab told him that the matter of guarding is as it was with the Ohr HaChaim. Once, the Ohr HaChaim was traveling with a caravan in the desert, and when Shabbos arrived, they did not want to wait for him, so he remained alone. A lion came to him, and the Ohr HaChaim showed him the sign of the covenant. When he saw this, not only did he not do anything to him, but he guarded him from all the beasts, and after Shabbos the Ohr HaChaim rode on him and traveled on him until he caught up with the caravan. That is the end of the story. The explanation of this—according to the statement of our Sages, “No wild beast has dominion over a human unless he appears to it like an animal.” Therefore, when the lion saw the sign of the covenant—for *bris* is a term for connection, and in it the *Tzelem Elokim* is seen most clearly, the true essence of the *human*—then it had no dominion over him, and on the contrary, its purpose is only to serve him.

From this it is also understood regarding the matter of warmth—that its relevance in matters of the world is only for the sake of *bechirah*, but its essence is in holiness specifically.

**11.** However, there can be a state and situation of “Wine (even) in the season of Tammuz is cool to me,” meaning that even at a time when the strength of the heat of the “sun of Hashem” shines, there is in it the matter of *coolness*, and there is no warmth or vitality in matters of holiness, due to the strength of the materiality (“donkey”).

The advice for this—according to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that was revealed and publicized by the Rebbe, my father-in-law—“For you shall see a *donkey*, when you look… at your *chomer* (materiality/donkey) which is the body, and you will see, *your enemy*, that it hates the soul… and you will also see that it is *crouching under its burden* that the Holy One, blessed be He, gave to the body so that it would be refined through Torah and mitzvos, and the body is lazy in fulfilling them, and perhaps it will arise in your heart, *you shall surely refrain from leaving it alone*, so that it can fulfill its mission, for if you begin with self-mortifications to break the materiality, this is not the path where the light of Torah dwells. Rather, *you shall surely leave it with him*, to clarify the body and refine it, and not to break it with self-mortifications.”

As a preface—that the saying of this Torah by the Baal Shem Tov, who added and revealed the interpretation of the verse (which had also stood previously)—constitutes an empowerment to clarify the matter of the body. Similarly, the revelation and publication of this Torah by the Rebbe, my father-in-law—who added to explain this teaching of the Baal Shem Tov and to reveal and publicize it in various ways of publication—constitutes an additional empowerment in the work of clarifying the body.

—The Nasi of our generation, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, is the Nasi of the Baal Shem Tov, only he is in a different body, for the matter of *hishtalshelus* (evolution) does not apply to the *Maor* (luminary) himself, for the essential, “if he is, he is entirely” as he is. Therefore, our Sages said (on the verse, “And you shall come to the judge who will be in those days”) that “Yiftach in his generation is like Shmuel in his generation.” In our generation, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, is the Baal Shem Tov and the Moshe Rabbeinu of the generation.

One must add in the explanation of the aforementioned Torah:

For a “donkey,” matters of Torah and mitzvos are a “burden,” as the saying goes, “Like an ox to the yoke and like a donkey to the burden.” Moreover, sometimes it does not want to carry the burden of fulfilling the Torah and mitzvos, which is the matter of “crouching under its burden,” “he stops and does not go any further.” This is the difference between a donkey and a horse: a horse, when you strike it, continues to go further, whereas a donkey, even when you strike it, it does not help at all.

And in order to clarify and refine the donkey, so that matters of Torah and mitzvos will not be a burden to it, to the point that it will feel that this is its entire vitality—it is impossible to begin with understanding and comprehension according to intellect, for due to the strength of the materiality, it will not be able to receive this. Rather, the beginning of the work is in a manner of *kabbalas ol* specifically, and through this it will be able to be clarified and refined until, in the end, matters of Torah and mitzvos will not be a burden, but on the contrary, it will feel that this is its entire vitality.

The beginning of the work of clarifying and refining the materiality is in the month of Tammuz, when the strength of the heat of the “sun of Hashem” shines—that at the very least at this time, it should not be in the category of “Wine in the season of Tammuz is cool to me,” but rather it will feel vitality and warmth in matters of holiness, and through this, vitality and warmth in matters of holiness will be drawn out for the entire year.

**12.** In this matter, a special elevation is added in our generation in connection to the Rebbe, my father-in-law (in addition to the fact that by revealing and publicizing the aforementioned teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, he added strength to the work of clarifying the materiality)—that in the month of Tammuz, on the twelfth day, falls the (birthday and) day of the *Geulah* (redemption) of the Rebbe, my father-in-law.

As a preface:

Since in the season of Tammuz the strength of the heat of the “sun of Hashem” shines (as expressed in the strength of the heat in the physical sense), it should have been a time of revelation and joy, including and especially due to the proximity and continuation to the Giving of the Torah (the end of the forty days that Moshe was on Mount Sinai on the seventeenth of Tammuz). However, because the sin of the Golden Calf caused it (on the seventeenth of Tammuz), the opposite of revelation and joy was created. Therefore, in the future, when all sins are rectified, including the sin of the Golden Calf, it will be a time of revelation and joy.

Something similar happened in our generation—that in the month of Tammuz, a matter of revelation and joy was created through the *Geulah* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, on the twelfth of Tammuz, when they saw miracles in a tangible way. Starting from the night of the arrest, when on that night many people were arrested and were immediately sentenced to death, and during the time that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was delayed until he came to the investigator, a change occurred, and through this he was saved immediately upon his arrival at the arrest. And likewise afterwards, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, related that when they informed him of his release from prison, he saw that the death penalty was written, *rachmana litzlan*, and they crossed it out with a pen and wrote ten years in Solovki (a place of exile in Siberia), and even on this they crossed it out and wrote three years in Kostroma, until the *Geulah* in its completeness on the twelfth-thirteenth of Tammuz—all of this was an open miracle.

—Although even then, in the ultimate revelation, there were those with whom it was necessary to struggle (“*m'hot zich gemutchet mit zei*”) so that they would admit that this was an open miracle, and there are those with whom one must struggle (“*m'matert zich mit zei*”) until this very day!

In the open miracle of the *Geulah* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, on the twelfth of Tammuz, the strength of the heat of the “sun of Hashem” that is in the season of Tammuz is revealed, and through this, strength is added to the general work of clarifying the materiality—to nullify the coolness that comes from the side of the material (“Wine in the season of Tammuz is cool to me”), and to add vitality and warmth in all matters of holiness.
