Therefore, through the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the strength of the revelation of the “sun of Hashem” that is in the *Geulah* of the twelfth of Tammuz is drawn down, revealed, and shines for us, and through this, strength and might are added to clarify the “donkey,” to act upon the materiality so that the light of holiness will shine in it, until he clarifies also the materiality that is in his portion in the world, the place to which he was sent by the Moshe of our generation to make it Eretz Yisrael, by fulfilling the mission without intermingling his intellect and changing the mission (even when the *Yetzer Hara*, the “donkey,” tells him that through the change he will succeed more), as discussed at length above.

**13.** The beginning of this is on Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Tammuz, in which a blessing and empowerment are drawn down for all matters of the month of Tammuz, as in the formula of the blessing of the month: “May He renew it… for life and for peace, for joy and for gladness, for salvation and for consolation, and let us say Amen.”

One should note the change in the saying of “Amen” in the blessing of the month by the *shaliach tzibbur*—that after the words “for life and for peace,” and likewise after the words “for joy and for gladness,” they answer “Amen” immediately. This is not the case after the words “for salvation and for consolation,” where they do not answer “Amen” immediately; rather, the *shaliach tzibbur* must awaken (“*mintern*”) and announce “and let us say Amen,” and only then do they answer Amen.

One can say the hint in this—that the first blessings, “for life and for peace, for joy and for gladness,” which are only good that is seen and revealed, they answer Amen immediately. This is not the case for the blessing “for salvation and for consolation,” because it comes after sorrow and grief. Therefore, even though “From the mouth of the Most High, evil does not emerge,” nevertheless, by itself, “*fun zich alein*,” “an Amen does not answer itself”… and there is a need for a special awakening so that there will be “and let us say Amen.”

Similarly regarding the matter of the passing: even though we know that the passing is a matter of elevation for the Rebbe, my father-in-law, as is known from the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that he could have ascended in a whirlwind to the heavens, but his will was to come to the elevation of “to the dust you shall return,” and furthermore, that the elevation is not only for him but also for us (for otherwise, he certainly would not have agreed to it)—nevertheless, since in revelation this is an opposite matter, “an Amen does not answer itself”…

(The Rebbe, shlita, concluded:) “And let us say Amen”—when the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, will come and lead us toward Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon, speedily in our days, *Amen*.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Sunday, Parshas Korach, 26 Sivan, 5710

#### 115

**– At a meeting of the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch" [*](#_edn9) –**

(Unedited)

**A.** We begin with *Dvar Malchus*[1](#_ftn531):

On this day, Sunday, Parshas Korach, six years ago (in the year 5704), my father-in-law, the Rebbe, came to the beis medrash for a "Siyum Mishnayos b'al peh" that had been organized by "Machne Israel."

Among the things he said—in connection with the Siyum Mishnayos—was a teaching in the name of the Rebbe Maharash[2](#_ftn532):

The conclusion of the Mishnayos is in Seder Taharos, the conclusion of Seder Taharos is in Maseches Uktzin, and the conclusion of Maseches Uktzin is regarding honeycomb.

The concept here is that through Mishnayos, one arrives at the highest level of "purity" (*taharah*). Even then, one must know that there is still an "uktzin" (a stem or sting)—for even in good fruits, there is a "stem"—and one must refine the stem until it becomes "honey." And even then, one must know that if one remains permanently in a state and condition of honey ("he is always sweet," "a sweet one"), without change, it cannot be a "korban" ("You shall not offer up any honey"[3](#_ftn533)).

**B.** Continuing the sicha[1](#_ftn531], my father-in-law, the Rebbe, also spoke about the work of "Machne Israel" and "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch."

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, directed and managed ("*ongepirt*")—up until his histalkus, and he will continue to manage even after the histalkus—the many aspects of the work of "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," and he chose me to bring these matters into action, including the efforts to secure funds for the many expenses.

After the histalkus, there was a certain weakening in the work of the Merkaz, and there is a shortfall for the expenses; it is for this purpose that this meeting was called.

#### 116

It is not my intention to conduct a "campaign" (*appeal*), but rather to awaken the realization that we must find a way to rectify the situation.

We must know that the work of the Merkaz—both in the known and publicized matters, and in the matters that cannot be revealed—must continue with full force, and certainly without giving any room or possibility for weakening or cessation, Heaven forbid, which is the opposite of the intention and will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

Consequently, if the current situation continues, where I am forced by necessity to involve myself personally in all the matters, I will have to set aside other areas of work.

Therefore, the advice is that you should choose one person, or a committee of several people, to deal with the necessary matters, and most importantly, that they should engage in this with *chayus* and enthusiasm.

– In the aforementioned sicha[4](#_ftn534), my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said that in America there is a deficiency: people warm up quickly and cool down quickly ("one gets warm quickly and one gets cold quickly"). One must therefore strive that in this matter, the warmth should remain, etc.

[The Rebbe shlita asked if anyone among those gathered had any other advice[5](#_ftn535).]

**C.** At the conclusion of the meeting, the Rebbe shlita said:

Just as we began with *Dvar Malchus*, we must also conclude with it:

When one studies the aforementioned sicha—and likewise in many other sichos—one notices that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was accustomed (at almost every farbrengen) to mention all the Rebbes: the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Rebbe Maharash, and the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e. Now, we must add and also mention my father-in-law, the Rebbe...

(The Rebbe shlita wept, and afterwards said:) I am confident in the power of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the success of the work of "Machne Israel" and "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch" (as we see tangibly regarding the activities with the children of Africa), and with greater intensity and greater strength.

## 117

Many seek to describe and explain the virtues and greatness of the Nesi’im of Chabad in general, and of the Nasi of our generation, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in particular, regarding various matters: that he was a man of mesiras nefesh, a gaon, a man of refined middos, a tzaddik, a man of ruach hakodesh, one accustomed to miracles, and so on and so forth.

These praises are all the more significant when defined according to the teachings of Chassidus—what constitutes mesiras nefesh, what constitutes a gaon, and so on.

Yet, in all of this, the essential point is missing. Furthermore, not only is this the essential point, but it is especially important because it is the most relevant, particularly to us—the community of his Chassidim and those bound to him. And that is: the fact that he is the Nasi, and the Nasi of Chabad.

For a Nasi in general is called the "head" of the thousands of Yisrael; he is the aspect of the head and the brain in relation to them, and from him they draw their sustenance and vitality. Through attachment to him, they are connected and unified with their source, high above.

There are several types of Nesi’im : there are those whose influence is in the aspect of penimiyus (internalization), and those whose influence is in the aspect of makif (encompassing). Within this itself, there are distinctions: whether they influenced through the revealed Torah or the hidden Torah, or both together; whether they taught the paths of avodah and Chassidus; whether they drew down physical blessings, and so on.

There are those who possessed several of these aspects, or even all of them.

This has been the nature of the leadership of the Nesi’im of Chabad from the Alter Rebbe until my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and including him: they encompassed all types and distinctions. They influenced through penimiyus and makif, through Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim, in both spiritual and physical matters. Consequently, their connection with those who belonged to them encompassed all 613 limbs of the soul and body of those who were connected.

## 118

Each and every one of us must know—that is, deepen his understanding and fix his thoughts upon this—that he is the Nasi and the head. From him and through him come all influences in both physical and spiritual matters, and through attachment to him (and he has already instructed in his letters how and through what one becomes attached), we are connected and unified with the source, and the source of the source, up to the highest heights.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*3 Tammuz, 5710*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Chukas, 9 Tammuz, 5710

#### 119

(Unedited)

**1.** Regarding the day of Shabbos, it is stated in the Zohar[1](#_ftn539) that "from it all the days are blessed." This means that all the days of the week following Shabbos receive blessing and vitality from the Shabbos that preceded them.

This is one of the reasons for the custom that a groom is called to the Torah before his wedding (not on the day of the reading closest to the wedding, but) specifically on Shabbos[2](#_ftn540) — because the day of Shabbos includes all the days of the week that are blessed from it.

As we stand on the Shabbos before 12-13 Tammuz, from which 12-13 Tammuz is blessed, and consequently, it is already connected to 12-13 Tammuz — it is appropriate to begin with the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, from the Festival of Redemption 12-13 Tammuz of last year, and to explain the connection and relevance to the Shabbos preceding it, Parshas Chukas (and also in connection to the Aliyah to the Torah on this Shabbos, in this Parsha).

**2.** In the Sicha of 13 Tammuz last year[3](#_ftn541), the Rebbe, my father-in-law, spoke regarding the matter of life — long life, true life, life without interruption (eternal life). He explained this in terms of avodah: that in addition to the fact that every person lives for himself, he also gives life to others ("not only does one live oneself, but one also brings others to life"), and he concludes: "True life is kedushah, and kedushah is Ein Sof."

By way of introduction — since every matter is by Divine Providence [as is known the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov[4](#_ftn542) that Hashem brings forth a wind from His treasuries to roll a leaf or a straw, etc., meaning, that Divine Providence applies even to the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms, and certainly to the human species, and all the more so to the Jewish people who are the crown of glory of the entire creation[5](#_ftn543), and even more so to the Nasi of Israel upon whom all matters depend, as stated in Rashi’s commentary on the Parsha of the week[6](#_ftn544) that "the Nasi

#### 120

is everything"], it follows that the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, regarding *eternal life* that were spoken specifically on 12-13 Tammuz *5709* (and not in the years prior, 5708 or 5707) — before his passing on 10 Shevat 5710 — are certainly by Divine Providence.

— The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related[7](#_ftn545) that when saying the Maamar on Rosh Hashanah 5687, before the imprisonment, "it spoke itself" (he was moved to speak) regarding the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that Divine Providence applies even to every single detail of the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms, without him knowing the reason for speaking about this (since this matter was not relevant to the content of the Maamar). He added that were it not for this ("had he not spoken this"), he does not know if he would have been able to endure and survive the imprisonment.

The same can be said in our case: On the *last* Festival of Redemption in his lifetime in this world, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, found it necessary to clarify ("to warn") and state that matters of kedushah are eternal. He added to explain in detail (so there would be no room to err in his intent) the matter of long life, true life that has no interruption, so that we would not think as it appears to physical eyes, Heaven forbid (for such a reality does not exist at all in kedushah), but rather we should know that even after the passing, there exists the matter of life without interruption, eternal life, with the Nasi of the generation, and through him, eternal life is drawn down to the entire generation. Therefore, even now, everyone can and must (not only live themselves, but also) bring others to life in matters of kedushah[8](#_ftn546).

**3.** Based on the above, that all matters are by Divine Providence — we must explain the allusion to this matter in the Parsha of the week[9](#_ftn547):

In the Parsha of the week, we speak of the Parah Adumah (Red Heifer), through which purification is achieved from the most severe impurity, the impurity of death, regarding which "the face of Moshe turned pale" because "he did not know how its purification would be achieved"[10](#_ftn548), until Hashem said to him, "This is the statute (chukas) of the Torah... and they shall take to you a red heifer..."

Its meaning in spiritual avodah — that the impurity of death (the lack of vitality) indicates a state and situation where the dveikus to Hashem, the Source of Life, is hidden, as it is written[11](#_ftn549), "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are alive, all of you, today." The purification from this state and situation (to effect the revelation of

#### 121

vitality through one's dveikus to Hashem) is the concept of "chukah," "This is the *chukas* of the Torah," and it is achieved specifically through the power of Moshe, as it is written[12](#_ftn550), "And they shall take *to you* a red heifer," "It is forever called by your name, the heifer that Moshe made in the desert." This means that it is in the power of Moshe to take a red heifer — a physical heifer in the literal sense, and in addition, also (a heifer that is) red, which indicates the Gevuros, the intensity of warmth ("koch") in physicality and materiality — and not only to elevate the "red heifer" itself, but furthermore, that it is in the power of Moshe to make from the red heifer the ashes through which there will be purification from the most severe impurity.

Now, the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made were divided into three parts: the first part, for the townspeople and all those who needed to be purified; the second part, for the High Priests to sanctify from it for other heifers; and the third part, placed for safekeeping[13](#_ftn551). In other words, the purification from the impurity of death is not only from the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made, but also from the ashes of other heifers (nine heifers) that were made after the time of Moshe. However, for the making of the other heifers, they needed the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made, from which the High Priests sanctify for the making of other heifers, to the extent that even for the making of the tenth heifer by Melech HaMoshiach[14](#_ftn552), they will need to sanctify from the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made, which exists forever[15](#_ftn553).

And its meaning in avodah — that the action of Moshe (including the *atpashuta d'Moshe*—the extension of Moshe—in every single generation[16](#_ftn554)) to reveal the vitality of dveikus to Hashem in every single Jew (even one who is in a state and situation of the impurity of death), continues and is drawn down in all the generations that follow, through those who engage in this (the High Priests who make other heifers) being permeated with the power of Moshe (by sanctifying with the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made).

**4.** We must add to this — based on what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh[17](#_ftn555) (in the name of the Tikkunim[18](#_ftn556)): "Regarding Moshe Rabbeinu, peace be upon him, that after his passing, his light spreads in every generation to six hundred thousand souls, like the sun that shines beneath the earth to six hundred thousand stars":

The sun exists and shines even during the night hours — in the second half of the globe (beneath the earth). Moreover, even in the half of the globe where it is not present at night, it shines there too through the six hundred thousand stars, for the light of the stars is also the light of the sun that is shining now through the stars. That is to say, it is not just that during the daylight hours

#### 122

the stars received the light of the sun and now (during the night hours) they shine on their own, but rather that the light which the stars shine during the night hours is the light of the sun.

The analogy in the subject matter, regarding Moshe Rabbeinu, and the *atpashuta d'Moshe* in every generation, up to the Moshe of our generation, the Rebbe, my father-in-law — that even now he exists and shines just as before (like the sun that exists and shines even during the night hours). If we were to walk together with him, we would see that he shines with all the intensity as before (and, on the contrary, in an even more elevated manner). However, since he has ascended above from elevation to elevation, and we (did not walk with him, but) remained in our place, therefore he is not visible to our physical eyes (just as at night one does not see the sun). Nevertheless, even in this state, his light spreads to all the Jewish people, whose totality is six hundred thousand souls, and through them, he shines throughout the entire world (just as the sun shines beneath the earth to six hundred thousand stars, as mentioned, that the light of the sun itself shines through the medium of the stars).

[And even though we do not feel the spreading of his light — it has already been explained above[19](#_ftn557) the saying of the Rebbe, my grandfather, that the horse's thought about straw does not negate the existence of the angels!...]

This matter is also reflected in the *Nigleh* (the revealed) Torah (like all matters in the *Pnimiyus*—the inner dimension—of the Torah) — regarding the purification of the impure from death through the ashes of the Parah Adumah — that through the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made, they sanctify to make other heifers. That is to say, even when it is not possible to sprinkle from the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made himself, but rather from the ashes of other heifers made thereafter, the ashes of those other heifers are also made through the fact that they sanctify from the ashes that Moshe made, specifically through the power of Moshe.

**5.** Based on this, we can explain the relevance to the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, in the aforementioned Sicha regarding the matter of life, "not only does one live oneself, but one also brings others to life":

When one encounters a Jew who is in a state and situation of the impurity of death, in whom one does not see the vitality of kedushah — one must purify him, bring him to life with the vitality of kedushah. This is in the power and ability (and consequently, the obligation) of everyone, because Moshe Rabbeinu (the Moshe of our generation) gave and gives him from the ashes of his heifer ("Moshe Rabbeinu gave you and gives you from the ashes of his heifer"). Consequently, his action is through the power of Moshe — "It is forever called by your name, the heifer that Moshe made."

#### 123

We should add an explanation regarding the precision of Rashi's language, "the heifer that Moshe made *in the desert*" — for seemingly, what does this teach us? Everyone knows that Moshe was in the desert, and certainly the heifer was made there. This teaches us that even for a Jew who is in a place and level of a *desert*, "a land of serpents, scorpions, and thirst where there is no water"[20](#_ftn558), one can effect the matter of purification. And to such an extent, that the heifer that *Moshe* made, from which the priests sanctify for the making of all the heifers thereafter, was *in the desert* specifically, where the need for the matter of purification is emphasized, unlike in Jerusalem, where they do not leave the dead overnight[21](#_ftn559), and similarly in Eretz Yisrael as a whole (and especially according to the Sages[22](#_ftn560) that Jerusalem is destined to spread throughout all of Eretz Yisrael), but specifically in the Diaspora, which is in the category of a "desert" in relation to Eretz Yisrael and Jerusalem.

Furthermore:

In addition to the fact that through the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made, his own purification is achieved, one must also enable him so that he himself can burn a heifer and make from it ashes to purify others, that he himself should be an influence on others to bring them to life in matters of kedushah, "moistening in order to moisten others"[23](#_ftn561).

And this matter, too, is done specifically through the power of Moshe — that a portion of the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made is used by the High Priests to sanctify for other heifers, for they sanctify the one making the heifer with the ashes of the first heifer that Moshe made. The analogy in avodah is that the continuation of his action to purify others (after he has become pure himself) is also through the power of Moshe.

However, since due to the great preoccupation with the action upon others ("bringing others to life"), to purify them, and even to make them "moistening in order to moisten others," it is possible that one might forget about oneself — there is a need to warn also regarding one's own avodah ("living oneself"), as in the saying of the Rebbe, my father-in-law[24](#_ftn562), "One must also not forget about oneself."

And this matter, too, is alluded to in the ashes of the heifer that Moshe made — that a portion of it was placed "for safekeeping," to teach you that in addition to the action with others using the part of the ashes

#### 124

with which the impure are purified, and from which they sanctify for other heifers, there is also a part that is placed for safekeeping, in which is alluded the avodah with oneself.

**6.** The lesson from this — that one must engage in influencing others, "not only does one live oneself, but one also brings others to life," and as the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, continue in the aforementioned Sicha[25](#_ftn563), that everyone can influence two or three minyanim of the Jewish people!

[The Rebbe turned to one of those present and said to him:]

When someone has the power to influence others, one must know that this power was given to him for the purpose of influencing in matters of kedushah. Even when the person being influenced by him is thinking about a different matter that he could receive from him, one must utilize the fact that he is being influenced by him in order to influence him in matters of kedushah.

— Surely he will not mind if I tell about his first action in public communal work (before he reached his current status and position where his name goes before him), which was in matters of Chassidus:

It was at the time when the Rebbe, my father-in-law, lived in Warsaw, and he traveled from his home for several weeks. At that time, there were some Chassidim who copied a key to the drawer where the manuscripts were kept, and they found someone who was willing to take the manuscripts for them in order to copy them, and they gave them to the aforementioned to copy the manuscripts.

This was his first action in public communal work — by virtue of which a copy remained of many manuscripts that were burned (Heaven forbid) later on.

— Once[26](#_ftn564), many manuscripts were burned at the Tzemach Tzedek's, and when it became clear to him that the Chassidim did not have copies, he cried out and said: "Gewald," why didn't you steal the manuscripts (to copy them)? If you had stolen them, I too would have benefited from it!...

He must therefore remember that his first action in public communal work was in matters of Chassidus, and accordingly, he must strive to utilize the power of influence over others for matters of kedushah.

**7.** We should add that the above (regarding the drawing down of eternal vitality in matters of kedushah) is also connected with the Aliyah to the Torah of the groom on the Shabbos before the wedding:

#### 125

The Aliyah to the Torah is a matter of drawing down an additional eternal vitality of kedushah (in addition to the kedushah that is drawn down from Above due to the nature of the day of Shabbos, which is "holy and enduring"[27](#_ftn565)) — as emphasized in the text of the blessing after the Aliyah to the Torah: "*And eternal life* He planted within us," through the fact that "He gave us the Torah of truth," because true life without interruption ("eternal life") is from the side of *kedushah* ("Torah of truth"), which is *Ein Sof*.

Therefore, the Aliyah to the Torah on the Shabbos before the wedding is an empowerment for the wedding — that it should be in the manner of an "everlasting edifice"[28](#_ftn566), a generation of the upright will be blessed, children and grandchildren engaged in Torah and Mitzvos[29](#_ftn567), as is known[30](#_ftn568) that through this, the power of the Ein Sof that is in created beings is revealed.

And there is a special empowerment for one who merits to be called to the Torah in the room of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, where he prayed and studied, and where he connected with the *Yechidah* aspect of every Jew whom he received for *Yechidus*[31](#_ftn569) — through which there is an even greater addition in the matter of "*And eternal life* He planted within us," true life without interruption, being permeated with kedushah, which is Ein Sof.

*

**8.** Regarding the Redemption of 12 Tammuz — the Rebbe, my father-in-law, writes in his well-known letter[32](#_ftn570): "It was not only me that Hashem redeemed on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, those who observe Mitzvos, and also those who are called by the name of Israel."

Redemption — does not exist without the preceding imprisonment. And since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, writes that the Redemption is for the entire Jewish people, it must be that the imprisonment was also a general matter that applied to the entire Jewish people.

And the purpose of the imprisonment and redemption — is not only that the undesirable state of the imprisonment should be nullified like before the imprisonment (for if so, what is the benefit of the imprisonment and the redemption?), but rather that through this, a greater elevation is added compared to the state and situation that existed before the imprisonment.

This is similar to what is explained in the discourses of Chassidus[33](#_ftn571) regarding the purpose of the Tzimtzum for the sake of revelation, that it is not for the sake of the revelation of the light that was shining before the Tzimtzum, for if so, what is the benefit of the Tzimtzum? Rather, it is for the sake of the revelation of a more elevated light, whose drawing down is through the avodah after the Tzimtzum specifically, and were it not for the Tzimtzum, it could not have shone at all.

#### 126

Likewise, regarding the breaking of the vessels and the sin of the Tree of Knowledge — that specifically through the avodah of *Birurim* (refining) thereafter, one draws down an additional light, etc. The analogy in avodah — regarding the matter of Teshuvah, that in addition to the rectification of the undesirable matters in such a way that no trace remains at all, a greater elevation is added compared to the state and situation from before, to the extent that where *Baalei Teshuvah* stand, even perfect *Tzaddikim* cannot stand[34](#_ftn572).

And similarly regarding the imprisonment and the redemption:

By way of introduction — that certainly even before the imprisonment there was an elevated state and situation in matters of avodah (even though there was still a need to refine and purify the matters that were done with ulterior motives, etc., or to complete the matters that had not yet been done), and therefore all of Israel were worthy of the influence of abundant goodness, and there was no place for the matter of suffering (imprisonment),

— And as explained in Torah Or[35](#_ftn573) regarding the general matter of the sufferings of this world, that "it is not because of punishment that one is not worthy to sit in the tranquility of this world, for we find with Nebuchadnezzar[36](#_ftn574) that because he took three steps for the honor of Hashem, they decreed for him kingship over the entire world and for his descendants after him for three generations, and there is no person in Israel who has not honored the Place with this, and all the good of this world is worthy for him" —

And nevertheless, after the imprisonment and the redemption, the general avodah must be (in addition to the refinement and purification of the matters that were done with ulterior motives, etc., or the completion of the matters that had not yet been done) in a more elevated manner, and even to an incomparable elevation.

## From the Sicha of 12 Tammuz, 5710

#### 127

**A.** Regarding miracles and their blessings, we find several levels of distinction, ordered from highest to lowest:

Highest of all is a miracle performed for oneself.

Below that is a miracle performed for one’s father. This applies whether the miracle occurred before one was born—which is still a lower level than a miracle performed for oneself—or after one was born. In the latter case, due to the connection between father and son, the miracle is attributed to the son (more so than in the categories that follow), as a miracle performed for the father is considered as if it were performed for the son—that is, for the part of the son that resides within the father.

Below that is a miracle performed for one’s *rebbe*. This is because "a son is the leg of his father," and while a father brings one into the life of this world and partially into the life of the World to Come, the *rebbe* brings one solely into the life of the World to Come. Furthermore, the father is certainly [a father] according to Torah law by virtue of the presumption of lineage, whereas the World to Come that the *rebbe* provides is a matter of uncertainty, for it is possible that the Torah study was not performed as it should have been (as explained in the *maamar* of 12 Tammuz).

#### 128

Below that is a miracle performed for a specific individual. The connection to a specific individual is more distant, to the point that it is possible there is no manifest connection or relationship between them at all, other than the fact that one *believes* that because he is a specific (general) person, he presumably has a connection to him as well.

**B.** However, a miracle performed for the *Nasi* of the generation is not like a miracle performed for a specific individual, for one’s *rebbe*, or for one’s father. Rather, it is truly as if it were performed for oneself. This is because the connection of the *Nasi* with the members of his generation is not a connection of *two* separate entities (not even like the connection of father and son); rather, they are one single body: all the members of the generation are the individual limbs, drawing and receiving their vitality from the *Nasi*—the head.

[More specifically:

Just as when vitality is channeled from the head to the limbs, it is not possible to divide and say that there are matters for which the limb receives vitality from the head, and other matters for which it has vitality of its own—rather, the entire vitality of the limb is from the head—so too is it regarding the channeling of vitality from the *Nasi* to the entire generation: in all matters, they receive vitality and influence from the *Nasi*.

As we find in the generation of Moshe, when he said, "Where will I get meat?"—because of the greatness of his level, he could not constrict himself to channel meat (even for the generation of the desert, who were a "generation of knowledge"). The *Ribono shel Olam* said to him, "Gather for Me seventy men... and I will take of the spirit that is upon you and place it upon them." Seemingly, what is the necessity that even the channeling of meat, which is below the level of Moshe, must be through him specifically? Because any influence, in any matter whatsoever, cannot be except through Moshe, just as the channeling of vitality to all the limbs is only through the head.

And so it is in every generation—for "there is an extension of Moshe in every generation," and furthermore, "there is no generation that does not have one like Moshe," and especially in the generation of *Moshiach*,

#### 129

as it is stated in *Tikkunei Zohar* that then Moshe himself will be present—that the channeling of vitality in all matters whatsoever is through the *Nasi* specifically.]

Furthermore, it can be said that a miracle performed for the *Nasi* is even more elevated (also regarding the members of his generation) than a miracle performed for oneself—like the superiority of the head over the rest of the limbs. In addition to the head being more elevated, it is also the source that channels vitality to all the limbs, and *this very vitality*, while it is still in the head, is more spiritual and elevated than when it has already been drawn down into the limbs.

There is another advantage in a miracle performed for the *Nasi* over a miracle performed for oneself: regarding miracles, we find two opinions: "How great is this person..." versus "How degraded is this person..." and we also find that "they deduct from his merits." But a miracle performed for the *Nasi*—the *heart* of all Israel, who is "tender... clean (of waste), and refined of all"—is certainly for the good and for the positive in every detail.

**C.** Based on this, we can explain the reason why the *Chag HaGeulah* of 12 and 13 Tammuz is called "the *Moed* of *Moadim*":

*Moed* means a time when a miracle occurred. 12 Tammuz is the general *moed* and miracle—the miracle of the head of Israel, from which all *moadim* and private miracles are drawn.

Therefore, this is a *moed* that concerns *all the children of Israel*—in the words of the *Rebbe* in his letter for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz: "It was not only me that the *Ribono shel Olam* redeemed on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, who observe the *mitzvos*, and also those who are called by the name of Israel." And it concerns *all times and places*—similar to what we find regarding the Exodus from Egypt, that "if the *Ribono shel Olam* had not taken our forefathers out of Egypt, then we and our children and our children's children..."

\*

**D.** It was discussed previously regarding the words of the *Rebbe* on 13 Tammuz of last year concerning long life, true life without interruption, since matters of *kedushah* are *Ein Sof*. The reason he spoke about this on 13 Tammuz *5709* (and not

#### 130

in the year 5708 or 5707) is that it was the last *Chag HaGeulah* before 10 Shevat 5710, at which time there is a need to clarify ("*bavorenen*") the matter of eternal life.

More specifically:

Regarding the word "life" (*chaim*), one could interpret it with simple explanations (*peshtlach*) that it refers to Torah and *mitzvos*, which "are our life," and likewise other matters that are called life, as our Sages said, "Ten are called 'living'." Therefore, he adds "long life"—for everyone knows that the meaning of "long life" (as we say in the text of the prayers, *Selichos*, and the like) is life *literally*, in the physical sense.

And he continues and adds, "true life, life without interruption":

Even regarding long life, and even life without interruption, it is possible that it is so by *chance*—that is, *in practice* there was no interruption, but it could have been otherwise. And since in this case we are speaking about a situation that to physical eyes appears to have been interrupted, and furthermore, according to *Shulchan Aruch* one must now perform certain matters, etc., therefore he emphasizes "true life, life without interruption"—true and eternal life in which an interruption is *not applicable*.

The reason for this—as he continues and concludes—is because true life is *kedushah*, and *kedushah* is *Ein Sof*.

—The truth is that this matter is understood from what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*: "The life of the *Tzaddik* is not physical life, but spiritual life, which is *emunah*, *yirah*, and *ahavah*." For regarding spiritual life in general, and *emunah*, *yirah*, and *ahavah* in particular, everyone understands (even a coarse intellect) that the concept of death is not applicable, and they are not in that category at all. However, this matter was written many years ago, and no one contemplates it, unlike the matter that the *Rebbe* spoke about in the recent period, which has now been published in print.

**E.** From this it is understood that even now we must fulfill the *shlichus* of the *Rebbe* just as before.

There are those who think there is a difference: Before, one had to fulfill the *shlichus* that the *Rebbe* imposed upon him, because the *Rebbe* could call him for *yechidus* or write him a letter: "How is it possible? I sent you on a certain *shlichus* and gave you the strength, and why are you not fulfilling the *shlichus*!" But now—he thinks to himself—he can do as he pleases.

To this, the *Rebbe* says that life is eternal, and consequently, all the matters of the *shlichus* and the strength given by him remain in their full force. And even now, he continues to demand with full force ("*mit di zelbe shtrengkeit*") the fulfillment of the *shlichus* he already sent, and he will continue to send!

—There are those who are astonished by these words. But the truth is that we find in the *Tanach*: "And a letter came to him from Eliyahu the Prophet"—many years after he ascended in a whirlwind to heaven! And if so, what is the astonishment that even now the *Rebbe* will continue to send?!... As for the manner of notification—the *Rebbe* has his ways, and we do not need to worry about how the *Rebbe* will notify us; we can rely on him!

**F.** And similarly regarding study in the *Rebbe's* *yeshiva*:

There are those who previously studied in the *Rebbe's* *yeshiva*, and now they have done a great foolishness and left.

[Even those who cloak this in the guise of the *mitzvah* of honoring one's father and mother—this is simply foolishness. For in the same *Shulchan Aruch* where the obligation of honoring one's father and mother is stated, it is also stated that regarding Torah study, one should not take into account the honor of one's father and mother. And they also said that "his lost object and his father's lost object—his own takes precedence," and all the more so regarding a spiritual loss, where the *Neshama* is liable to be lost in the body and the *Nefesh HaBehamis*—in such a situation, one should not take into account the honor of one's father and mother.]

One must know the greatness of the privilege of studying in the *Rebbe's* *yeshiva*, and those who have merited this must thank and praise the *Ribono shel Olam* for the greatness of the privilege that has fallen to their lot, and hold onto it with full force. And those who have done the great foolishness and left—it would be better for them to return and ask the administration, and perhaps, just perhaps, they will be admitted.

**G.** Each and every one of the students, the *mekusharim*, and the *Chassidim* must know that he is one of the "people of Moshe," and this matter is for eternity and for all time, for him and for his generations, until the coming of *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*.

And furthermore—even those who previously did not have a connection to the *Rebbe* can now become *Chassidim* of the *Rebbe*.

The point of the matter is that there is no change at all between before and now.

—If there is a change, it is only *for the better*, as explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that after the passing, *it is easier* to receive the influence from the life of the *Tzaddik*, since they are not within a physical vessel and garment.

#### 132

And similarly regarding the channeling of blessings to all those who are engaged and will be engaged in the *avodah* of the *Rebbe*—that now, after the passing, when he is not limited by the limitations of the physical body, all the blessings are drawn down *with abundant influence*.

—The *Rebbe* once said that he was always a debtor, but he never went bankrupt ("*er iz keinmol nit geven bankrupt*"), *chas v'shalom*. Now the *Rebbe* is paying all his debts, all the blessings he promised in general, and especially to those who are engaged and will be engaged in his *avodah*, and as mentioned, the drawing down of blessings now is with abundant influence.

**H.** This situation—that there is no change at all, but rather for the better—is from the side of the *Rebbe*. In addition to this, we must also do something ("*m'darf alein oich epes ton*").

The connection of the *Rebbe* with *Chassidim* is in such a way that from the side of the *Rebbe*, all matters are drawn down. The *Rebbe* wants to draw down, for it is the nature of the Good to do good, and more than the calf wants to suck, the cow wants to nurse. However, there is a need for the initiation of one's own *avodah*, and then the *Rebbe* assists, to the point of assistance that is incomparable to one's own *avodah*.

Similar to what is told in the *Midrash* that R' Chanina ben Dosa wanted to dedicate something and had nothing, and he found a large stone but could not lift it, until angels appeared to him and said, "We will lift your stone to Jerusalem, provided that you place your hand and finger with us." He placed his hand and finger with them, and they were found standing in Jerusalem. That is to say, even though the lifting of the stone was not according to his strength at all, but specifically by the strength of the angels, nevertheless, the angels stipulated with him that he should place his hand and finger with them. The reason for this is because the intention is that there should be *one's own avodah*, and through one's own *avodah*, even by giving only a finger, they assist him to bring the stone—the "heart of stone"—and dedicate it to Heaven, a *kedushas haguf* or at the very least a *kedushas damim*.

**I.** And it should be added that the example of *hekdesh* applies to the general matter of the connection to the *Rebbe*:

One who dedicates one limb—if it is a limb upon which the soul depends, the *kedushah* takes effect on the entire body.

#### 133

And this can be explained in two ways: (a) The taking effect of the *kedushah* from the side of the one who dedicates is only on this limb, but since the vitality of the entire body depends on this limb, the *kedushah* spreads (automatically) throughout the entire body (and seemingly this is what the language of the *Gemara* implies, "the *kedushah* spreads to the whole"). (b) Since the vitality of the entire body depends on this limb, it is as if he dedicated the entire body from the outset (and in the *Shas* it explains the reason for the laws). And even though he says explicitly that he is dedicating only this limb, it is like one who says, "I am a *nazir* on the condition that I will not offer the three sacrifices," for by saying "I am a *nazir*," the obligation of the *nazir* sacrifices takes effect upon him, and he cannot stipulate afterwards that he should be exempt. And similarly in our case, it becomes as if he dedicated the entire body from the outset, and he can no longer remove the *kedushah* from the rest of the limbs except for this limb.

And similarly regarding the connection between a *Chassid* and the *Rebbe*—that even when it is a matter of a private affair (one limb), it is a limb upon which the soul depends, both from the side of the *Rebbe* and from the side of the *Chassid*:

When one comes to the *Rebbe* to ask about a spiritual or physical matter, it is not because the *Rebbe* is an expert in this specific matter, but because the *Rebbe* is a *neshama klalis*, like the head that includes the vitality of all the limbs of the body (as mentioned in section B), including regarding this private matter.

And the answer of the *Rebbe*—even regarding this private matter—is in such a way that he applies himself ("*er git zich op*") with his *neshama*.

—And certainly not in a way of "automatically," for among *Chassidim* in general, the concept of "automatically" is not applicable, as per the saying of the *Tzemach Tzedek* that *Chassidim* must be "*avodah'dike yirei shamayim*," and not "*b'milah'dike yirei shamayim*."

And his intention in this is that through this private matter, he will be able to elevate and sanctify his soul (of the private individual) as much as possible ("*wifl es is nor meglich*").

[And how much is possible—it is stated in *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu* that each and every one of Israel can say, "When will my deeds reach the deeds of my forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov?"]

And since this is so, then every private matter is in the category of dedicating a limb upon which the soul depends, through which his entire existence becomes *kadosh*.

#### 134

And since the *Rebbe*, the head who rules and governs all the limbs, has dedicated his soul—then he has no choice!—but it is possible that it will be for the better, and for this the *Rebbe* has acted so that it will be "with kindness and mercy." The only choice is whether to begin this today or to delay until tomorrow, and since one can begin today, why delay until tomorrow?!...

Today—the birthday and the *Chag HaGeulah* of the *Rebbe*—is a time prepared for making good resolutions in all the matters mentioned, and through this, one receives all the blessings for success in physical and spiritual matters.

\*

**J.** In the *maamar* of 12 Tammuz, it is explained that Torah study must be with *bitul*, by preceding it with the *avodah* of *tefillah*. But if one is not *batel*, then one is not a vessel for the truth of the Torah, and then the study of Torah causes *yeshus* (self-centeredness) in him. And when one studies Torah with *yeshus*, one descends, *chas v'shalom*, from level to level, etc.

And he details several levels in this—"that he feels himself excessively... that is, he takes credit for himself that he studies much Torah and there is created in him an existence of 'yesh' and he is important in his own eyes... until even his study is afterwards also to be arrogant, and to be considered in the eyes of those who see, or to be contentious and the like, and he can also descend afterwards even further, *chas v'shalom*, until it becomes for him a potion of death, etc."

And here we see ("*ich vil aich weizen*") the greatness of the precision in the language of the *Rebbe* in every single word:

First of all—seemingly, he could have said in short that when one studies without *bitul*, the Torah becomes a potion of death, *chas v'shalom*, similar to the language of our Sages—which he brings in the *maamar*—"If one merits, it becomes a potion of life; if one does not merit, it becomes a potion of death."

And the explanation for this—as the *Rebbe* explained the parable of a man wandering in a forest—is that it is not sudden, that just now he was walking on the king's highway and suddenly finds himself in the thickets of the forest in a place of wild beasts. Rather, the beginning is in a way that he deviates from the king's highway by only a hair's breadth, and over time—if

#### 135

he does not return to the straight path but continues in this direction—the "hair's breadth" becomes "the ropes of a wagon of sin."

And similarly in our case, the beginning is only from the lack of *bitul*, and from this comes *yeshus*, etc., until eventually one can come to a standing and situation where it becomes the opposite of a potion of life, *chas v'shalom*.

**K.** And within this itself there are several levels—as explained in the details of the expressions in the *maamar*:

The beginning of *yeshus* is "that *he takes credit for himself* that he studies much Torah and there is created in him an existence of 'yesh' and he is important in his own eyes." That is, the study itself is as it should be, but he takes credit for himself. As the *Rebbe* told about one of the young *Chassidim* who prayed at length for several hours, and afterwards one of the elder *Chassidim* said about him: "*Zich alein hot er shoin moichel geven*"—that this is the matter of taking credit for oneself. And this *yeshus* is from the *kelipah nogah* of *Atzilus*, which is called "*Re'u Mah*" (See what), meaning that he takes credit for himself for his *bitul*, and consequently, it is not true *bitul*, and therefore the Torah cannot ascend to the world of *Atzilus* where "He and His attributes are one," but remains in the world of *Beriah*.

Below that—"that even *his study* is afterwards also *to be arrogant*." That is, not only is the study as it should be and he only takes credit for himself, but the study itself is also to be arrogant. But nevertheless, this is only in his own eyes, "*bei zich in tzimmer*," saying that one must know one's own virtues, and as is known the saying that just as one must know one's own faults, so one must know one's own virtues, "*iz farwos zol er take nit wissen ma'alos atzmo*?!" And even though he lacks in the *avodah* of *tefillah*, this is not relevant—he argues—to Torah study, for it is explicitly stated in the *Gemara* (and ruled as *halacha* in *Shulchan Aruch*, and so rules the *Alter Rebbe* in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*) "A person should always engage in Torah and *mitzvos* even if not for their own sake, for from 'not for their own sake' one comes to 'for their own sake'." And since these calculations are between him and himself, and not to others, this is *yeshus* that is from the *kelipah nogah* of the world of *Beriah* (and not below that), which is mostly evil.

#### 136

Below that—that his study is also in order "to be considered *in the eyes of those who see*," and this *yeshus* is from the *kelipah nogah* of the world of *Yetzirah*, which is half and half, and therefore it is not only in his own eyes, but also in the eyes of others.

Below that—"*to be contentious and the like*," meaning, not only that through his study he will be considered in the eyes of those who see, but that he studies in order to show his greatness by rejecting the words of his colleague, and furthermore (which is why he adds "and the like") that he rejects his colleague on a matter that is not true, saying that his colleague's innovation is certainly not true, and therefore, first of all, one must reject his words in any way possible, with whatever is in his hand, even on a matter that is not true, and afterwards he will find the true explanation... that in addition to the fault in the contentiousness itself, there is also the detriment that he introduces a matter that is not true into the Torah. And this matter is from the *kelipah nogah* of the world of *Asiyah*, where the majority is evil and the wicked prevail.

And afterwards he adds, "and he can also descend afterwards even further, *chas v'shalom*, until it becomes for him a *potion of death*, etc."—that this matter is from the *sitra achra* entirely.

And all this begins, as mentioned, from the lack of *bitul* in Torah study, even when the study is not to be arrogant, but he studies from fear of the lash, or he studies just because, not for its own sake and not not for its own sake (as explained in *Tanya*), but nevertheless, since *bitul* is lacking, the study is done in a way of *yeshus*, etc., until he comes to a standing and situation of the opposite of a potion of life, *chas v'shalom*.

**L.** And in order for Torah study to be with *bitul*, in which case the study is a "potion of life"—which is a matter of healing in addition to the matter of nourishment that is in the Torah (as explained in the *maamar*)—this is through preceding it with the *avodah* of *tefillah*:

And as a preface—before the *Baal Shem Tov* there was the matter of fasts and self-afflictions, but the *Baal Shem Tov* innovated [that one should not break the body, but refine and purify it, like the well-known Torah on the interpretation of the verse "If you see the donkey of your enemy crouching under its burden... you shall surely help with him," that the *avodah* must be in the refinement and purification of the body, so that it will not be "crouching under its burden," but on the contrary, "as a donkey for a burden," and furthermore] that the *avodah* must be specifically with *joy*.

And this matter is emphasized also regarding the *avodah* of *tefillah*—not only the preface of "one should not stand to pray except with a heavy head," but also the preface of "one should not stand to pray... except with the *joy of a mitzvah*."

And from this it is understood also regarding the matter of *bitul* that is achieved through the *avodah* of *tefillah*, that the *avodah* is not in the nullification of his existence, but in the *connection to the Ribono shel Olam* (the content of the matter of *tefillah*), and this matter is drawn down and permeates also into Torah study, so that it is recognized and felt by him that the Torah is the *wisdom and will of the Ribono shel Olam*, and then the study is not from *yeshus* but from true *bitul* to the Torah.

**M.** This matter concerns especially the students of the *yeshivos*—regardless of whether they study in a *Chassidic yeshiva* or not—that they must know and remember always, "I have set the *Ribono shel Olam* before me always," that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*.

And in the language of our Sages, that Torah study must be with the preface of the blessing of the Torah, "Bless with Torah first"—to remember the "Giver of the Torah"—that through this, the importance and greatness of the Torah is recognized and felt by him, that it is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*.

And especially when he contemplates that the Torah is in a state of incomparable elevation relative to the worlds, for the creation of the world is with only two letters, as our Sages said, "With the *yud* the World to Come was created, with the *hei* this world was created," and above the letters of speech in general are the letters of thought, and above the letters of thought are the *middos*, and above the *middos* are the *mochin*, which is the matter of the Torah, the wisdom of the *Ribono shel Olam*, for He and His wisdom are one.

\*

**N.** It was already discussed previously regarding the need to rectify the matter of traveling on *shlichus* during the summer period, since last year it was not as it should have been. And although "one does not cry over the past," the precision in this is that "one does not cry" specifically, but there must certainly be a rectification of the matter.

#### 138

All those who travel on *shlichus* must know that together with them travels the *Rebbe*,

—I am not saying that "a piece of a *Rebbe*" travels with them, for every essence is indivisible, but the entire *Rebbe* ("*der ganzer Rebbe*") travels with each one of them—

And consequently, they must know the greatness of the responsibility in the matter—that aside from the very fact that they are troubling (as it were) the *Rebbe* to travel with them wherever they go, they must know that when the *Rebbe* travels with them, he is personally supervising every single movement of theirs, and examining their *avodah* in the fulfillment of the *shlichus*, and consequently, they must fulfill the *shlichus* with *hiddur*.

And likewise, there must be extra caution in their private conduct, because they are looked upon as "*Lubavitcher bochurim*," and when they conduct themselves as they should, this influences those who see them to want to send their children to *Lubavitch yeshivos*, and to marry their daughters to *Lubavitcher bochurim*, unlike if their conduct is not as it should be, *chas v'shalom*, in which case the responsibility rests upon them.

And also those who travel to their homes—who also must engage in their places in the matters of the *shlichus* of the *Rebbe*—must know that the *Rebbe* travels with them, for the inner intention of their traveling to their homes is not for their private matters, but for the fulfillment of the *shlichus* of the *Rebbe* in their places.

And similar to the words of the *Rebbe* who said once (to one of the *shadarim*) that one must not only take, but also give, "*farzeien ruchniyus*." And furthermore, it is possible that the main intention of the *Rebbe* is the giving, for regarding *the taking*, he could certainly have managed without it, and *kal v'chomer*: if he can give advice to a Jew for success in his matters, he could certainly give advice to himself, and it must be that his intention in this is *the giving*, but because of the opposing side, he had to conceal the inner intention in various matters.

**O.** Just as those who travel from here must know that the *Rebbe* is with them wherever they go, likewise those who come here, to the four walls of the *Rebbe* [even those who come only in their free time, or when the *baal habayis* thinks they can come...], must know that their main residence is here, within the four walls of the *Rebbe*, and that for the time being (even if this time lasts for a long time) they are traveling

#### 139

from here, similar to the story regarding the "*bar bei rav d'chad yoma*" (and it should be noted that the main residence according to Torah (as we find regarding *Sukkah*) is not in time, but in the soul).

It is stated in the *Gemara* that in the future, "the stones of a person's house and the beams of a person's house will testify against him, as it is said, 'For a stone shall cry out from the wall, and a beam from the wood shall answer it'." That is to say, even after thousands of years have passed (from the time this verse was said until the coming of the great and awesome day of the *Ribono shel Olam*), the beams of the house—which does not exist for a long time—will testify about what happened inside it. And all the more so regarding the four walls and the beams of the *Rebbe's* house, in which he prayed and studied and engaged in his matters and received people for "*yechidus*" while uniting with the *yechidah* aspect of their souls, then certainly the beams of this house—in which we are now—"have absorbed" all the matters connected with the essence of the *Rebbe*!

The difference is only that there are those whose physical four cubits are also here, and there are those whose physical four cubits are in another place, and they must take these four cubits with them, and as mentioned, the *Rebbe* travels with each one of those who travel on his *shlichus*, and certainly because of this he will influence them with everything necessary—for the *Rebbe* does not remain a debtor, and in the language of our Sages, "the *Ribono shel Olam* does not withhold the reward of any creature"—for abundant success in physical and spiritual matters.

(At the conclusion of the *farbrengen*, the *Rebbe* said:)

"*A gutten Yom Tov*" until the next *Chassidic farbrengen*, and certainly "if the *Rebbe* should be healthy—as one of the *Chassidim* wrote to me—he will lead us toward *Moshiach*," speedily in our days, *amen*.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5710*

#### 140

**A.** Regarding the month of Av—for on this Shabbos we bless the month of Av—it is stated in a maamar of the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*[1](#_ftn656) that, seemingly, it is difficult to understand why the *Churban* (destruction) occurred in the month of *Av*, the essence of which is *rachamim* (mercy).

*Av* denotes mercy, as it is written,[2](#_ftn657) "As a father (*av*) has mercy." Furthermore, the order of the letters in the word *Av*—*Aleph, Beis*—from top to bottom, denotes mercy. As it is stated in the *Zohar*,[3](#_ftn658) the order of letters from bottom to top represents *dinim* (judgments) and *gevuros* (severities), while from top to bottom it represents *rachamim*. This is why in the month of Tishrei, where the order is bottom-to-top—*Tav, Shin, Reish*—the world is judged,[4](#_ftn659) whereas the month of Av, with its order of top-to-bottom—*Aleph, Beis*—is *rachamim*.

How, then, is it possible that the month in which so many matters of *pur'anus* (calamity) occurred—the destruction of the First and Second Temples, the sin of the spies (which was the root cause of the *Churban*), and all five things enumerated in Maseches Taanis[5](#_ftn660)—is called *Av*, which specifically denotes *rachamim*?

The maamar explains that this is similar to the concept of "Hear, my son, the instruction of your father,"[6](#_ftn661) and "He who loves him seeks out instruction (*mussar*),"[7](#_ftn662) where, on the exterior, it is a matter of *din* and *gevurah*, but in its interior, it is a matter of *rachamim*.

**B.** One may explain this matter as follows:

The truth is that all matters are *rachamim*, for from Him, may He be blessed, no evil emanates,[8](#_ftn663) and certainly His conduct with His people Israel—who are His children and the flock of His pasture—is entirely in *chessed* (kindness) and *rachamim*. However, there is *rachamim* that is revealed, and there is *rachamim* that is greater, above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (order of evolution), which, due to its immense loftiness, cannot be revealed except through the garment of *din*.

The explanation for this is:

#### 141

The need for *greater* *rachamim* arises specifically when there is a state and situation of *din*. In such a case, it is impossible for the *rachamim* to be revealed as they are, because of the opposition of the *middas hadin* (attribute of judgment). Therefore, the *rachamim* must be concealed within the garment of *din*.

When *rachamim* are concealed within the garment of *din*—thereby appeasing the *middas hadin* so that it has no opposition—there is an additional advantage: it becomes possible to draw down *rachamim* that are infinitely greater, up to *Ein Sof*.[9](#_ftn664)

Therefore, this month is called *Av*, which denotes *rachamim*, because the matters of *pur'anus* are the garment of *din* within which the greatest *rachamim* are concealed.

**C.** This is further emphasized on Shabbos Mevarchim HaChodesh—when we bless the month of *Menachem* Av:

The name of the month regarding legal documents according to Torah, such as in the writing of a *get* (divorce document), is "Av" (without the word *Menachem*). However, in the *Birchas HaChodesh* (blessing of the month), the custom of Israel (which is Torah) is to call the name of the month "*Menachem* Av."[10](#_ftn665)

The reason for this may be explained as follows:

The intent of *Birchas HaChodesh* is to draw down throughout the entire month (including the days before *Rosh Chodesh*, which are days of preparation for the month) the concept of "salvation and consolation." The general concept of "consolation" is specifically *after* the sorrow—that is, the *revelation of the interiority* of the sorrow that preceded it (as discussed above[11](#_ftn666)).

This concept is also emphasized in the name of the month—"*Menachem* Av"—which signifies (not the drawing down of greater *rachamim* as they are concealed within the garment of *din*, but) the drawing down of greater *rachamim* *in a revealed manner*, even below ten *tefachim*.

This is similar to the story[12](#_ftn667) that when the Rebbe Maharash asked his father, the Tzemach Tzedek, about the "end" (*ketz*) hinted at for the year 5608 (1848), and his father replied, "What do you want? The coming of Moshiach is the revelation of the interiority of the *neshamah*,"[13](#_ftn668)—and *Likutei Torah* had been printed, which is the revelation of the interiority of the Torah, through which the revelation of the interiority of the *neshamah* is achieved—the Rebbe Maharash said to him: "But we want the coming of Moshiach below ten *tefachim*!"

*

#### 142

**D.** Based on what was said above regarding the drawing down of greater *rachamim* specifically in the month of Av, we can explain the precision in the language of the Alter Rebbe in the *Tanya* lesson for this day[14](#_ftn669):

His language is: "Therefore, the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy cleanse all blemishes, as it is written,[15](#_ftn670) 'Forgiving iniquity, transgression, and sin, and cleansing.'"

One must understand the precision in the Alter Rebbe's language—that he quotes the words from the verse, "Forgiving iniquity, transgression, and cleansing," and *omits* the word "sin" (*chata'ah*) that appears in between?

The explanation for this is:

The revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy—*greater rachamim* that are above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—is intended to atone for *zedonos* (willful sins), which are from the three completely impure *kelipos*. This is not the case regarding *shegagos* (unintentional sins), for which atonement is achieved through *korbanos* (sacrifices), and there is no need for the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy.

As explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*[16](#_ftn671) regarding the greatness of the elevation of the passing of *tzaddikim*, as our Sages said,[17](#_ftn672) "Why is the section of Miriam juxtaposed to the section of the *Parah* (Red Heifer)? To tell you that just as the *Parah* atones, so too does the death of *tzaddikim* atone." At the passing of a *tzaddik*, there is a "revelation of the light of the *tikkun* and 'preserving kindness' (*notzer chessed*)," from the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, and this revelation "effects salvations *in the midst of the earth* [not in the heavens above, but 'in the midst of the earth,' 'in the very middle of the earth,' earthliness and materiality], to atone for the iniquity of the generation, and even for *zedonos* which are from the three completely impure *kelipos* that are below *nogah*," just like the Red Heifer, which "purifies the impurity of the dead even though it is the 'father of fathers' etc., and below *nogah*." This is not the case for "the *korbanos* on the altar, (which) are the aspect of elevating *mayin nukvin* from the *nefesh habahamit* that is in *nogah*... they do not atone except for *shegagos*, which are from the overcoming of the *nefesh habahamit* that is in *nogah*."

Therefore, when the Alter Rebbe explains that "the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy cleanse all blemishes," he quotes the words from the verse "Forgiving iniquity, transgression, and cleansing," and omits the word "sin"—because for atonement for *shegagos* ("sin"), there is no need for the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy.

The reason the word "sin" is also mentioned in the verse—one may say—is because of the end of the verse, "and will not cleanse" (*lo yenakeh*), according to the exposition of our Sages[18](#_ftn673) that "He cleanses those who repent, but does not cleanse *those who do not repent*," to teach us that even for "sin" (unintentional) "He does not cleanse

#### 143

those who do not repent," because even "the unintentional ones require atonement" (as Rashi writes[19](#_ftn674)), for even *shegagos* are "from the overcoming of the *nefesh habahamit*" (and had He not opened a path for them initially, they would not have come to this overcoming). This is not the case in *Tanya*, where the subject is the action of *teshuvah* ("He cleanses those who repent") through the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy to cleanse all blemishes; there is no place or need to add the word "sin," which was said in relation to the state and situation of "will not cleanse" at the end of the verse.[20](#_ftn675)

*

**E.** The matter of *teshuvah* (through which the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, the greater *rachamim*, is effected) is also mentioned in the *parsha* of the week:

In the *parsha* of the week, the census of *Bnei Yisrael* is discussed—close to the end of the forty years before entering the Land—by Moshe and Elazar the Priest. In the census of the tribe of Reuven, Datan and Aviram are also mentioned,[21](#_ftn676) and the text continues, "They are Datan and Aviram, the chosen of the congregation, who contended against Moshe etc., when they contended against Hashem, and the earth opened its mouth and swallowed them and Korach etc."[22](#_ftn677) And afterwards it adds, "But the sons of Korach did not die,"[23](#_ftn678) because "at the time of the dispute *they contemplated teshuvah in their hearts*, therefore a high place was fortified for them in *Gehinnom* and they sat there."[24](#_ftn679)

This highlights the greatness of the merit of *teshuvah*—that even after "the earth opened its mouth and swallowed them," *teshuvah* was effective so that "a high place was fortified for them etc.," and as it is written,[25](#_ftn680) "He brings down to the grave (*sheol*) (and nevertheless) and brings up."

**F.** One should add and explain something puzzling in the account of the census of *Bnei Yisrael* in the *parsha* of the week:

Since the purpose of the census is to know the number of *Bnei Yisrael* *who are currently present*, why were families mentioned who were no longer in the world? In the tribe of Reuven—*Datan and Aviram*, even though it is explicit in the continuation of the text that "the earth opened its mouth and swallowed them," and in the tribe of Yehudah—*Er and Onan*[26](#_ftn681), even though it is explicit in the continuation of the text that "Er and Onan died in the land of Canaan"?!

#### 144

And one cannot say that the text needed to mention them to clarify that no trace of them remained so that a question would not arise as to why these families were not mentioned, because if so, the text should have also mentioned the "five families (that) were missing from the sons of Binyamin."[27](#_ftn682) From this it is proven that there is no need to clarify regarding the missing families. If so, why did the text mention Datan and Aviram and Er and Onan specifically?

**G.** This will be understood by first explaining the connection of the census of *Bnei Yisrael* before entering the Land to the *parsha* of *Pinchas*—"*Pinchas*" is written with a *vav* (full) [for regarding the two opinions as to whether it is written deficient in every place and only once full, or whether it is written full in every place and only once deficient[28](#_ftn683), in the *parsha* of *Pinchas* it is full], with the addition of a *yud*:

It is stated in the *Zohar*[29](#_ftn684) that "a *yud* was added to Pinchas because he was zealous for this," just as in Yosef, to whom a *hei* was added, "A testimony in Yehosef,"[30](#_ftn685) "because he guarded himself from this, he became attached to the *Shechinah* and held onto that testimony." That is, because of their merit in the matter of guarding the covenant, upon which the connection of Hashem and *Knesses Yisrael* depends, the letters *yud* (in P*i*nchas) and *hei* (in Ye*h*osef) were added to them.

This is the connection of Pinchas (with a *yud*) to the census of *Bnei Yisrael*—that in the census of *Bnei Yisrael* as well, the matter of guarding the covenant is emphasized, as explained in Rashi's commentary in our *parsha*[31](#_ftn686) that "Hashem placed His name upon them, a *hei* on this side and a *yud* on that side, to say, 'I testify about them that they are the children of their fathers (that the Egyptians did not have power over their mothers)...' the tribes of *Y-H*."

The reason the testimony regarding guarding the covenant is specifically in the two letters *Y-H* can be explained simply, according to our Sages[32](#_ftn687), "A man and a woman, if they are meritorious, the *Shechinah* is between them," "for He divided His name and caused it to dwell between them, the *yud* in *ish* (man) and the *hei* in *ishah* (woman)." Therefore, the two letters *Y-H* constitute testimony that all are pure and all are holy.

**H.** Based on this, one can explain the reason that in the census of *Bnei Yisrael* in the *parsha* of *Pinchas*, before entering the Land, it is mentioned, "Er and Onan died in the land of Canaan":

It is known[33](#_ftn688) that the sin of Er and Onan (the lack of guarding the covenant) hinders the *Geulah* (redemption), the entry into the Land in absolute perfection.

#### 145

It is explained in the *Chassidus* discourses on *Parshas Vayechi* (from the discourses of the Alter Rebbe in *Torah Or*[34](#_ftn689) to the discourses of the Rebbe Rayatz[35](#_ftn690)) that in addition to the matters of the *avodah* of Reuven, Shimon, and Levi, there must also be the *avodah* of Yehudah, "This time I will thank Hashem," the perfection of *avodah*, which is why "she ceased from bearing."[36](#_ftn691) And nevertheless, even in the seed of Yehudah there can be a hindrance, etc., through the sin of Er and Onan, because the connection of Hashem and *Knesses Yisrael* depends on this matter.

Therefore, when discussing the census of *Bnei Yisrael* before entering the Land, the text repeats and emphasizes the negation of the matter that could, Heaven forbid, hinder the entry into the Land.

**I.** And there is still room for the question: Since there is Moshe Rabbeinu, who has the power to rectify and does rectify all matters—how is it possible that this hindrance remains, "How could he allow this matter?!"

The answer to this—as mentioned earlier—is "They are Datan and Aviram, the chosen of the congregation, who contended against Moshe":

Datan and Aviram were indeed "the chosen of the congregation," and they were joined by the "two hundred and fifty princes of the congregation" who were heads of the Sanhedrin,[37](#_ftn692) and also Korach, who "was clever" (and even though "his eye misled him," nevertheless, he had something to hang his hat on),[38](#_ftn693) but nevertheless, because "they contended against Moshe," this is "contending against Hashem," as it is written,[39](#_ftn694) "And they believed in Hashem and in Moshe His servant," meaning, that faith in Hashem and in Moshe His servant are connected to each other, and consequently, the lack of faith in Moshe is connected with the lack of faith in Hashem,[40](#_ftn695) and as a result, the entry into the Land was hindered for them.

And nevertheless, even in such a state and situation, *teshuvah* is effective—as the text continues and concludes: "But the sons of Korach did not die," as mentioned above.

Therefore, Datan and Aviram were also mentioned in the census of *Bnei Yisrael* before entering the Land—to emphasize the negation of the matter of "contending against Moshe," which could, Heaven forbid, hinder the entry into the Land.

*

**J.** From the matters of the census of *Bnei Yisrael*—through which the strength of "a matter that is counted is not nullified" is created in them.[41](#_ftn696)

#### 146

Therefore, even though *Bnei Yisrael* as a whole are "the fewest of all the peoples,"[42](#_ftn697) and especially those who observe Torah and *mitzvos*, who are "few" among *Bnei Yisrael* as a whole—which is why there are those who argue, "From where do you take the strength to stand firmly on the path of Torah and *mitzvos* without being impressed by the whole world?"—not only do they stand their ground firmly, but furthermore, they also influence others, as the Rebbe demanded long ago, in the *sicha* of 13 Tammuz,[43](#_ftn698) that one must not only live oneself, but also bring others to life ("Not only that one lives oneself, but one also brings others to life").

The strength in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* must be not only while one is in the *yeshivah* or the *beis medrash*, but one must go out to the street and approach a Jew who does not know if he wears a *tallis katan*, and does not even know if he wears a *tallis gadol* during prayer, and even regarding putting on *tefillin* he does not know his state and situation, and say to him: "Listen, Jew, I am not asking you for money, I am not asking you for anything, I only want you to put on *tefillin* (at least to put them on) every day! Do me a favor, do yourself a favor, do a favor for your parents and grandparents and great-grandparents up to Yaakov Avinu, and do a favor for your descendants after you until the end of all generations until the coming of Moshiach!"

Someone might argue that it is not polite to approach a person whom he does not know, does not know what is going on with him, and is not even sure of the fact that he is a Jew since it is not recognizable on his face... The answer to this is that *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) overrides everything, and even for a doubt one clears away the debris,[44](#_ftn699) and similarly regarding *pikuach nefesh* in spirituality, that even for a doubt (including the doubt if he is a Jew) one must strive and do everything to bring him to life.

Similar to the story in the *Gemara*[45](#_ftn700) that "Rav Ada bar Ahava saw a certain non-Jewish woman who was wearing a red cloak in the street; he thought she was a daughter of Israel, he stood up and tore it from her. It turned out that she was a non-Jew, and they fined him four hundred *zuzim*"—that because of a *doubt* of saving a soul from Israel from a forbidden matter *for a few moments*, he did not spare his money to wait to clarify first if she was a daughter of Israel!

And to add, that the effort for the benefit of others in matters between man and Hashem also relates to his conduct in matters between man and his fellow—not like those who argue that while regarding matters between man and his fellow, matters that relate to the benefit of the settlement of

#### 147

the country, there is a need to intervene in the affairs of others, whereas in matters between man and Hashem, and especially *mitzvos* that are "statutes" (*chukim*), the conduct of others does not concern me, for I am not a "policeman" of Hashem...—as we find in the *Gemara*[46](#_ftn701) regarding covering the head as a remedy for "fear of Heaven," that "one day... his cloak fell from his head, he lifted his eyes, saw a palm tree, his inclination overcame him," and he stumbled into the prohibition of robbery (not just theft in secret, but robbery in public). From this it is understood that the effort for the benefit of others in matters between man and Hashem, such as covering the head and putting on *tefillin*, also relates to matters between man and his fellow, up to the negation of theft and robbery.

**K.** However, at the same time as engaging in the benefit of others, one must also remember about one's own *avodah*. And in the words of the text[47](#_ftn702)—after the introduction of "When you see the naked and you cover him"—"and do not hide yourself from your own flesh."
